et avoit jai bien pres close toute la gorge, si que li femme ne pooit expirer por le conduit qui estoit estoupez, et ne pooit ne mengier ne boivre, et fust morte s’elle demorast ensi I jor ou II.	and had closed almost the entire throat, so that the woman could not breathe through the blocked channel, and could not drink or urinate, and died if she delayed for one or two days.
Et li apostemes estoit jai si montez qu’il avoit fuer mis II rains par les II pertuis dou neis.	And the wound was so high that it had been set with two incisions through the two holes.
Je hastai donques tantost, et fichai en l’un I oncine, puis lou traï fuers, et en traï grant porcion de bowe;	I then operated, and found in the one the bone, then removed it, and took out a large portion of the bowel.
puis refis autreteil en l’autre pertus dou neis, et li ovrai la bouche et li pressai la lengue;	then removed another part from the other side, and opened the mouth and pressed on the tongue.
aprés fichai l’oncine en ces apostemes, et en copai une partie, et n’en issit fuers que un poc de sanc;	After cutting the gallbladder according to these instructions, and removing a part of it, and there will only be a small amount of blood.
et ensi fut destoupez li conduis de la gorge la femme, et comensa maintenant a boivre aigue et puis vin, et ne cessai de taillier de cel aposteme par lonc tens;	And the woman's throat is torn out, and she begins to drink water and then wine, and does not stop cutting at that wound for a long time.
et li apostemes recroissoit adés, et remplissoit lou leu que je avoie vuidiet, tant qu’il refut mout gros;	And the wound healed over, and filled the empty joint that I had emptied for dinner, until it refused to take in anything large.
adonques je l’engignai et lou cauterizai dedens la gorge:	Therefore, I engaged and cauterized the throat:
ensi demora sens croistre;	It did not take long to heal.
et me partis de ces parties, et ne soi que Deus fist de li aprés moi.	I will begin from these parts, and I will only make God do as I have done after me.
de l’uve	Of the urethra
Quant reume dessent a l’uve, et elle est enflee et elle est longe, si est apelee «perpendiculaire»;	When the woman comes down to the uterus, it is long and thin, and is called "perpendicular".
et s’elle est desoz grosse et reonde, si est apelee «uve».	And if it is too large and round, it is called "uterus".
Quant elle est curee si com nos avons dit en la division, et li cure ne profite mie, et tu vois que li chaus apostemes est apaisiez, et elle est subtilz, si covient que tu la copes;	When it is treated as we have said in the division, and the treatment does not benefit, you see that the abscess is calmed, and it is subleased, then you can copy it.
et celle qui est reonde assemblee et n’est mie longe;	And that which is round and assembled is not long.
et elle est sanguine ou de fusse color ou noire, si covient que tu eschues l’incision de li.	And it is blood or blackish-colored or black, then you can evacuate the incision.
Car il i a grant peril sus lou malaide.	For there is great danger to the patient.
Il covient donques, quant tu la vois, selonc la maniere que j’ai dit, de sa blenchor et de sa longesce, que tu faices seoir le malaide devant lou soleil, et li presse la lengue a l’estrument dont nos avons fait la remembrance ci devant;	It is therefore, as you see, according to the manner I have said, of the woman's girdle and her age, that you should make the midwife stand before the sun, and press the tongue on the instrument we have made in front of it.
puis fiche l’oncine en l’uve, et la trai desoz, et la cope a I des II estrumens que j’ai dit en l’incision des II amandres.	Then clean the wound in the uterus, and cut the tissue, and the copper we have said in the incision of the two breasts.
Et covient que tu ne coper mie fuer que la superfluiteit qui est outre le termine natureil;	And it is necessary that you do not cover more than the natural termination.
car se tu en copes plus, si grieves a la voix, et a la parolle;	For if you cover more, you will grieve to the voice and to the speech.
et aprés l’incision, use de ceu que nos avons dit en l’incision des II amandres, et le cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	And after the incision, use what we have said in the incision of two thumbs, and treat it as soon as it is healthy.
Et se li malaides a paor dou coper, si covient que tu i use d’engien a la cauterization de li sens paor.	And if the patient has fear of pain, then you must use an engine for the fire cautery of the painful part.
Et li maniere dou cautere si est aigue ague.	And the manner of cautery is sharp and quick.
Et est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, et puis li presse la lengue a l’estrument que nos avons dit ou chapistre de cautere, et confis avec aigue vive chaus, si qu’elle ne soit mie trop espesse ne trop clere;	And the patient should place his head on the device we have mentioned in the chapter of cauterization, and then press the tongue with the instrument, and confuse it with hot vinegar if it is not too thick or too clear.
et en emple le chevement de cest estrument, de coi ci est li forme:	and in using this instrument, of course, its form is:
Et ait ou chief une cheveure ou om met la medecine, si com li chevemens d’une cuillier, et met l’estrument a tout la medicine sus l’uve;	And if the head has a hair or puts medicine, as the hair of a pin, and places the instrument at all the medicine under the eye.
et li malaides soit gisans sus son costeit, si que li salive et li muscillaige corre de sa bouche de la medicine dedens, si qu’ele ne dessende a la gorge, et lou blece;	When the patient has a dislocated shoulder, if the saliva and spittle flow from the mouth due to the medicine given, if it does not descend to the throat and chin,
puis tien ta main a tout la medicine et la presse sus l’uve, la quantiteit de la moitiet d’une houre, tant que tu la vois nercie et li mordications de la medicine soit apaisie;	then hold your hand on all the medicine and press on the wound, as much as you see the flow and the sting of the medicine is relieved;
et se tu vues, pren coton et l’envoloupe sus aucun estrument, et moille lou coton en la medicine, et boute l’estrument a tout le couton en la cainne desus, tant que li coton s’aerde sus l’uve;	and if you see, take cotton and wrap it around any instrument, wet the cotton in the medicine, and tie the instrument with all the cotton in the gut, as much as the cotton sticks to the wound;
et fai ceu sovent, tant que li cauteres soit parfais, puis la laisse elle seche, et chiet aprés IIII jors ou V.	And do this as often as the cauterization is perfect, then let it dry, and check after four or five days.
Et se tu as mestier de rencomencier lou cautere de la medicine, si le rencomence, et aprés le cautere l’essue entor l’uve, de couton embut em burre, et mundifie ceu qui est entor de la medicine;	And if you are a practitioner of medical cauterization, if it reoccurs, and after the cauterization, cleanse the flesh around the urethra with a cork, and clean what is outside of the medical area.
et soit arosez d’aigue froide, et soit curez de gargarismes tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if it is inflamed with cold water, and be sure to use gargles as long as it is healthy.
Ceste cure est plus save de l’incision, ne que li cautere;	This remedy is safer than the incision alone, just the cauterization.
s’elle est curee de fumigation selonc ceste maniere, pren calament et ysope et origanum et rue et camomille et avronne et semblans herbes, et les assemble toutes ou aucunes d’eles en I pot, et i met aisil, et fai bullir;	If it is treated with fumigation according to this method, take a lump of salt, pepper, oregano, rue, chamomile, and thyme, and mix them all together or any of them in one pot, and put on fire, and boil;
et li potz soit bien gluez de fort terre, et enmi le pot ait I estrument cheveit selonc ceste maniere:	and it may be well stuck with strong earth, and if it does not hold, have an instrument made according to this manner:
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain, et soit li uns des chiés boutez en la bouche dou malaide tant que li vapor monte a l’uve par la caine, tant que li uve soit mortifie;	and it should be made of silver or gold, and one of the ends should be inserted in the patient's mouth as much as possible until the vapor rises through the nose, until the nose is numb.
aprés lou rencomence sovent, tant que li uve seche, et garde que tu ne faices ceu au comencement de l’avenement de l’aposteme chaut, car plusors choses i avienent;	after the vapor restarts often, until the nose is dry and make sure you do not do this at the beginning of the onset of the abscess, as more things can come.
et ne faire mie ceu fuer que a la declination d’aposteme chaut.	and only do this when the onset of the abscess has declined.
Et se cist estrument n’est presens, si pren une caine et met dedens lou chief une craiffe d’uef, si que li bouche au malaide n’ait mie trop chaut;	And if this instrument is not present, then take a needle and insert the head of the screw into a crack in the bone, if the mouth of the patient does not have too much pain.
car li craiffe d’uef ne lait mie la vapor grever la bouche, et c’est bone cure ensamble salut.	For the screw crack does not cause pain in the mouth, and it is a good cure together.
Maintes fois s’aert a la gorge os ou espinee de poisson, ou aucune chose;	Many times it has happened in the throat, either an arrow or a fish spine, or nothing.
si covient donc que tu traies ceu que tu pues veoir, et li presse la lengue au soleil a tout l’estrument, si que tu voies mues la chose;	Therefore, if you must try this, and press the tongue against the sun with all the instruments, so that you see the thing.
et ceu que ne t’apert mie et est reponus en la gorge, covient que tu faices vomir le malaide ainsois que li viande soit cuite en l’estomac;	And if it does not open you, then you must make the patient vomit, unless the meat is cooked in the stomach.
par aventure si istra li chose aerse par le vomissement;	If by chance the thing is done through vomiting;
ou li malaides englutisse une piece d’esponge, ou une piece de navel, ou une racine de laitue, ou I morceil de pain sec;	or if the patient swallows a piece of sponge, or a piece of navel, or a root of millet, or a morsel of dry bread;
et lie a l’esponge I fil, et puis la transglutisse;	and then it binds to the sponge and then glues together;
et quant elle venra au leu, si s’aerdra, et puis trairas fuer;	and when it comes to the shoulder, if it is loose, and then tighten and hold fast;
et s’elle ne vient fuer de ceu que nos avons dit, si pren I estrument de plonc selonc ceste forme:	and if it does not come loose from what we have said, then use the instrument of thrust according to this form:
Et soit li estrumens corbés au chief si qu’il puist plus legierement entrer en la gorge, et ait le chief en haut leveit;	And let the instrument be hinged at the head if it can enter more lightly into the mouth, and have the head raised above.
et warde que tu ne touchier l’epiglote, que li tous ne li viegne, ne ne bouter mie l’os dedens;	And be warned that if you do not touch the epigastrium, all will not survive, and neither should you overcrowd the bones.
et mues vaut que li malaides i boute l’estrument, por ceu qu’il seit mues ou li chose est aerse;	And it is better that the patient and the tool be used, because it is needed or the thing is urgent.
si la boute aval, ou il la traie fuer a tout l’estrument igalment, tant qu’elle soit fuer.	If the thing is not cut, or it is not pulled out evenly throughout the entire tool, as far as it goes.
de la sansue de la gorge	of the throat of the mouth
Aucune fois est medicinee li sansue, si com j’ai dit en la division, par la cure de medicines;	Never has medicine been without its remedies, as I have said in the division, by the treatment of medicines.
et quant ceu ne profite mie, adonques regarde en la gorge dou malaide au soleil, puis que tu li presses la lengue a l’estrument que je t’ai dit.	And if this does not help, then look in the patient's mouth at the sun, then press the patient's tongue to the instrument I have given you.
Et se tu vois la sansue, si la trai a tout I petit uncine, ou as tenailles subtilz que valent a ceu.	If you see the lance, if it has all its small hairs, or if it has subtle needles that are worth this.
Et se ceu ne vaut, si pren une caine chevee, et la boute en la gorge dou malaide, puis boute ou chevement de la caine I fer chaut, et fai ce sovent.	If it is not worth anything, then take a hair from the head, and put it in the mouth of the patient, then pull or cut the hair with the forceps, and do this often.
Et se teigne li malaides d’aigue toute jor.	And the patient's scalp is scabbed all over every day.
puis pren plein I voirre d’aigue froide, et oevre la bouche, et la giete ens sens englutir, et la mueve a sa main sovent;	Then fill me with cold liquid, and operate on the mouth, and the throat feels like it's being swallowed, and it moves to my hand often.
et si tost com li sansue sent l’aigue, si chiet.	and if the tongue feels the cold liquid, then it is done.
Et s’elle ne chiet si com nos avons dit, si subfumige lou malaide d’asefetide, a l’estrument que j’ai dit en la fumigation de l’uve;	And if it does not move as we have said, then the surgeon should submerge the mouth in asafetida powder using the instrument I mentioned during the fumigation of the urethra.
fai ceu maintes fois, car elle cherra sens targier.	Do this many times, for it will feel numb.
Et li maniere de la fumigation si est que tu preignes I pot ou il ait charbons vis, et soit li pos covert d’un coverseil perciet en mileu, et en celui pertus soit li chiés de l’estrument;	And the manner of the fumigation is if you preign it or if there are charcoal bits, and it should be covered with a covering sheet in a clean place, and in that pertus the head of the instrument.
puis i giete ta fumigation, et li malaides mette lou chief de la cainne en sa bouche, et cloie la bouche, si que li fumee n’en isse mie, mais viegne jusc’a la sansue;	Then pour the fumigation on it, and the patient places the tip of the tail in his mouth, and closes his mouth so that the smoke does not escape, but goes into the wound.
et la sansue cherra maintenant, et s’elle ne chiet, si rencomence la fumigation par maintes fois;	And the wound will now hurt, and if it does not stop, then repeat the fumigation many times.
et soffre li malaides soif, et menjuce choses salees et als, et ne boive point d’aigue;	And the patient suffers from thirst, and drinks salty and acidic things, and does not drink water.
et adonques li iert mestier qu’elle isse fuer par cest governement.	And therefore, this is the best way to relieve the patient according to this government.
Et li forme de l’estrument a coi on trait la sansue, si est, quant on la puet veoir, semblans a tenailles corbés por mues entrer en la gorge;	And the shape of the instrument with which you treat the wound, if it can be seen, resembles combs that can enter the mouth.
et ait semblance au bec de soigne, et i ait asperiteit de lime, si que ceu qu’elle prent, elle ne puet lassier;	And it seems like a tool for the beak of care, and it has sharpness like lime, so that whatever it touches, it cannot hold.
et vez ci la forme:	And then its form is like this:
li chapistres des apostemes	2. The cauteries for the abscesses:
Mout de semblances d’aposteme sont, selonc ceu que li remembrance vient ci aprés d’un et d’autre en cest livre, et sont diver en perforation et en taille;	The appearances of abscesses are, according to which memory comes after one another in this book, and they are different in perforation and size.
et c’est en II manieres dont l’une est en sa semblance meisme, et de ceu qu’il tient moistor.	And it is in two ways that one is itself in its appearance, and because it is moist.
Et li seconde maniere si est por les leus ou il sont au cors.	And the second way is by the hands or when they are at the core.
car li apostemes dou chief est autres que cil dou fondement, et li apostemes dou leu charnut est autres que cil qui vient en jointures, et chescuns ait son jugement en l’uevre.	For the wounds of the head are different from those of the foundation, and the wounds on the face are different from those that come in joints, and each person will have their own judgment in the work.
Et si a apostemes c’on ne doit mie percier, tant que li bowe est meure selonc son acomplissement;	And if an abscess does not have to be measured, as long as the bowel is dead according to its completion.
et si a de telz qu’il covient percier quant il sont crut, et ne meurent mie selonc lor acomplissement, si com aposteme qui sont delez jointures.	If it is of such a kind that one must perceive when they are about to be born, and they do not die until their completion, as if amputations of joints.
Car quant apostemes vient delez jointures, et on le laisse tant qu’il est porris entor, par aventure si sont corrumput li liien et li nerf de la jointure, par coi ce est cause de contraction en celui membre.	For when wounds come from joints, and they are left as they are until they are fully healed, by chance if the ligament and nerve of the joint are corrupted, because this is due to contraction in that member.
Ou li aposteme est delez lou membre principel, et se tu tardes la perforation tant qu’il soit meurez, si nuira au membre principeil;	If the amputation is of the principal member, and if you delay the piercing until it is dead, it will harm the principal member.
ou il est delez lou fondement, si le perce on ainsois qu’il soit meurs;	If it is of the foundation, then if one does not pierce when it is dead, it will harm the foundation.
et ne covient mie que tu perces aposteme crut sens digestion acomplie, fuers que celui qui est delez lou fondement, qu’il ne porrisse em parfont, et soit alongiez dedens, et i viegne fistule;	And it is only necessary to pierce the amputation when it is thought to be complete with digestion, as if the foundation, which would not harm the principal member, would not be cut off, and would be long-lasting, and a fistula would be formed.
et ne puisse saner en grant termine.	and cannot be cured in a long time.
Et covient que tu saiches l’oure de la perforation de l’aposteme qui est meur selonc l’acomplissement, et c’est quant li dolor est apaisie, et li departemens de la fievre, et l’amenuisement de la dolor et de la roujor, et dou debatement et de l’aguisement dou chief de l’aposteme, et les autres signes;	And it is necessary that you suture the wound of the abscess that is inflamed according to its completion, and when the pain is relieved, and the fever subsides, and the lessening of the pain and the healing of the wound, and the debilitated condition and ague of the abscess, and the other signs.
et covient que tu faices seoir la perforation ou plus dependant leu de l’aposteme, et la ou il apert mues;	and it is necessary that you check the wound or more dependent on the abscess, and where it opens.
et soit li perforation dou lonc dou cors, et se li apostemes est as mains ou as piez, ou en jointures et au ners et as arteres, et en toz leus igalz ou il n’a point de ploieure.	and if the wound is long and deep, and if the abscess is in the hands or feet, or in the joints and arteries, and in some places there is no plastering.
En ces que ploient, par selonc celui membre.	In those cases, according to the member, they.
Et quant apostemes est en leu charnut, si vaut mues que tu laisses la perforation tant qu’il soit confermez en digestion acomplie, si com nos avons dit.	And when an abscess is in the flesh, if it is large, you should leave the puncture as long as it is confirmed in digestion completed, as we have said.
Car se tu lou perces devant ceu, si iert alongiez li cors dou venim de lui, et est plains de mout d’ordure;	For if you do not heed this, then the heart will be far from you, and it will be bitter to despise excrement.
et par aventure endurcissent les levres et li parfondetez de lui.	and by chance they harden their lips and make them more beautiful for him.
Et si a aucun aposteme que sont perciet selonc le large dou cors, selonc ceu que li membres en ait mestier.	And if there is no abscess that is punctured according to the large corse, according to the member, which the members can bear.
Et covient que tu amenistres em petis apostemes, petis pertus;	And it is necessary that you use small incisions, small punctures.
et en grans apostemes, grans pertus, et maintes fendures selonc la semblance de la grandor de l’aposteme;	and in large incisions, large punctures, and numerous furrows according to the appearance of the size of the incision.
et si a de tels apostemes ou il covient chever lou keur, et coper;	and if there are such incisions or they must be made deep, and covered.
quant il est jai devenus ausi com I drapelz, et est amortis, si covient faire ausi com on fait as bubes:	When it has become as soft as I am, and is worn out, then it is necessary to do as we do with bubbles.
et si a de telz que sont fendut en III angles, et si a de telz dont on cope ausi com la fuelle de mirte, si com apostemes des angres;	If it is of those that are cut at three angles, and if it is of those that are coped as the thorn of the myrtle, and like the gouts of angers.
et si a de telz ou on fait une reonde taille, et autres tailles et semblant copeure.	And if it is of those that are made in a single cut, and others in different sizes and shapes.
Cil qui n’ont point de chief, si com aposteme souef superficial, il covient que tu lou perces plainnement;	Those who do not have a head, if the cut is superficial like an abrasion, then it must be pierced gently.
et covient quant li apostemes est gros, et il a coillit grant bowe, et tu lou perces, si ne traire mie toute la bowe en celle houre, mais en trai une partie;	And when the cut is large and has a thick bow, and it pierces, if you do not draw all the bow in that hour, but draw a part.
puis estoupe l’aposteme jusc’a l’autre jor, puis en trai aucune chose derechief;	Then comes the aposteme, just like the other day, and no proper thing is done.
fai ceu par maintes fois de greit en greit, tant que li bowe isse toute;	I do this again and again, as long as the bowel is full.
meismement se li malaides est de foible vertut, ou femme portans, ou petis enfes, ou viez hons decrepites.	However, if the man is of weak will, or a woman carries, or eats pets, or old men are in decay.
Car li esperis tressaut aucune fois avec l’issue de la bowe, que par aventure muert li malaides, et tu ne t’en persois.	For the expectoration there is no time with the end of the bowel, that by chance dies the patient, and you do not know it.
Eschuez donques cest chapistre par grant cautele, et quant tu as perciet ton aposteme, si essue la plaie, et regarde se li plaie de l’aposteme est petite;	Avoid this chapter with great caution, and when you have perceived the aposteme, if the wound bleeds, and look at whether the wound of the aposteme is small.
et se c’est une tailleure plainne, si amenistre tentes de lin ou de viez coton;	And if it is a flat one, then use linen or cotton threads.
et se c’est uns grans apostemes, et il i a mout de pertus, si covient que tu boutes en chescun une tente si qu’ele viegne l’une contre l’autre;	And if it is many abscesses, and he has a fever, then you should make tents in each one so that they do not meet against each other.
et se tu as copeit en l’aposteme une partie dou cuir, et tu l’as cheveit entor, si covient que tu l’emplisses de viel couton ou de rasure de dras de lin sens moistor, et le lie jusc’au tier jor;	And if you have treated an abscess with some leather, and it has healed, then you should fill it with fine cloth or the rough side of a linen cloth that is not moist, and the limb will be well.
puis l’oste, et le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then the bone, and the care of the ointment as long as it is healthy.
Et se decorremens de sanc avient a ton ovraige, si amenistre aigue froide et aisil, et moille I drapeil, et met sor le leu decorrant par maintes fois.	And if the evacuation of blood occurs in your work, if it is cold and wet, and you become dizzy, and then your arm hangs down, and you must hold it in place many times.
Et se li decorremens de sanc persevere, se i amenistre governement et cure, et les poudres que j’ai dit em mains leus en cest livre, et se c’est ou tens d’iver, et li leus ou li apostemes est est mout nervous, si couvient que tu mettes sus tentes et drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile chaut;	And if the patient persists in losing blood, and he has good governance and care, and the powders I mentioned in my hands are in this book, and if it is not feverish, and the abscess is painful, then you should make tents and drape them with wet cloths soaked in wine and olive oil.
et se c’est en esteit, et li leus est charnus, si covient que tu mes sus drapelz moilliez en aigue et en oile, ou en vin et en oile froit, jusc’au tier jor, si com nos avons dit;	When the head of the shoulder is dislocated due to moisture, and it is reset but cannot stay in place, repeatedly dislocating with slight movement as we have experienced, then you must first reset the dislocation. If this is the case, and the patient's skin is wet, either with water or olive oil, or wine and olive oil, as we have said before, then...
et puis deslie l’aposteme et l’essue et le cure, si com il covient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And then remove the stitch and the pus, if necessary, as soon as it is healthy.
Et ceu covient il conoistre universement en cures des apostemes:	And this is how to completely understand all treatments for sutures:
or vos ai dit coment on doit aler avant as cures des apostemes, et vez ci le chapistre.	Or have you been told what to do before the treatments for sutures, and then read this chapter.
des soros	of sore
Ou keur dou chief vienent petis apostemes, et sont manieres de nous que sont en toiles, ausi com li josier d’une geline, et mout en i a de semblances.	When the heads of many abscesses come and are like ours, as if it were a grape, and they have similar appearances.
Il en i a de gras et de telz ou il a moistor ausi com poulz;	It has thick and long hairs or hair, and it is moist as well as that of a pig.
et si a de telz qui sont dur et pierous au taillier, et n’i a point de doutance se li artere n’i fait contraire.	And if they are thick and rough at the haircut, and there is no doubt that it will not hurt, then it does not matter.
Et li ovraiges de la taille si est que tu esprueve a tout I estrument qui est apelez «entromissoire», de coi li forme vient ci aprés, quel chose il contient.	And the cutting of the size if it is that you spree with all the instruments called "entronomer", whether the form comes after, what it contains.
Car s’il contient moistor, si lou fent par desus dou lonc.	For if it contains moisture, they are made by cutting too long.
Et quant li moistor est vuidie, si escorche sens rien laissier la peil qui contient celle moistor, car il revient adés quant on i laisse rien;	And when the moisture is seen, it is better to shave the hair that contains the moisture, because it will return to its place when left alone.
puis plonge coton en oignement egiptien, s’il est presens;	Then dip cotton in Egyptian ointment, if it is present.
se ceu non, en aigue et en seil, et en emple la plaie, et la laisse jusc’a l’autre jor;	If not, use warm and wet, and apply the wound, and leave it until the next day.
et ceu corront ceu qui est demorez dou nit.	And when one comes across something that is not well known.
Et pues rencomence lou coton, si com devant, le second jor, et lou tier, tant que tu saiches bien qu’il ne demoure point dou nit;	And then the cotton begins again, as before, the second day, and the limb, as long as you see that it does not cause pain all night.
puis cure la plaie d’oignement a ceu convenauble, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then, treat the wound with ointment according to what is convenient, as long as it is healthy.
Et se li apostemes tient I nout gras, si le cope selonc ceste forme, dou lonc;	And if the abscess holds fat, then the graft according to this form, long.
et i giete tes oncines, et l’escorche de toutes pars, et met toute ta cure de traire fuer la cotte ou il gist;	And if your bones get wet, and scar all over, and put all of your care in drawing the dressing for the wound where it grows.
et se li artere te fait contraire, si fai ceu que je t’ai dit aprés.	If the artery is pushed against it, then I will do what I have said after this.
Et ausi fai de l’aposteme s’il est pierous, et dou taillier et dou curer si com je t’ai dit.	2. And if the aposteme is too tight, and it is cut and treated as I have said.
Et li taille sus l’aposteme pierous et le moiste, si est plus legiere, car il sont de poc de sanc.	3. And the tailor makes the aposteme too tight and wet, if it is lighter, because there are not many veins.
Et si a aucuns de ces apostemes ou chief ou il n’a point de moistor, et de ces fut I apostemes que je copai ou chief d’une vielle femme;	And if in any of these abscesses or gashes, and of these that I have cut from an old woman's thigh;
et trovai l’aposteme ausi com une piere xourde, aspre et blainche, et ne pooit brisier;	and found the abscess like a gash, sharp and sore, and could not be cut;
et s’on en eust ferut aucun, on li eust ausi bien fait plaie com d’une piere.	and if we had made no abscess, we would have made a wound as good as a gash;
En autres apostemes venans ou chief, fuer que ces qui vienent as chief des enfans et as racines des oreilles, li overture si soit toz jors au plus dependant leu, por mues issir la bowe;	In other abscesses coming, let these which come from the children and roots of the ears be opened as soon as possible, for it is the most dependent part of the body, to relieve the belly;
et les cure si com il covient.	and they cure as it is fitting.
des scrophules	Of scrofuly (a term used to refer to
Maintes fois avienent cist aposteme au col, et desoz les asseles, et ens angres, et aucune fois vienent autre part ou cors, et sont mout, et sont enjanrees l’une avec l’autre.	There are often times of abscess at the collarbone, and the screws come loose, and the wounds, and never any other part is hurt, and they heal, and one bone is joined to another.
Et chescune scrophule est proprement dedens sa cote, si com li nout et li aposteme dou chief, si com nos avons dit;	And every scrofula is properly located on its side, just as the wound and the abscess are on the cheek, as we have said.
et les semblances de ces scrophules sont maintes.	and the appearances of these scrofulas are many.
Il i a de teles que contienent moistor, et si a de malignes qui ne vuellent obeir a santeit.	The patient has to remove the items that contain moisture, and if they are not willing to follow the advice for health.
en celle donques que tu vois de bone disposition au tochier, et est semblans a la color dou cors, et muet de chescune part et n’est mie aerse as ners dou col ne a l’artere ne au conduit, et n’est mie parfonde;	in the one that you see in good arrangement at the temple, and is similar to the color of the cheek, and uniform in all parts and is not rough as nerves are, nor in the artery nor in the conductor, and is not rough.
si covient que tu la copes par desus, et l’escorche de chescune partie, et estent les II levres dou keur as oncines, se tu en as mestier, si com nos avons dit en apostemes dou chief;	if you decide to cut it with scissors, and burn in every part, and the lips are like claws, if you can handle it, as we have said about the cheek.
et la trai poc et poc, et soies seur que tu ne coper lou nerf ne la voine, et ne soit mie li spatumile agus ne trenchans, que li mains n’eschaipe, et ne voise trop avant, que tu ne coper mie ceu que tu ne dois.	And the tailor makes it small and small, and be sure not to cut the nerve or vein, and not to tear, that the hands do not slip, and do not see too far ahead, that you do not cut more than you should.
Et se tu copes la voinne ou l’artere, et ceu ne te laisse ovrer, si met en la plaie vitriole broiet, ou aucunes poudres que restainchent sanc, et estraint la plaie;	And if you cut the vein or artery, and it does not bleed, then put vitrol or some powders that stick to the wound, or any poultices that stop bleeding, and pull the wound;
et la laisse tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez, et soit amollie li plaie, et encomence a porrir.	and let it be as long as the swelling is relieved and the wound is softened, and perspire.
Et quant li sans est estainchiez, si revien a ton ovraige, tant que tu l’acomplisses;	When the dislocation is not reduced, if it returns to your care, as soon as you manage to reduce it.
puis quier a ton doit indice s’il i demoure nules petites scrophules, si les cope et les munde.	Then wonder if your patient suffers from a few small scrofula, such as the cope and the mund.
Et s’il a en la racine de la scrophule voinne grant, si ne covient mie que tu copes celle scrophule en sa racine, mais la lie d’un fil double fort, et la laisse cheoir par li, sens nuisement;	And if the patient has a root cause of the scrofula being large, then you must only remove that scrofula at its root, but tie it with a strong double thread and leave it to hang, without causing any harm.
puis emple la plaie de viel coton plongiet en oignement egiptien, puis la cure.	Then use the wound of fine cotton plunged in Egyptian ointment, then the cure.
Et se tu copes toute la scrophule, si covient que tu assembles les II levres de la plaie, et les cout maintenant, puis qu’il n’i a point demoreit de superfluiteit por la grandor de la scrophule.	If you cover the entire wound, it is necessary to assemble the two lips of the wound, and then sew now, before there is no excess due to the size of the wound.
si covient que tu entendes a coper la racine de li, et traire fuer, et la cout si com nos avons dit.	If you understand how to cover the root of it, and cut it off, and sew it as we have said.
Celles scrophules que tienent superfluiteit, perce lai ou il apert meure;	Those scrofula that hold superfluity, if they are pressed or cut open, will die.
et la perce ensi com celle devant dite, en dependant, puis i amenistre tentes avec oignement et semblans choses, si qu’elle corrompe ceu qui est demorez de la corruption;	And the point is like the one previously mentioned, depending on it, then try different treatments with care and similar things, so that it does not corrupt what is being saved from corruption.
et quant li plaie est bien mundee, si la cure d’oignement enjanrant char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when the wound is well-healed, if the cure with ointment causes scarring, as long as it is healthy.
de squinance	Of the scalp
Li ancien dirent et parlerent de la tailleure de la gorge;	The ancients said and spoke of the lengthening of the neck.
mais je ne vis onques en nostre terre qui la feist, et c’est li escripture de lor parole.	But I have never seen anyone do this in our world, and it is the scripture of their words.
A ces qui ont squinance, il covient que li fendure de la gorge qui est apelee «epiglote» soit eschuee;	To those who have squinting, it is necessary that the fenestra of the neck called "epiglotis" be avoided.
et c’on ne faice aide par ceu, por ceu que toutes les voines et li pormon dou malaide sont a ces qui ont aposteme chaut en la bouche, ou en la gorge ou en II amandres.	And none can help this one because all the veins and the flesh of the patient are affected by those who have abscesses in the mouth, or in the throat, or in the groin.
Quant li maladie est en la chenal dou pormon, il covient coper l’epiglote por fuir la perdition qui vient de l’estranglement.	When the disease is in the throat, it is necessary to cut the epiglottis to avoid death that comes from strangulation.
Il covient donques, quant nos volons fendre l’epiglote, que nos le fendons desoz III cercles ou IIII une petite fendure dou travers, entre les II cercles ou par la quantiteit de la fendure dou syfac, ne mie en la cartillaige;	It is therefore necessary, when we wish to cut the epigastrium, that we cut it with three or four small incisions, passing through the two circles or along the quantity of the incision, and not into the cartilage.
et cil leus si est covenaubles a la section de l’epiglote qu’il n’i a point de char, et li vasseil sont lonc d’enqui.	And they see that it is not possible to cut the epigastrium without causing pain, and the veins are long and difficult to find.
Et se li maistres est paourous, si covient qu’il estende le cuir de la gorge a tout l’oncine, puis fende lou keur tant qu’il viegne a la cheneil;	If the masters are unable to handle it, then it comes to extending the neck skin to all the bones, then cutting as far as it reaches the cheek.
et eschue les vasselz de sanc, se tu vois aucune chose, et puis cope lou syfac, si com nos avons dit;	And avoid the veins of blood, if you see nothing, and then cut the skin, as we have said.
et est demostrez par la section dou fleume de la cheneil ki saut fuer par le leu qui est rompus, et par la defaute de la voix;	And it is demonstrated by the section of the swollen cheek that it was forced to jump by the shoulder that was broken, and due to the lack of voice.
et laisse la plaie overte une piece.	And leave the wound overhanging a piece.
Et quant li houre est passee de coi on doute l’estranglement, assemble les II levres de la plaie dou keur, et la cout toute soule sens la cartillaige;	And when the hour has passed, if it is doubted that the extraction is not possible, gather the two lips of the wound as far as the cheek, and cut through until you feel the cartilage.
puis aministre medicines qui font naistre char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then administer medicines that make the patient healthy.
Albucasim dist c’on ne faice ce jusc’a tant que li gorge est toute estoupee, et li malaides est jugiez a mort, et li defaut li alaine.	Albucasim says that nothing should be done until the throat is completely swollen, and the patient is near death, and the lack of air is severe.
Adonques cope on l’epiglote por ceu que li malaides ne puet alener, et il respire par la plaie, et ensi est gardez de mort;	Then keep the epigastrium warm because the patient cannot breathe, and he breathes through the wound, and it is kept alive.
et por ce commanderent li anciain a laissier la plaie overte tant que li malice de la maladie soit passee, et elle est passee en III jors ou en IIII Et adonques il comanderent a coudre la plaie et curer, tant qu’elle fut curee;	And because the ancients advised leaving the wound overgrown until the disease had passed, and it had passed in three days or four, they then ordered to suture and dress the wound, as soon as it was dressed.
et je vos dirai ceu que je vis.	And I will tell you what I see.
Je vis que une damoisele prist I coutel, et le ficha en sa gorge, et copa partie des chenelz dou pormon;	I see that a maiden was cutting her hair, and she had parted the front of her hair, and took some of the dark curls.
et je fui apelez por li curer, et la trovai ausi com morte.	I was called to cure him, and I found him already dead.
Je descovris la plaie, et trovai le sanc qui en estoit issus, et soi bien qu’elle n’avoit mie copeit voine ne conduit fuer que la gorge, et li vens issoit fuer par la plaie.	I discovered the wound, and found the blood that flowed from it, and although she did not have any veins or lead the way but only the gore, it was due to the wound.
Je me hastai, et cousi la plaie, et la curai tant qu’elle fut sanee;	I hurried, and saw the wound, and cured it as soon as it was healed.
et n’avint a la damoisele fuer qu’elle fut roge de voix, et revint aprés a sa disposition;	and she did not come to the damsel until she was red of voice, and returned afterwards to her place.
por ceu di je que en la tailleure de l’epiglote n’ait mie paour.	because I say that in the tailoring of the epigastric there is no pain.
de la grosse gorge	Of the large maw
Cist apostemes est apelez «hernie de gorge», et est uns grans apostemes en color d’une jaisse, et est molt en femmes;	These hernias are called "throat hernia" and are large hernias of the color of a yarn, and are very common in women.
et est selonc II manieres:	and there are two ways to treat it:
naturez, et accidens;	1. The first sentence translates to: "When a bone is fractured due to an accident or injury.
ou natureil n’a point d’engien.	2. The second sentence translates to: "Nature has no mechanism for healing such injuries.
Et li accidens est selonc II manieres, de coi l’une est semblans a gras nous, et li autre maniere est semblans a aposteme qui vient de nous d’artere;	3. The third sentence translates to: "Injuries can occur in two ways: either they resemble large wounds, or they are similar to amputations that come from arteries.
et il i ait paour, et ne covient mie ovrer de feir fuers que en celi qui est petite, et le prueve et cerche a tout l’intromissoire:	4. The fourth sentence translates to: "If there is no bleeding, and it is not possible to stop it with a small forceps, the surgeon should look for an alternative method.
se tu le trueves ausi com I nout gras, et ne pent a nulle voine, si le cope, si com on cope les nous, et le trai a tout sa coife, s’il en i a point;	5. The fifth sentence translates to: "If the surgeon cannot stop the bleeding with a large forceps, and it does not stop, just like when we cut ourselves, the wound should be cleaned thoroughly, if necessary.
et encerche bien tot, et le cure si com il covient, tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	1. And he cuts well throughout, and the cure is done as it should be, as long as it is perfectly healthy.
des nous	The first sentence to translate is
Maintes manieres de nous sont, dont je dirai toutes les semblances;	1. There are many ways to us, which I will describe all the appearances.
et or covient que je die toute la difference qui est entre nout et issue.	1. and it is necessary that I make a clear distinction between wound and dislocation.
Je dis que issue est chalors et fievre tenans, tant que li ebulicions est passee, et est acomplie li porriture;	1. I say that dislocation is inflammation and fever holding, as long as the ebullitions have passed and the secretion has been accomplished.
adonques repose li fievre et li chalor.	1. And then the fever and inflammation rest.
Avec lou nout n’a ne chalor ne fievre ne dolor, et contient I syfac, qui est ses propres sac et est selonc la color dou cors, et encomence ausi com une jaisse, et devient gros;	1. With the wound having no inflammation, fever, or pain, and containing ichthyin, which is its own sac and is according to the color of the corset, and becomes like a pimple, and becomes large.
et sont selonc II semblances, ou grais, ou moiste, et mout de color sont si com j’ai dit en la division.	1. They are according to two appearances, either sharp or blunt, or moist, and of different colors, as I said in the division.
Il covient, quant tu viens a la cure dou nout, que tu esprueves et l’enquier premierement a tout l’estrument qui est apelez «entromissoire», selonc ce que sa forme venra ou chapistre qui est aprés.	It is necessary, when you come to the cure of a newborn, that you examine and first inquire about all the instruments called "entromissoire" according to what appears in the chapter after the work.
Et li maniere de l’inquisicion des apostemes des nous est que tu preignes ou plus moiste leu que tu trueves en l’aposteme, et torne tes dois poc et poc, tant que tu saiches que li estrumens ait perciet le keur, puis que ce soit selonc la grandor de l’aposteme;	2. The manner of incising the abscesses of the nose is that you prick it more with your finger than with a needle, and turn your two fingers often until you feel that the skin has given way, then that is according to the size of the abscess;
puis estrai l’entromissoire, et pren garde en ceu que saut fuer.	3. Then draw out the entromiser, and hold tight until it gives way;
Se moistor corrans cort, queil color elle ait, si le fent si com j’ai dit des autres apostemes;	4. If the abscess is moist, cut it according to its color, as I said about other abscesses;
et se aprés l’entromissoire nen vient moistor, saiches qu’il est gras, si le fent donques en croix, et le prent as pinceures, et l’escorche legierement de chescune part et warde la cotte ou il gist que tu la traies saine avec le nout;	After the entrenchment, if there is no moisture, it is fat and if you make it a cross, take it with pliers, and lightly scrape each part and wipe the wound with the nail;
et se tu ne la pues traire saine, si la trai par pieces si qu’il n’i demoure rien.	and if you do not make it clean, if you take it in pieces so that nothing comes out.
Car s’il i demoure rien, si revient li nous par maintes fois;	For if nothing comes out, it will return to us many times.
et s’il en demore un poc, et li sans te grieve, si emple la plaie d’aucunes poudres corrosives agues, et estraint la plaie, et met sus choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez;	And if it drains a pouch, and does not grieve you, use the wound with some corrosive powders, close the wound, and put soothing ointments on the incision, and cure other wounds as long as it is healthy.
et se li nous est grans, si cout les II levres de la plaie, et le cure de ceu qui enjanre char.	If it is large, then we will cut the two lips of the wound, and treat the one who is causing the pain.
et se li voine batans t’est contraire ou autre si te haste et emple le leu de vitriole broiet, et lou laisse liiet II jors ou III, tant que li plaie porrisse, et repose li ebulicion dou sanc;	If the vein is battered and it is against or otherwise, if you hasten and use the leech of vitriol broth, and leave it for II to III hours, as long as the wound is burning, and rest the inflammation of blood;
puis revien au coper ceu que i est demoreit dou nout.	Then return to the compass that it is not too much out.
Vez ci les formes des estrumens entromissoires, et sont de III manieres:	See the forms of the entangled protrusions, and are of three kinds:
grans et moien et petit;	large and moldy and small.
et s’en i a III quarrez qui sont apelez «albaret», et I qui est apelez «breb», et s’en i a de III manieres:	and there are three kinds that are called "alabar" and one that is called "breb", and there are three kinds:
grant, moien, et petit, por encerchier les apostemes de fistule;	To prevent dislocation, one must first grasp the head of the shoulder with a firm grip, using a small movement to avoid causing further injury. This is done to securely hold onto the fistula's openings.
et sont ausi com les aguilles dont on cout les sorceles, et sont d’arain citrin, ou de fer, ou d’argent, et mues valent cil qui sont jaune, et sont plus esprovez de plonc noir por encerchier les corbeures de fistule;	They are similar to the beaks of birds, which are counted in gold, silver, or copper, and are more valued if they are yellow, and are more skilled at grasping the fistula openings than black ones.
et sont de III manieres:	They come in three different ways:
grans, moiens, et petis, selonc la quantiteit de la largesce des pertus.	large, medium, and small, depending on the size of the abscess.
Les formes des oncines sont de mout de semblances, si com tu vois ci:	The shapes of the tumors are quite varied, as you can see here:
grans, moiens, et petis;	The first sentence translates to: "Great, means, and small ones.
et si a oncines qui ont II corbeures de III manieres ausi;	The second sentence translates to: "And if there are those who have two eyes of three kinds?
et si a oncines qui ont III corbeures, et sont ausi de III manieres;	The third sentence translates to: "And if there are those who have three eyes and they are of three kinds?
et si a oncines qui ont II corbeures, et oncines d’une corbeure soulement, et sont de III manieres;	The fourth sentence translates to: "And if there are those who have two eyes and one eye only, and they are of three kinds?
et tuit cist sont necessaire en lor leu.	The fifth sentence translates to: "And these are necessary for their healing.
Li chief de ces a coi on fent sont trenchant, et de telz i a qui ne taillent mie fuer que d’une part, dont on escorche les nous, por ceu c’on ne cope la voine ne le nerf;	The sixth sentence translates to: "The head of these we make very sharp, and such ones are those that cannot cut through flesh, because one does not touch the vein or the nerve.
et de ces intromissoires sont les alemeles reponues en mainches, si que li malaide ne s’en persoivent a l’overture des apostemes;	and of these intramuscular injections, the aliments are returned in handcuffs, so that the patient does not escape from the opening of the abscesses.
et sont de III manieres:	and there are three ways:
grant, petit, et moien, si com tu vois;	great, small, and slow, as you see;
et n’en use on mie fuer que en leu charnut, si com jambes, et bras, et mameles, et as angres, et en semblans leus;	but only use them in the joints of the legs, arms, and hands, and the fingers, and in similar places;
et aucune fois fait on I autre estrument petit, semblant a escorces de fistices, selonc ceste forme, a coi on estainche sanc:	and no other instrument is ever made that resembles the forceps of scissors, according to this form, and it is not cut:
et le met on aucune fois au leu qui saine a copement des voines, et as arteres, et aucune fois reont selonc ceste grant forme:	and it is placed on none at all times in the shoulder that can withstand the pressure of the veins and arteries, and never returns to this great form:
Aucune fois enflent les mameles d’aucuns homes quant cil encomencent estre corrumput, tant qu’eles semblent mameles de feme;	No time have the hands of some men swollen when they are in great pain, as if they were hands of women:
et demorent laides et enflees, et qui les vuet curer, si le covient soier selonc ceste forme des ceste ligne .b. jusques a .g.:	1. And the lame and swollen ones, and those who see them cured, if they come to agree with this form of this line: b. until g:.
puis escorche la graisse, et emple la plaie de medicine enjanrant char, puis assemble les II levres de la plaie a costure, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee;	2. Then scorch the fat, and apply the wound with a hot needle, then stitch the lips of the wound as close as possible, and cure it until it is healthy.
et se li mamele cline aval, et est amolie por sa grandor si com il avient as femmes, si la fent en II costelz desus, par II semblans fendures;	3. And if the wound is inclined, and is widened for its growth, as it is in women, if they are made into stitches, through the similar twists.
de coi l’une soit tenans a l’autre a la fin de l’une et de l’autre, si que li plus grans ligne conteigne la menor selonc ceste forme, des ceste ligne .b. jusc’a la ligne .g.;	4. And if one holds onto the other at the end of each and every one, if the largest line contains the smallest according to this form, up to this line g. until g.
puis escorche le cuir qui est entre les II levres, et oste la graisse, et i amenistre ceu que nos avons dit de costure et de poudres, et ceu qui est necessaire en la cure, tant qu’il soit sanez;	Then the skin that is between the second lips is burned, and the fat is removed, and what we have said about sewing and powders is carried out, and what is necessary for the cure, as long as it is healthy.
et s’il n’est sanez, ou li incision n’est mie toute faite, por ceu que li malaides ne vuet reposer, ou por le decorrement de sanc, si covient que tu emplisses la plaie de coton moilliet en oignement corrosif;	And if it is not healthy, or the incision is not completely done, because the patient does not rest, or due to the evacuation of blood, then you must fill the wound with cotton soaked in corrosive ointment.
et le laisse tant qu’il menjuce le remenant et la graisse, puis le cure tant qu’il soit saneis.	And leave it as long as it drains the discharge and fat, then treat it as soon as it is healthy.
des apostemes des asselles	Of the abscesses of the horseshoes
Cist apostemes que vienent desoz les asseles sont manieres de scrophules dures ou il ait cotes, et s’en i a que contienent moistor.	The abscesses that come from the horseshoes are made of hard scrophulous or have corners, and they contain moisture.
Cil donques qui contienent moistor covient qu’il soient copez selonc ceste forme, des la ligne .b. jusc’a la ligne .g.:	Therefore, those that contain moisture must be cut according to this form, along the line .b., and then along the line .g.:
Et quant toute li bowe qui est en l’aposteme est vuidie, si emple la plaie de viel coton, et la laisse jusc’a l’autre jor, puis oste tout le coton, et cure d’oignement avenant a ceu tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when all the bone in the abscess is visible, use a piece of clean cotton and leave it until the next day, then remove all the cotton and treat with ointment as needed until it is healthy.
Et se li apostemes est de semblances de scrophules, si le fent si com nos avons dit en fendures des scrophules, et se li plaie rent bowe, si amenistre cautere si com nos avons dit devant.	When the patient's response resembles scabs, if it is like we have said in our descriptions of scabs, and the wound is not deep, then apply a cauterization as we have described before.
de la routure de l’artere	of the rupture of the artery
Quant li artere est route, et li cuir est soudez qui est sus, si en vient maintes fois apostemes, et tout aussi avient il a la voine enflee et aposteme;	When the artery is pricked, and the blood flows out, if it happens many times, and also the vein bleeds;
et si le conoist on ensi quant c’est por l’artere, si est li apostemes lons em parfont;	and if the patient has pain when it is the artery, if it pricks the vein;
et quant tu le sens a tes dois, si sens I estraignement;	and if you feel pain in your hand, if you hold it steady;
et quant c’est por la voine, si est reons defuer aparans;	and if it is for the vein, if it is pulled out;
et c’est folie de coper cest aposteme, et meismement quant il est desoz les asseles et as angres et ou col et em mout d’autres leus, et est mout grans.	and it is madness to stop the bleeding, and at the same time when it is loosened and the bands and buttons are broken and the guts and the inside of the body, and it is greatly hurt;
Il covient donques eschuir la cure de fer, et celui qui est a chief covient eschuir ausi, et en celui qui est d’enfleure d’artere fent par desus le cuir dou lonc;	It is therefore necessary to avoid the use of iron, and the one who is in charge must also avoid it, and in the one who is made of entangled arteries by being cut through the skin long.
puis oevre la taille as oncines, et depart bellement l’artere des toiles, tant qu’ele soit descoverte;	Then work the size as the bones, and beautifully cut the artery of the tendons, as much as it is discovered.
puis boute desoz li une aguille, et la fai percier jusc’a l’autre costeit, et estraint l’artere d’un fil double en II leus, selonc ceu que je t’ai ensigniet en l’estraction des II arteres qui sont en temples;	Then sew it with a needle, and make it pierce on the other side, and tighten the artery with a double thread in it, according to what I have shown you in the extraction of the arteries that are in the temples.
puis point le leu qui est entre les II liens d’un intromissoire tant que li sans en isse qui i est, et soit deliiez li aposteme;	Then, if the leg that is between the second and third joints of an instrument is not released when it is inserted, and there is no dislocation, then release the abscess.
puis amenistre la cure que enjanre bowe, tant que li liien chient;	Then, if the cure does not fit well enough to hold the bow, then...
puis cure ceu d’oignement avenant a ceu, tant qu’il soit sanez;	Then, if the cure is applied to this wound, then...
et se li apostemes est por la taille de la voinne, si covient que tu teignes a ta main ceu que tu pues de l’aposteme a tout le cuir, puis boute l’aguille desoz le leu que tu tiens a ta main, et la fai percier, et i ait I fil double, si que tu le trais de l’autre costeit;	And if the abscess is large enough to cover the vein, then... do this: grasp the abscess with your hand, remove it from the limb you are holding in your hand, and cut the thread with the other hand, and make sure there are two strings, so that you take it off from the other side;
puis lie l’aposteme, si com je t’ai dit, ou liien de l’une de II pars as II chiés dou fil;	Then tie the suture, if I may, or one of the two parts of the second part of the two heads of the hair.
et se tu doutes que li filz n’isse fuer, si i reboute une autre aguille a tout I fil desoz tout l’aposteme a l’incision de la premiere aguille, et estraint les filz en IIII leus;	And if you doubt that the threads will not hold, then replace another needle at the end of all the thread and draw out the threads through all the sutures at the first needle's end, and draw them tight in four places.
puis cope l’aposteme tant que li superfluitez en isse, puis cope la superfluiteit dou keur et laisse ceu qui est liiez;	Then pull the suture as much as the excess will allow, then pull the excess from the end and leave what is left.
puis met sus I drapeil moilliet en vin et en oile, puis li amenistre cures de tentes et d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then apply a wet cloth to the wound and oil it, and treat it with tent boards and bandages as much as it is necessary.
des apostemes des ners	The first sentence to translate is: "Ou cautere de feu comande au
Ausi com aposteme vienent en l’artere et en la voine, vienent aposteme as ners quant il sont ferut, ou par trop grant travail, et semblans choses.	When the fire cautery is instructed to the patient, apostes come from the artery and vein, come apostes from nerves when they are too tight or due to excessive work, and similar things occur.
Et ceu avient plus sovent as adjutoires et as dois et en toz leus ou il ait jointures, et c’est I grief apostemes, et sa color semble la color dou cors, et est em plusors dispositions sens dolor;	And this often happens with helpers and you must do it in all joints, and it is an injury, and its color resembles the color of a wounded heart, and it is more commonly found in positions that cause pain.
et quant on l’estraint forment, si sent li malaides dolor, et n’est mie em parfont dou cors, mais desoz lou keur;	And when it is held steady, if it feels pain, and it is not from a wounded heart but from the curvature of the neck, then...
et muet bien de toutes pars, et ne va ne avant ne arrier, ne desoz ne desus, et celui qui est en jointures ne covient mie coper par fer:	And it remains still for all purposes, and does not move before or after, nor is it dislocated, and the one who is in joints cannot be moved without force.
par aventure i vanroit contraction;	by chance, it may contract.
et cil qui est ou chief ou ou front, fent le cuir au spatumile.	And the one who is head or face, makes the hide at the stump.
Se li apostemes est petis, si le tien a unes tenailles, et le cope en sa racine;	If the abscess is small, and it is held with nails, and the poultice is applied to its root.
et s’il est grans, si le sospent a l’oncine, et l’escorche, puis l’oste et assemble la plaie a la costure, et lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if it is large, and the gout spreads to the bone, and the flesh burns, then the bone assembles the wound at the seam, and the cure is done as soon as it is healthy.
des grosses boces pendans	Large hanging jaws
Aucune fois avient en ventres et ne mie autre part thelul, et est une maladie qui est apelee «funge» par la semblance d’aus, et est li racine subtilz, et li chiez gros;	There is no time in the womb and does not affect any other part, and it is a disease called "fungus" because of its appearance, and it is at the root, and the head is large.

Then tie it with the second thread to the pouch and the indicator, 2. place it between the two loops, 3. then gently pull on the handle quickly and cut the end of the thread.
puis laisse corre le sanc poc et poc, car c’est li muedres;	1. Then leave the vein loose for a moment, as it is evil.
et met poudre sus et sus la poudre I drapeil glueit d’un moieuf d’uef cuit destempreit d’aigue rose, confit avec oile roset boin et fres, et lou laisse sus jusc’a l’autre jor, et le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	1. Then put powder on it and on the powder, 2. then cut a piece of bread and dip it in cooked meat broth that has been cooled with rose water, olive oil, and salt, 3. then place it on the other side, and care for it as long as it is healthy.
Li forme des forces a la mundification si est ceste:	The form of the forces at the mundification if this is:
li dui chiés soient tenves et soient trenchans, et soient li chiés ausi grant com li mainche igalment:	The heads should be thin and even, and as strong as the right hand consistently.
li error de la mundification si est quant li keurs dedens fuit a l’incision;	The error of mundification if it is when the teeth come out at the incision.
donques il covient que tu l’estendes a ton ungle, ainsois que li leus faice aposteme;	Therefore, you must stretch it to your nail, unless the tooth causes apoplexy.
et le cope igalment, et se tu ne lou pues tenir a ton ungle, si le tien as tenailles, et puis le cope.	And the crown should be even, and if you do not hold it to your nail, then the crown will have sharp points, and then the crown.

si le cope si com tu pues mues, et te garde de la partie de la verge, ce ne li nuira niant.	If the copse is as you say it is, and you keep hold of the part of the bark, it will not harm you.

cure le donques, si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Cure the wound as we have said, until it is healthy.
dou retenement de l’urine	The second line of the text translates to: "Hold back the urine.
Li retenue de l’urine si est d’opilation de piere, ou de sanc congeleit, ou de bowe, ou de char nee, ou de semblans choses, que nos avons dit en la division;	The retention of urine if it is of opiliation of the urethra, or of sanguination of the incision, or of bowels, or of cholestatic jaundice, or of similar things, which we have said in the division.
et se li urine n’est desliie , et tu vois estre la retenue por la piere qui est jai ou col de la vessie, si covient que li malaides soit corbés sus ses genoulz;	And if the urine is not discharged, and you see that it is retained by the urethra which is at the hip or the neck of the bladder, then it comes to pass that the patient's health is endangered.
et li soient mis li piez sor le dos, et estende son ventre de la partie desus lou dos, et restraigne li malaides s’alainne tant com il puet;	And it is placed on the back and extended over the abdomen from the part below the back, and the patient's pain is limited as much as possible.

et soit d’argent subtilz legiere chevee, si com li penne d’un oiseil;	and let silver subtly lighten the hair, as if it were the tail of a swallow.

et cope la superfluiteit de la lainne et le boute jusc’au chief de la siringue, puis oint la siringue d’oile ou de burre et d’aubin d’uef, et fai seoir le malaide sus I siege, et li arose la vessie et la verge d’oile moiste et d’oile d’olive et d’aigue tede;	and cut the superfluity of the hair and tie the root of the thread with the thorn of the ring, then anoint the ring with oil or balsam and ointment of urine and olive oil and German tea, and make the patient sit on the seat and the verge of the bladder wet and oiled and ointed with olive oil and German tea.
puis met legierement la siringue en la verge, tant qu’elle viegne a la racine de la verge, puis double la verge desus devers la boude;	Then gently place the thread at the edge, as it reaches the root of the leaf, then fold the leaf inwards towards the vein.

puis estent le fil a tout la laine poc et poc, et li urine en suit la laine, puis l’estrai fuer, et fai corre l’urine;	Then the thread is pulled through all the hair, and the urine follows the hair, then it is drawn out and the urine is made up.

des maladies de la vessie	Of diseases of the bladder
Quant escorcheures ou sanc vient en la vessie, ou porriture i est assemblee, et tu i vues distiller aigues et medicines, si fai a tout l’estrument qui est apellé «clepsedre», et c’est li forme:	When scald or blood comes into the bladder, or when there is purulent discharge and you see water and medicines being distilled, then make sure to cleanse all the instrument called "clepsieder", and it is in this form:

de la piere	The first sentence to translate is: "Car en

de la piere des femmes	of the women's incision
Poc avient que piere soit enjanree en femmes, et s’il avient aucune fois, si est li cure grief, et est deffendut por III choses:	1. A wound comes when a piercing is infected in women, and if it has never happened, it is due to the grief of the surgeon, and is defended by three things:
l’une est que per aventure li femme est vierge;	1. One is that by chance the woman is virgin;
et li seconde est c’on ne puet trover femme bien saichant qui se descuevre as mires, meismement quant elle est caste.	1. The second is that it is not often found a woman well-bred who has been disfigured by wounds, even when she is young;

et li quarte maniere si est que li piere de la femme si est plus em parfont que li piere de l’ome, por coi il i couvient faire plus parfonde taille, et grant paour i a. And the fourth way is that if by chance the woman's wound is more than the man's, because it requires a more perfect size, and great pain it causes. And if it becomes necessary to set it, then choose a skilled midwife, and if you cannot find one, then cut it yourself, and if you cannot cut it, then do not cast the woman in shame;

c’est a savoir, petites et grans et aspres et souez, longes et reondes, et qui ont rains.	This is to know, small and large, sharp and smooth, long and curved, and those that have joints.

de hernie carnouse	of hernia carcinoma
Ramice aquouse n’est autre chose que assemblee de moistor ou blanc syfac, qui est desoz lou keur des coions, que contient l’uef;	Wet dressings are nothing more than assemblies of moisture or white soap, which are made from the urine of the cow, which contains the urea.
et est apelez «syfac», et aucune fois est proprement en la toile de l’uef, si c’on cuide que ce soit I autre oef;	And is called "si fac," and never properly in the thread of the eye, if one takes care that it is not another tool;
et c’est li cuir dou coion entre lou blanc syfac que nos avons dit;	and it is the white skin between the "si fac" we have mentioned;

dou chastrement	1. "dou chastrement" translates
Saiches que chastremens est escomeniez en nostre loi, et por ceu il me plairoit que je n’en parlasse mie en cest livre;	1. Sicknesses that are caused by cold are mentioned in our law, and this is why I preferred not to discuss them in this book.
et n’est necessaires fuer que por II manieres:	2. It is necessary for two reasons:
dont l’une est que li mires en saiche respondre quant on li demandera, et en saiche la cure;	3. One reason is that the patient's response to the question and treatment can be determined through observation;
et li autre, por ceu que nos avons sovent mestier de chastrement d’aucunes bestes por nos aidier, si com de bouc et de mouton et de chait et d’autres bestes.	4. The other reason is that we often perform castration of certain animals for our help, such as sheep and lambs, and goats, and others.
Je dis donques que chastremens est fais selonc II manieres:	5. Therefore, I say that sicknesses are treated in these two ways:
ou par atraction, ou par fendure.	6. Either by attraction or by burning.
En celle que nos faisons par attraction, faisons nos seoir la beste en aigue chaude, tant que li coion soient mollifiez et pendant;	In the one that we make by attraction, let our seat be the best in hot water, as long as the coin is softened and during.
puis les preing a ta main, tant qu’il soient remis et que tu ne les sentes plus.	Then put your finger in it, as long as they are back and you no longer feel them.
Du chastrement de taille:	Of size reduction:
covient que tu teignes la beste, et li presse le cuir des coions a ta main senestre, puis lie le suspensoire, et cope sus chescun oef a I cop, quant tu les avras bien escorchiez;	It is necessary that you tighten the best seat, and press the curved part of the coin with your left hand, then pull the suspender, and cut each knot at the end of the coin when you have well burned them.
et i laisse aucun poc dou syfac et lou subtil syfac qui est sor les vasselz;	and leave no small sore or subtle sore that is on the veins.
et ceste maniere de chastrement est muedre que cele qui est faite par attraction, por ceu que a l’atraction demoure par aventure aucune chose des coions, par coi li beste desire luxure;	This method of restraint is more effective than that which is made by attraction, because attraction does not tire from any adventure, as the beast desires pleasure.
puis cure la plaie tant qu’ele soit sanee.	Then treat the wound while it is still healthy.

Hermofrodie est selonc II manieres as homes:	Hermann's method can be divided into two categories for humans:

en la seconde maniere, des homes dont li urine saut par lou cuir des coions, si n’a point de cure.	In the second manner, men whose urine leaps from the skin of their thighs, if there is no treatment.
de la tentigene	The first sentence to translate is "de la tentigene

de l’issue des gemelz	Of the issue of the twins
