puis la quier saigement a ton pooir, que tu conoisses s’il i a os ou nerf, et est chevee em parfont, et demande bien au malaide de la dolor qu’il sent au presser de ta main, et le leu ou il la sent;	Then, if you are wise, you will know whether it is bone or flesh, and ask the patient well about the pain they feel when their hand is pressed, and where they feel the pain.
et quant tu savras vraiement le leu ou elle est, et s’elle est loing de jointure, ou de nerf, ou d’artere ou de voine, ou en aucuns des leus que je t’ai dit, si la cope selonc ceu que je t’ai dit, et oste fuer la fautreure et les chars corrumpues que sont dedens;	And when you truly know the bone or flesh, and whether it is far from the joint, or the nerve, or the artery or vein, or any of the joints I have mentioned, if the copper according to what I have said, and the falsehood and the corrupt bones that are dense.
et puis la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee, et se li fistule est bien parfonde de droit endroit, si covient que tu copes em parfont, tant com tu pues, puis i met tentes moillies en medicine ague, et les boute jusc’au chief de la fistule, tant que li medicine corrode la superfluiteit qui est demoree au fons;	Then the cure, as long as she is healthy, and if the fistula is well lined with the right place, then it should be covered as soon as possible, as soon as you can, then put fine cloths in the medicated water, and the bougies are inserted into the head of the fistula, as long as the medicine corrodes the superfluity that is left in the font.
et puis i met oignemens enjanrans sainne char, tant qu’il soit sanez;	then put clean bandages on the healthy part, as long as it is healthy.
et s’il n’est sanez par ceu, si le cauterize si com nos avons dit, et se li os est corrompus de la fistule, si le cope.	if it is not healthy by this, then the cauterization is done as we have said, and if the part is corrupted by the fistula, then it should be cut off.
Se voinne ou ners ne te greve ou membres principelz, si com nos avons dit;	If the joint does not cause pain or the principal limbs do not suffer, as we have said.
et se li os est descovers, et il i a corruption et noiror, si lou reis tant que li corruption soit toute ostee, puis le cure de choses enjanrans char tant qu’il soit sanez;	And if the bone is discovered, and it becomes corrupted and black, until the corruption is completely removed, then the treatment of things that are strange and unusual will be done as soon as it is healthy.
et s’il n’est sanez, et rent bowe si com devant, saiches que tu n’es mie alez jusc’a font:	And if it is not healthy, and the belly becomes thin, as before, you should know that you are not fit to do this.
si descuevre et quier tant que tu soies au fons, et oste toute la corruption, puis restore le leu;	If the dislocation is discovered and you want it as much as you can be at the joint, and remove all the corruption, then restore the limb.
et s’il est ensi sanez, c’est bien.	And if it is healthy, that is good.
Se ceu non, saiches que la corruption est trop en parfont, que tu n’i pues avenir;	If not, you should know that corruption is too advanced, and it will not improve.
si n’i a autre engien que dou lassier a nature;	if there is no other means than natural remedies.
et s’il i a i petit os corrumput, et tu le pues traire as tenailles, si l’estrai a I estrument covenauble a ceu, et s’il i a maint os, si les trai trestoz, ne n’en laissier nes un;	if there is a small corrupted bone, and you can remove it with needles, if possible, and if there are more, do not leave any;
et se li moistor te fait contraire, et il n’i a error ne paour, si cope et moistor et char, et delivre les os.	and if the moisture is against you, and there is no pain or fear, then cope with it and endure the heat, and deliver the bones;
Et se tu ne les pues oster a une houre, si met sus la plaie chose enjanrant porriture, et laisse tant que li leus soit porris entor les os, et adonc si avront plus legierement les os;	And if you do not cut the bones in an hour, if you put something slippery on the wound, and leave it as long as it is moist between the bones, and then they will become lighter between the bones;
et se c’est uns grans os, si com de jambe ou de cuisse, si reis tant soulement la corruption tant que li noiror soit toute ostee, puis restoure la plaie;	and if it is large bones, such as thigh or knee, if only the corrosion remains until blackness covers the entire area, then restore the wound.
et s’il en i a grant partie dou corrumput, et vient jusc’a mole de l’os;	and if it has large parts of corroded bone, and comes near the bone;
si le covient soier et coper tout jusc’a la corruption, et puis le cure tant qu’il soit soudez;	if it is necessary to sew and cover all the corrosion, and then treat as much as possible;
et je te dirai d’une fistule qui avint I home en sa jambe, si que tu i preignes exemple et aide en ton ovraige.	and I will tell you about an abscess that came to one's leg, if you take it as an example and help in your practice.
Il fut I jovencelz entor XXX ans, qui ot une dolor en sa jambe d’une cause que vint dedens le cors, tant que les matieres vinrent a la jambe, et fut enflee d’un gros aposteme, et n’ot point de cause defuer por ovrir;	It was the young man who had been in his thirties, who had a pain in his leg for a cause that came from the chest, so much that the materials came to the leg, and he was hidden by a large abscess, and there was no reason to open it;
mais li mire par lor folie ovrerent tant sus que li apostemes ovri, et en corroient mout de matieres, et devint fistule, et i vint mout de pertus que tuit gitoient bowe et moistor dou cors;	But the patient was so mad that they overwrote everything, and it corrupted the materials, and became a fistula, and then pus came out of the wounds and the cold made the body shiver and the moisture increased.
et maint mire i mirent cure entor II ans, et n’i ot nul saige en l’art de mains, tant que je i fui apelez, et vi sa jambe et les medicines dont on le curoit, et ceu que corroit par les pertus a grant cors;	And for two years, they were cured, and no one had any knowledge of the art of hands, as I was called, and I saw their leg and the medicines used to cure them, and what was corrupted by the pus at great cost.
et devenoit rouges li cors dou jouvenceil, et avoit color citrine.	And the patient's cheeks became red, and had a citron color.
Je boutai une tente en l’un de ces pertus, et puis cerchai toz les pertus, et trovai que li uns venoit encontre l’autre de toutes les parties de la jambe.	I sewed a tent in one of these holes, and then checked all the holes, and found that some came together at the other part of the leg.
Je me hastai donques, et copai en l’un des pertus tant que je descovri une partie de l’os, et le trovai corrumput et perciet, et venoit li corruption jusc’a l’os dedens;	I was surprised, and I found in one of the wounds a part of the bone, and I discovered it was corrupted and decayed, and the corruption reached the dens of the bones.
je soiai ceu qui m’aparissoit de l’os corrumput, et cuidai qu’il n’i eust autre corruption, fuer que celi que je ostai;	I was the one who appeared from the corrupted bone, and I took care that it had no other corruption, as long as I stayed.
et comensai a restourer la plaie de medicines sodans par lonc tens, et ne pot souder;	and began to restore the wound with long stitches of sodanic medicines, and could not stitch.
et puis rencomensai, et descovri l’os si com devant, et trovai la corruption continuee en l’os, et la soiai, et puis l’ostai, et me penai de souder le leu;	and then I took it out again, and revealed the bone as far as possible, and found continued corruption in the bone, and treated it, and then put it back in, and made a decision to stitch the joint.
mais je ne pou tant que je copai entor une palme de l’os, et le traï fuer a tout son mole, puis le restourai de medicines;	but I could not do it until I cut off a piece of the bone, and it was all its size, then I restored it with medicines.
et il fut sanez et soudez hastanment, et ne covint plus rencomencier l’ovraige fors por la foibleté dou malaide, qui ne pooit soffrir, et por la paour de mort que je avoie de lui.	And it was cured and relieved quickly, and he did not want to repeat the operation because of the inability of the surgeon, who could not endure it, and for fear of death that I had for him.
Car por l’evacuation sanglotoit sovent, mais il fut sanez entierement, et nasquit en leu de l’os une char dure, et fut de bone disposition et n’ot point de nuisement ne de contraire dou tout en tout, ne a l’aleir ne a venir.	For as the evacuation of blood is often, but it was completely healthy, and a hard char was found on the bone, and it was well positioned and had no harm or opposite effect in any way, nor in the air nor coming.
Et se li os est brisiez en aucun leu dou cors, si le covient soier en ceste maniere:	And if the bone is broken in no joint of the arm, then it should be set in this way:
pren I liien, et l’estrain au chief de l’os qui apert, et comande aucun k’il l’estende en haut;	Take the levers, and draw the head of the bone up to the open end, and command that it does not extend further up.
et met I autre lien de lainne plus gros dou premier liien, et le lie sus la char qui est desor l’os, et estent le chief, si que tu traies la char corrumpue au desoz, et descuevre la char sus le leu ou tu vues soier, que li soie ne blece la char;	And take another lever of greater size than the first one, and lie it on the cheek that is on the bone, and pull the head, if you can draw the broken part of the bone away from the cheek, and release the cheek, so that the lever does not break the cheek.
et met I tison ou une tauble desoz l’os por mues coper la char corrumpue;	And place the incision at a distance of one finger's breadth from the bone to cover the corrupted part.
et covient tant soier com on puet veoir et sentir la corruption, et soier ancor autre fois.	And soak as much as possible and see and feel the corruption, and soak again.
Et se li os est corrumpus, et n’apert mie, et li corruptions est en mileu ou en une partie, si descuevre la char toute;	And if the bone is corrupted and does not open, and the corruption is in the surrounding tissue or a part of it, then cut through the entire bone.
puis met I tison desoz, et puis soie des l’une partie a l’autre la corruption, et soit li soieure dou lonc de la corruption I poc, si com nos avons dit;	Then make another incision, and then soak the affected part with water from one end to the other, and let the water be as long as the corruption is deep. As we have said.
et se li corruptions est en la jointure, si cope la jointure corrumpue, et soie l’os ou elle contient de l’autre part;	And if the corruption is in the joint, then cut the corrupted joint, and see if the bone or it contains another part.
et se li corruptions est en la continuation des II jointes, si n’i a autre angien que dou coper;	And if corruption spreads to the continuation of the second joints, if there is no other cause than cold copper.
et se li corruptions est ou poignil de la main, ou ou poignil dou piet, si est mout fort celle chose, mais toutevoie il covient que tu enquieres celle corrosion, coment elle t’apert;	And if corruption is or a prick of the hand, or a prick of the foot, if it is very hard that thing, but it is necessary that you inquire about that corrosion, knowing how it opens.
et la mundifie en toutes les manieres que tu pues, mais que li voine ou li nerf ne te faicent contraire;	And you purify it in all ways that you can, but the vein or the nerve will not oppose you.
et saiches que li incisoire et les soies por coper ces os sont maintes, selonc l’assise des os et l’aparance d’ous, et lor grossece et lor subtiliteit, et lor grandor et lor petitece, et lor duresce;	And you question the incision and the bones that these bones are many, according to the seat of the bones and their appearance, and their thickness and their fineness, and their growth and their smallness, and their hardness.
et por ceu covient il apareillier a chescune semblance d’ovraige son estrument;	and because it happens in each appearance of the work's instrument.
et saiches que l’uevre te moustrera l’estrument dont tu avras mestier, selonc la conissance de cest art, et le tesmoignaige des manieres des maladies;	and you should know that the work will show the instrument you will use, according to the knowledge of this art, and it testifies to the ways of diseases.
si porpense l’estrument dont tu as mestier selonc ceu qu’il le covient.	if the instrument you will use does not match according to what is needed.
dou feu	The first line of the text is
Li chiés porrissent ou par cause dedens, ou par cause defuer;	The head of the shoulder presses due to weakness or by reason of drought.
et quant tu avras medicinee celle corrosion par la cure des medicines, et il ne profitent mie, si covient coper celui membre jusques au leu ou li corrosion vient, si que li malaides eschaipe par ceu de la mort, ou par la malice, qui est plus grans, de la defaute dou membre;	And when you have treated the corrosion with medicine, and it does not improve, then it may be necessary to cut into the member up to the place where the corrosion comes, if the malady is greater than that of the death or the malice, which is more serious, of the fault of the member.
et li signes si est que li membres devient noir, si qu’il semble qu’il soit ars dou feu, et porrist aprés la noiror, pues va celle corrosions de membre em membre, et prent par tout le cors;	When the signs appear that the limb becomes black, if it seems that it is from burning heat, and then after the discoloration, this corrosion spreads to all the limbs, and takes hold of everything.
si te haste dou coper, et se c’est par la percussion d’aucunes venimouses bestes, si com scorpion de mer et wivre et semblans, se li corrosion est au chief dou doi, si le cope, et ne li doner mie espaice de venir jusc’a la main.	If you feel heat in the body, and it is due to the impact of some beasts' venoms, like a sea scorpion and wasp, and if corrosion occurs at the site of heat, then the cope, and it does not give any spice to come to the hand.
Et s’elle vient jusc’a la main, si la cope a la jointe, si que la corrosion ne viegne jusc’a bras;	And if it comes to the hand, if the cope is at the joint, if the corrosion does not come to the arm.
et s’elle vient au bras, si le cope au coute;	If it comes to the elbow, if the cautery is at the cost.
et s’elle passe le coute, c’est li mors, et n’i vaut amenistremens fuers que li quantitez de sa vertut;	If it passes the cost, it is death, and there is no remedy except for the quantity of his virtue.
et tot ensi fai quant li corrosion vient ou piet:	And so entirely makes what the corrosion comes or pierce.
s’elle vient en la premiere jointe, si la cope aprés l’autre jointe;	If it comes in the first joint, if the cautery after another joint.
et s’elle vient ou piet, si cope tout le piet;	And if it comes or pierce, if the cautery all the virtue.
et s’elle monte en la jambe, si cope a la jointure dou genoil;	And if it goes up in the leg, if the cautery at the joint of the great toe.
et s’elle vient desus le genoil, si n’i a autre engien que dou lassier le malaide a mort;	And if it comes from above the knee, if there is no other engine but to kill the patient.
et li maniere dou coper ou dou soier le membre si est que tu le lie desus et desoz, et estende uns menistres l’un des liiens aval, et uns autres ministres l’autre liien amont, et tu dessevre la char qui est entre les II liiens a I spatumile large, tant que li os soit descovers;	And the manner of coping with or treating the member if it is that you bind it and loosen, and extend some measures on one of the lings above, and others on the other ling below, and you sew the thread that is between the two lings at the widest part of the bone as long as the bone is discovered.
puis le cope ou soie, et met de chescune part I drapeil de lin, si que li soie ne touche le leu sain, et viegne au malaide autre lesion et aposteme chaus.	Then the treatment or stitching, and use a different thread for each part, so that it does not touch the healthy skin, and go to the surgeon for another wound and gangrene.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient quant tu oevres, si cauterize le leu hastanment, ou tu met sus aucunes poudres restraignans;	And if the blood comes out when you work, if you cauterize the skin at once, or if you put on any constricting powders.
puis revien a ta medicine tant qu’elle soit acomplie, puis lie le membre navreit d’un liien covenauble, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez;	Then return to your medicine as soon as it is accomplished, then tie the injured limb with a flexile cord, and treat it as soon as it is healthy.
et je te conterai k’il avint a I home en som piet:	and I will tell you what happened to my home in a short time.
il li avint une noiror qui sembloit arsure de feu, et celle corrosion vint premier en son doi dou piet, tant qu’elle porprist tout le piet;	It appeared a black thing that seemed to be burning, and this corrosion came first in its youngest part, consuming the whole piece.
et quant li hons vit la corrosion, si se hasta de coper le piet, et fut sanez;	And when the wound was seen, if it could be closed, it became healthy.
et lonc tens aprés li revint li corrosion ou doi de la main, et il vint a moi, et je li mis sus choses repercussives aprés la mundification dou cors, et ne pot cesser li corrosions;	And later when the wound was returned to the hand, it came to me, and I put on things with the effect of disinfecting after embalming the corrosive parts, and it could not stop the corrosions.
et il vot que je li copasse la main, et je ne vou, que je avoie esperance de repercuter la matiere;	and I say that I will hold his hand, and I do not have hope of reflecting the matter.
et doutai ausi que se je tailloie sa main, qu’il ne morist, car li vertus de l’ome estoit foible;	and it also doubts that if I cut his hand, he will not die because the strength of the hand was weak.
et il se despera toz, et revint en sa terre, et se hasta de coper sa main, et fut sanez;	and he became desperate, and returned to his land, and managed to save his hand, and he was healthy.
et je n’ai ceu conteit fuers que por ceu c’on faice autreteil, s’on en a mestier.	and I have not heard of this before because we have other things to do, and we are used to it.
Aucune fois vient aposteme en leu charnut, et demore si longement qu’il fait grant assemblee de bowe;	Never has an apoplexy come to the wild boar, and it takes as long as it takes for a great assembly of arrows.
et puis ront et perce, et en saut li bowe, et demoure li leus vuis, ausi com uns vasselz;	Then it cuts and pierces, and with a jump, it breaks the bow, and frightens the watchers, just as some hunters do.
et li cuir qui est desus est ausi subtilz com I drapelz deliiez, et ne corront mie jusc’a l’os, ne jusc’au nerf, et telz maladie si est apelee «sain», et n’est mie apelee «fistule»;	The skin that is covered is as delicate as silk, and does not cover the bone or the nerve, and such disease is so called "holy" but should be called "fissure";
mais s’elle est si alongie qu’elle viegne jusc’a l’os em parfont, si est apelee «fistule»;	But if it is so long that it reaches the bone, then it should be called "fissure";
et li cuire si est que tu cope celui cuir tout entor, et meismement quant il est subtilz, ausi com uns drapelz;	And if the skin is such that it cuts through the entire skin, and at the same time, it is as delicate as silk, like some hunters do;
et ne s’aert mie por sa corruption.	and do not keep it for its corruption.
Et se tu as fiance que li cuirs s’aerde, et li corruption n’est mie en parfont, et li cuir est espés de char, si le cure de clistere ensi:	And if you are engaged and the hair does not become corrupted, and it is very thick, then the cure of clothing is easy:
regarde se li seins est grans, et li bowe qui en ist est de puant odor, adonques le clisterize de medicine egiptiaine qui est ensi faite:	look if the breasts are large, and the bow which is in it has a strong odor, therefore, the treatment with Egyptian medicine which is made here is:
prenez aisil, et oile, et litargire, igalment, et metez cuire en I vassel au feu, tant que li medicine soit rouge, et deviegne ausi espesse com miel;	take ashes, oil, and turpentine, mixed, and cook in one vessel over the fire until the medicine is red and as thick as honey:
et puis pren de ceu selonc ta necessiteit, et le font en aigue et en miel, et en clisterize lou sein, et estraint le pertus;	and then take according to your need, and make it in wine and honey, and cure the breast, and strain the pustule:
et laisse la medicine ens par II houres, puis l’estrai en espreignant;	and leave the medicine on for two hours, then remove it by pulling it out.
fai ce mout de fois, tant que li seins soit mondefiiez, et soit ostee li puor;	do this as many times as the breast is deformed and until the pain stops.
et aucune fois est clisterizeis d’aigue de cendres, quant ceste medicine n’est presens, et est que tu preignes cendres de fust de vigne, et giete aigue desus, puis la coule, et en clisterize, tant que tu saiches que li seins est bien mondez;	and never put ashes of smoke in the wound while this medicine is present, and if you use grapevine ash instead, and it causes pain, then remove it as soon as you feel that the breast is well-shaped.
et se li malaides ne le puet soffrir, ne la medicine egiptiaine ne l’aigue de cendres, si le clisterize d’aigue et de miel ou il ait un poc de litargire broiet;	and if the patient cannot bear it, and the Egyptian medicine does not cause pain, then remove the ashes of smoke with honey or if there is a little bit of burning, it should be done.
ou tu la clistirize de miel et de vin melleit, que li mielz ait proprieteit de mundifiier et de laver, et li vins fait aerdre le sain;	If you choose to rinse the wound with honey and wine mixture, where honey has the property of cleaning and washing, and wine makes it aerated and healthy.
et quant tu as ce fait, et tu as fiance que li seins est bien mundifiiez, si le clisterize de ceu que fait naistre char en li, et est que tu preignes emplaustre diafinit, et le font avec oile roset et en vin;	And when you have done this, and you ensure that the wound is well cleaned, if the rinse of this what is made in the, and it is that you preignes emplaustre diafinit, and they make with rose oil and wine.
ou tu le clisterize d’aucunes medicines et d’oignemens, dont j’ai dit les proprietez ou traitier des oignemens;	Or if you rinse the wound with some medicines and ointments, which I have mentioned their properties or treated of ointments.
et se li pertus dou sein est petis, et li cainne dou clistere n’i puet entrer, si l’eslarge d’un fer un poc, et met ens une tente de l’oignement egiptiein, ou oignement basilicon, tant k’il soit eslargiez;	And if the wound is small, and the rinse of the wound does not enter, if it is enlarged by a pin, and put in a tent of Egyptian ointment or basilicon ointment, as much as it is eslargiez.
et se li plaie est trop large, si la cout et i laisse tant soulement I leu ou li clistere puisse entrer, et se li pertus que giete bowe est au desus, si le cope ou plus bas leu que i est.	When the wound is too large, if it does not bleed sufficiently, and the doctor allows it to only touch the skin or the clyster can enter, and if the pus that gushes out is green, then the doctor or lower down on the leg than it is.
Car quant li bowe est en parfont, si n’i laisse enjanrer char;	When the wound is fully formed, if it does not leave any space for the stitch;
et se tu ne pues coper lou sein desoz si com tu vues, si appareille en tel maniere que li bowe corre au plus bas leu que i est, car quant li bowe est parfont, si n’i laisse enjanrer char et se tu ne pues coper lou sein desoz si com tu vues, si apareille en teil maniere:	and if you do not cover the wound with something like we have seen, if it appears in such a way that the wound correals to the lowest part of the leg where it is, since when the wound is fully formed, if it does not leave any space for the stitch, and if you do not cover the wound with something like we have seen, if it appears in such a way that the wound correals to the lowest part of the leg where it is;
que li bowe corre legierement aval, et n’i lassier rien de la bowe;	That the bowel is cut lightly, and nothing of the bowel is left.
et pren medicines consolidatives por mettre sor le sain, et estent sus I drapeil de lin que cuevre tout le sain;	And take consolidating medicines to heal the wound, and they are laid on a flaxen cloth that covers the entire wound.
puis cope as forces endroit le pertus dou sein I poc plus large dou premier, pues estent oignement souef sus I autre drapel selonc la quantiteit dou pertus, et le met sus le pertus dou sain por aligier la bowe, et n’oster mie le grant drapeil fuers que aprés maint jor une fois;	Then apply as much force as possible to the narrower part of the chest, and lay another flaxen cloth according to the quantity of the wound, and place it over the wound of the sore to align the bowel, and do not leave the large cloth until after one more time.
et celui qui est sor le pertus dou sein, oste sovent por oster la bowe, et saiches ceu que corra de la bowe, se c’est venin ou poc ou assez, ou digeste, ou indigeste;	And the one who is sore at the wound of the chest often presses on the bowel, and examines what comes from the bowel, whether it is poison or not, or too much, or not enough, or digested, or undigested.
et pren warde se li patiens sent dolor ou nom, et s’il i a aposteme ou non, et quant ta medicine s’est en teil maniere estendue et tu vois la nature que saut sus le pertus dou sain, si saiches que li seins s’aert ja, et aproche li santez;	et pren warde se li patiens sent dolor ou nom, and if the patient feels pain or not, and when your medicine has been extended and you see the nature that it is ascending and if the chest seems to be already broken, and approach the health.
et puis le deslie le matin, ou le tier jor, et quant tu delies la plaie, si chainge I autre drapeil, et renovele l’oignement.	and then take off the bandage either in the morning or at night, and when you examine the wound, if it changes to another fold, and change the dressing.
Et se li seins giete bowe indigeste aprés maint jor, saiches que li seins ne s’aert mie.	And if the breasts become wet and indigestible after the year, it is advisable that the breasts not be exposed to the air.
Et se venins subtilz cort aprés lonc tens, si ne te desperer mie de la santeit, car li santez aproche.	And if the venomous substances are found after a long time, do not despair of your health, as the health is approaching.
Car il i a homes cui tarde enjanremens de char en ses plaies, et de ces que font le contraire;	For he has many times injured his wounds with sharp things, and those who do the opposite.
et se bowe indigeste saut dou sein aprés maint jor, saiches que li seins ne s’aert mie;	and if the belly is indigestible and jumps after one night, thinks that the chest is not broken.
et se li seins tarde d’aerdre, et est porloigniez, si ajoste medicines sechans moistes en substance et seches en vertut, si com oignement diafinit, car il i a grant partie de vitriole, et c’est li derriene medicine;	And if the shoulder is late in healing, and it is treated, if the dry medicines are moistened in substance and fresh in virtue, as specified, because it has a large part of vitrol, and this is the rear medicine.
pren oignement dyafinit, et le font avec oile roset, et l’arose de viel vin igal en substance;	If the ointment is specified, and it is made with rose oil, and the wine is mixed in small amount;
puis le confit et en use;	Then it is preserved and used.
et ceu meisme fait mielz cuit engroissiez, quant oignemens dyafinit n’est presens, ou tu pren mirre et aloen et encens, et le broie, et le poudre sus le miel quant il est sor le feu;	And the same thing is made honey cooked, when the ointments are not present, or you take razor and oil and incense, and the powder, and the honey when it is on fire;
et puis en glue I drapel, et l’estent sor le sein, et aucune fois i aministre on aristologe longe, et racines de lis celeste, qui est ausi com farine de veces et centoire;	Then in glue I drapel, and stretch it around the neck, and never once has an astrologer given any advice on this, and the roots of these celestial herbs, which is also like flour and cinnamon.
et en use de simples ou de compostes:	and in use of simple or compound drugs:
broie les, et en fai poudre, et met sus le miel que j’ai dit, et en use;	break them, and make a powder, and mix with the honey I mentioned, and use it.
et se li cure est alongie, et n’est curez par ceste cure, adonc saiches que la corruptions est em parfont, et fait empression en l’os, ou as membres durs, ou as liemens;	and if the wound is long, and not cured by this cure, then you should know that the decay has begun, and it makes an impression in the bone, or in hard members, or in limbs.
si le cure de la cure de fistule, si com nos avons dit ci devant.	If the treatment of the fistula cure is as we have said before.
de l’aposteme de l’ungle	The first sentence to translate is: "Car en l’ovraige de cest chapistre avient
Panarice est un aposteme que naist desoz l’ungle dou pouchiet de la main, ou dou piet, ou par aventure naist en autres dois;	Panacea is an aphrodisiac that often cures the thumb of the hand, or finger, or by chance in other parts;
et quant il est envielliez, et on n’i prent garde, si i vient I aposteme chaus, et corront et giete bowe tant qu’elle corront la racine de l’ungle, et par aventure la corront toute;	And when it is infected, and it is not guarded, if the aphrodisiac comes out, and runs and soaks the wound as far as the root of the finger, and by chance it runs all over;
et vient li corrosions jusc’a l’os, tant qu’il i vient dolor puant, et est li chiés dou doi larges, et est li color fuxe.	And there comes the corrosion to the bone, as far as it comes with pain, and the head of the joint is wide, and the color is changed;
Quant tu le cures si com nos avons dit en la division, et li cure ne profite mie, si covient que tu copes a i. fer toute la superfluiteit qui est demoree de l’ungle, puis cauterize la plaie aprés.	When you treat it as we have said in the division, and the cure does not benefit, then you must cut off all the excess that is growing from the finger, then cauterize the wound afterwards.
Li cauteres est mout grans aide se li os est sains, et li ungle est sainne;	The fire cautery is a great help when the bone is healthy, and the nail is healthy.
et se li ungle apresse la char ens, et l’encomence a poindre, et la blece, si covient que tu mettes lou rait desoz l’ungle que point la char, et la boute en haut, et cope celi char subtilment et legierement, et met sus le remenant de la char medicines ardans et corrosives por oster tout;	And if the nail presses on the bone, and begins to prick, and darkens, then you should remove the part of the nail that points at the bone, and cut it off high up, and cope with the remaining part of the nail subtly and gently, and put on the remnant of the nail with medicines that are hot and corrosive to heal everything.
puis le cure d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then the treatment of wounds as long as they are healthy.
Et se li corrosion est en l’os, si le cope, et trai fuer, car tant com li os corrumpus i est, si ne puet saner;	And if corrosion is in the bone, and it is coped, and taken out, because as much as the bone corrupts and is, so it cannot be healed.
et se tu vois le doi corrumpre, si le cope en I des nous si com il est devant dit, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez;	If you see the second bone corroded, if the copes in I are as described, then treat it as soon as it is healthy.
et s’il est ferus, et boutez, et il sent grant dolor, si covient que tu le sainnes premier;	And if it is frozen, and cut it off, and it feels great pain, then it is necessary to first cleanse it.
puis cope l’ungle dou spatumile agut en taillant de travers desus, et warde que li taille ne viegne jusc’a la char qui est desoz l’ungle, car li malaides sentiroit trop grant dolor;	Then cut the nail of the frozen toe with a sharp knife, and make sure the cut does not go through the skin, because the patient will feel too much pain.
et s’il avient, si met chose sus qui apaise.	And if it happens, then put something on that soothes.
la dolor dou sourdoit de la main	The pain of the elbow
Li dois ajostez qui naist en mains d’aucuns homes par aventure est toz charnus, et par aventure i a teil ou il a osses, et aucune fois i a ungle, et aucun d’aus naissent en la racine de la jointure, ou li naissance est en aucuns nous des dois.	The elbow dislocation that occurs in the hands of some men by chance is very common, and it often happens without causing any damage, and never causes a fracture, and no one is born with this deformity, or the birth is not in any of us from the two.
Cil qui naist en aucune nout dou doi ne se muet, et cil qui naist a la jointure dou doi, par aventure se muet;	Those who do not move at all in any joint, and those who are moved at the frozen joint, by chance stay still.
la taille de celui qui est charnus si est legiere, en teil maniere:	The size of one who is lame is as follows:
taille le en sa racine d’un large spatumile.	The size of one who is lame is as the root of a wide spatule.
Cil qui naist en la racine de la jointure si est grief a curer:	He who has pain in the root of the joint is difficult to cure:
si te tien dou coper.	If you hold tight to the pain.
En celui qui naist ou doit au derrien nout, si covient que tu copes premier la char reondement jusc’a l’os, puis cope l’os a une soie convenable a ceu, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	In the event of a fracture that needs to be treated from the back, if you are able to first cover the bone with a suitable cloth, then cover the bone with a bandage, and then treat it until it is healthy.
Li soudemens que vient as dois ensamble vient par naissance, ou par soudement de plaie, ou par arsure de feu, ou par semblans choses.	The symptoms that come are those that come from birth, or from wounds, or from burns, or from other things.
Si couvient que tu copes celle soudeure, si que li doit repairent selonc lor formes naturelz;	If you cover that spot with your hand, then it should repair according to its natural forms:
puis met entre dous tentes ou drapelz moilliez en oile roset, qu’il ne se soudent;	Then put between two cloths or flannels made wet with rose oil, so they do not stick:
ou tu met entre dous pieces de plonc subtilz, tant que li leus soit soudez, si com il covient.	Or you put between two pieces of soft cloth, as long as it does not stick, if it comes out:
Se soudemens vient a aucun de ses dois avec la paume, si cope celle sodure si com il covient.	When the patient touches either of his two hands with his thumb, if it is not too painful, then it should be done.
des vils	of wounds
Vis sont voinnes grosses envoloupees pleines de superfluitez melancoliouses, que vienent em plusors membres dou cors;	Giant veins filled with excess melancholic fullness come from more and more limbs of the heavy body.
et plus avient en jambes de ces qui vont a piet et qui travaillent et portent, que a autres.	And more come in the legs of those who go to church and work and carry, than in others.
Il covient donques que tu li aministres aucune fois espurgement de cole, et puis le saine de la basilique.	Therefore, it is necessary that you never administer any purging of colic, and then the proper dosage of the basilicon.
Li cure de fer si est selonc II manieres:	The iron cure is followed in two ways:
l’une est c’on les cope, et traie on fuer le sanc noir;	One is to cut and draw the black blood;
et li autre maniere si est que tu lieves la voinne, et la trai toute fuer.	And the other way is if you love the vein, and cut it all through.
Li taille si est selonc ceste maniere:	The size is followed in this way:
arose li premier la jambe d’aigue chaude mout fort, tant que li gros sans soit subtiliiez, puis estrain la jambe dou malaide des desus la cuixe jusc’a la partie desoz le genoil;	First, the first leg of the hot, strong ankle is raised until it is not subtle, then the knee of the patient is strained to the part below the knee of the groin.
puis cope la voinne en I leu, ou en II ou en III, d’une taille large, puis eslieve et trair fuer le sanc noir a ta main, des l’un chief jusc’a l’autre, tant que tant de sans en isse com li vertus dou malaide puet soffrir;	Then close the vein with your hand, either with one, two, or three fingers, of a large size, then lift and take out the dark blood from your hand, from one end to the other, as much as you can, as much as the patient's strength allows.
et puis la lie, et li comande qu’il se teigne de viandes enjanrant cole noire;	Then tie it off and command that it be painted with black meat juice.
et recomence l’evacuation et la sainie quant les voinnes sont plainnes, et nuist au malaide.	And continue the evacuation and cleaning as the veins become clear, and inform the patient.
Li alevemens de li est selonc ceste maniere:	The lesions of the dislocated joint are caused in this manner:
reis la jambe dou malaide, s’il i a mout de poil, puis le met ou bain, et li arose la jambe d’aigue chaude tant qu’elle deviegne rouge, et enflent les voinnes;	Straighten the patient's leg, if it has hair, then wash it with warm water, and make the leg red hot until it turns red, and dilate the veins.
et se tu n’as point de baing, si le chaufe au feu, et puis le cope endroit la voinne dou lonc au chief dou genoil, ou en la partie desoz a la cheville;	And if you do not have a fire, if the cauterization is done with heat, and then the point is placed where the vein is long and thin at the head of the thigh, or in the part below the ankle.
puis aoevre le cuir a l’oncine, et escorche la voinne de chescune part, tant qu’ele apere quant on la sent;	Then apply the leather to the wound, and scarify the vein in every part, as soon as it appears when touched.
et on la voit rouge et noire, et quant elle entre ou cuir si semble ausi com une corde blainche;	And it is seen red and black, and when it enters or the leather seems as if it were a bluish cord;
puis boute le rait desoz, tant qu’ele soit alevee dou cuir, et puis la pent a l’oncine legier, puis le cope en I autre leu ensus III dois;	Then bind the wound tightly, as soon as it is healed with leather, and then cut at the ankle lightly, then the thread is passed through the other leg, three times.
puis escorche le cuir sus la voinne tant qu’ele apere, puis la lieve au rais, si com tu as fait, et la pent a un autre uncine, si com tu as fait premiers;	Then scorch the skin on the vein as much as it appears, then soften it with oil, just as you have done, and it can be used for another incision, just as you have done first.
puis cope une autre taille, ou plusors se tu en as mestier, puis la lieve, et la cope au doi dou piet, puis la trai et lieve jusc’a la seconde taille;	Then cut a larger size, or more like it, then soften it, and then lay it flat, and then tie it to the second size.
puis l’estrai de taille en taille, tant qu’elle isse toute fuer, puis la cope;	Then extract the limb in the size, as far as it will go, then soften it.
et se tu ne la pues traire et lever, si i boute une aguille a tout I fil fort double, et la lie et la trai, et i boute desoz I rait, et torne ta main d’une part et d’autre, tant qu’il en isse;	And if you do not manage to lift it and straighten it, if it does not come out with a needle as strong as double thread, then soften it, tie it, and pull it out, and cut your hand from both sides, until it comes out.
et garde qu’elle ne cope, car s’elle cope, si ne la puet on traire ne lever, et en vient nuisement au malaide;	and make sure it does not break, for if it breaks, and cannot be treated or lifted, it causes harm to the patient.
et quant tu l’as toute traite, si met sor le leu de la plaie laine moillie en vin et en oile roset;	and when you have fully treated it, place the wound of the hairy skin with fine linen soaked in wine and rose oil.
et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	and keep it until it is healthy.
Et se li vis est contraite et torte et envoloupee ensamble, et ele n’est mie droite, si com nos avons dit, si covient que tu la fendes tortement, mais ne la coper mie;	And if the wound is contracted and twisted and enveloped together, and it is not straight as we have said, but if you cut it off violently, do not cut it off, but if it is not straight.
et la trai si com nos avons devant dit.	and the skin is stretched as we have said before.
Li forme dou fer dont on cope la vis si est corbes, et ne trenche mie, qu’il ne cope la voinne;	The form of iron used when cutting the eye if it is hard, and does not cut through, is that it does not cut through the vein.
et est de grosse corbeure, car s’il estoit subtilz, si coperoit la voine, mais soit gros si com nos avons dit, et ci est li forme:	and is a thick nail, because if it were fine, it would cut through the vein, but since it is thick as we have said, and this is the form:
de la voinne civile	of the common vein
Ceste voinne est enjanree en jambes, en chaudes parties ou il ne naist herbes ne arbre, et en terre ou il n’a point de moistor;	This vein is joined in the legs, in hot parts or where there are no herbs or trees, and in the earth where there is no moisture.
et par aventure naist autre part qu’en jambes, et ceu avient de la porriture que vient desoz le cuir, si com il vient dedens le cors serpens et vers, enjanrez entre cuir et char.	and by chance grows in another part than in the legs, and this comes from the fat that comes out of the skin, as it does from the tail of a snake and towards, joined between the skin and the arm.
Et se li signes de l’encomencement de ceste voinne si est qu’il vient en la jambe une tres grans enflammation, puis se chainge li leus, et comence li voinne fors issir, ausi com une racine d’une plante.	And if the signs of the beginning of this vein are that there is a very large inflammation in the leg, then it changes color, and begins to bleed, as if from the root of a plant.
Quant li chiés apert, si covient que tu envoloupes entor une piece de plonc des une З et demi jusc’a II З., et la noe, et laisse le plonc pendant a la jambe, et totes les fois qu’il en ist point au defuer, si l’envoloupe entor le plonc, et la nowe;	When the head is opened, if you cover one end of a piece of lint with one and a half fingers, and hold it there, and leave the lint on the leg, and every time it is not closed, if the lint covers the end of the lint, and the now;
et s’elle est trop longe, si en cope une partie, et envoloupe le remenant, et ne la coper mie en sa racine, tant qu’elle soit toute issue;	and if it is too long, if you cut off a part, and cover the remaining part with lint, and do not cover the root as much as it is all out;
car se tu la copes, si rentre en la char, et fait venir aposteme et porriture ou leu, et male maladie;	for if you cut it off, it will enter the body, and bring forth pus and blood, or the limb, and serious illness;
por la queil chose il covient qu’elle soit traite poc et poc jusc’a chief, et n’en remaigne rien ou cors;	For this particular thing, it is necessary that it be treated as soon as possible and quickly, and nothing else or more remains.
et est aucune fois ceste voinne quant elle est traite de V paumes de lonc, ou de X, et uns hons vint ja a moi, a cui elle issit de X paumes de long, et quant tu la copes, si boute I rais ou pertus, et la perce jusc’a fons, si que tout en isse;	And there is no time for this vein when it is treated with V hands of length, or X, and some came to me before, which was X hands of length, and when you press, if it hurts or punctures, and the hole is small, then all is well.
et soit vuidie li matiere qui est dedens, et amenistre au leu medicines enjanrans porriture aucun jor, puis le cure si com les apostemes.	And let the matter be digested, and administer the medicine to the patient without any food for one hour, then the cure is like that of the abscesses.
Et aucune fois a ceste voinne mains rains, et meismement quant elle apert en la jointure dou piet, ou ou piet, et i vient mout de pertus, et dont il saut rains;	And there is no time for this vein hands to be closed, and at the same time when it opens in the joint of the shoulder or the shoulder, and if there is pain, and it jumps out of its place;
cure le donques si com nos avons dit devant.	If you have followed our advice before, then you will know how to treat it.
des vers qui naissent entre cuir et char	Of those that are born between leather and horsehair.
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «maladie de buef», por ceu qu’elle avient maintes fois as bués, et est un petis vers qui naist entre cuir et char, et va par tout le cors montant et dessendant, et le sent om bien a l’aler de membre en membre, tant qu’il desront le cuir ou il vait, et saut fuer;	This disease is known in our country as "beef disease," because it often occurs with many wounds, and is a sharp pain that travels from the skin to the bone, and goes up and down the entire body, and is felt throughout the limbs, until it reaches the skin or bone, and then it jumps.
et est enjanrez de porriture d’aucunes humors, si com vienent vers et serpens et lumbris et ascarides ou ventre;	and is caused by an excess of certain humors, such as worms that come and go in the belly, and snakes and limbs and Ascaris.
et doute on de son malice, car quant il va par le cors, et il monte au chief, et il vient a l’oil, par aventure rentre, et destruit l’oil;	and one wonders about its maliciousness, because when it goes through the body, it rises to the head, and comes to the brain, by chance it enters, and destroys the brain.
et ceu avient maintes fois.	And this often happens.
Quant tu le vues curer et traire, si ne puet on fuers que quant il vait:	When you see it being cured and treated, if not, when it will be.
si covient donques que tu lies le leu desus et desoz d’un fort liien bien estroitement, puis cope sus et le trai fuer, et se li vers est em parfont en la char, et tu ne le trueves, si le cauterize de feu sus, tant qu’il muire;	If it comes to pass that you read the lever of the shoulder and below a strong ligament well tightened, then pull on it and cut it off, and it will be firmly fixed in place, and you will not need to sew it, if the cauterization by fire is done as follows:
et li plus grans nuisemens que il fait, si est qu’il corront l’oil, si com nos avons dit;	and the greatest harm it can cause, if it goes to the oil, as we have said.
et se tu le vois venir ou chief pres de l’oil, si estraint desoz lui le sorcil forment, puis cope sus, et le trai fuer;	And if you see it coming towards or near the oil, hold it firmly by the horn, and cut off the cauterization; then pull it out.
et covient user le malaide de mundifiement de cors de medicines solutives por les males humors porries, et se warse de viandes enjanrans porriture.	1. It is necessary to use the cautery of the maltreats to dissolve the solutions of drugs for the humors, and to avoid foods that are not pure for nourishment.
de la dolor qui vient de ventositeit	From the pain that comes from dislocation
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «vakirir», et est une dolor que vient en aucuns membres, et pues se mue de membre en membre;	2. This disease is called "wakir" in our land, and it is a pain that comes to any part of the body, and spreads from one part to another.
et je vis ceu que je vos di.	3. And I see what you say.
Je fui apelez a une femme malaide, et me descovrit som bras, et vis une petite enfleure en la voinne dou brais;	4. I was called to a woman who had been treated with a cautery, and I saw my arm, and saw a small pimple in the vein of the arm.
et I poc aprés, li vis monter ausi com un ver a l’espaule, plus tost que nulle chose, ausi com vif argent quant il cort de leu a autre;	5. And later, I saw it rise as if it were a snake in the shoulder, more quickly than anything else, as if it were living silver when it cuts through the flesh.
li dolor se departit de celui leu, et se ficha en l’espaule, et puis un poc aprés corrut par tout le cors, tant qu’ele vint en l’autre brais;	The pain leaves that limb, and it tightens in the shoulder, and then a while later spreads throughout the body, so much so that it comes to the other shoulder.
puis me contait qu’elle tornioit adés entor le cors, si com je la vis.	Then it tells me that it dislocated itself further towards the front of the body, just as I see.
Je me mervillai mout coment elle se movoit ensi de membre em membre, car je n’avoie onques veut ceste maladie selonc ceste maniere.	I marvel at how it moves from limb to limb, as I have never wished for this disease in this manner.
Toutevoie, je avoie veut maint que bien avoient veut movoir dolor de leu a autre, mais je ne l’avoie mie veut, si com je le vis en la femme;	Indeed, I wanted to ensure that the pain moved from one part of the body to another, but I could not make it happen, just as I see in the woman.
et je me pensai que c’estoit por ceu que li femme avoit sec cors, et les voinnes descovertes, et por ceu apparoit celle ventositez constrainte;	I thought it was because the woman had a stiff chest, and the veins were exposed, and because that constriction appeared.
et n’aperent mie selonc ceste raison a ces qui sont delicious, et qui ont moistes cors et voinnes reponues.	And it is not apparent to those who do not understand this reason that those who are delicate have moist skin and veins that have been replenished.
Et quant tu vues curer ceste maladie, et li malaides sent celle dolor, s’elle t’apert si com nos avons dit, si la lie desus et desoz hastanment, et puis cope sus tant que cele ventositez constrainte au leu isse fuer;	And when you see this disease being cured, and the patient feels pain, if it opens as we have said, if the limb is not held tightly, and then released as much as the constraint allows to the limb;
et cauterize le leu;	and cauterize the limb;
et se tu ne la vois a tes eulz, si le cure de ceu qui deboute les ventositez, si com pilules fetides, et pilules de serapin, et semblans autres.	And if you do not see it with your eyes, whether the cure of this that relieves the constraint is like pills made from the dried flesh of fish and other similar things;
des saiettes	arrows
Les saiettes sont diverses, selonc lor semblances et selonc les leus dou cors ou elles chient.	Arrows are various, according to their appearances and according to the bones of the hand or they pierce.
Li diversitez de lor si est qu’il i a de celles qui ont grans pointes, et petites, et chevees, et soudees;	The variety of their wounds is that some have large points, and small, and hairs, and sores.
et de celles qui ont II angles, et de celz qui ont lengues, et de celles ou il a pieces;	and of those with angles, and of those with tongues, and of those where there are pieces.
et celle qui chiet en aucun membre si chiet selonc II manieres:	and the one who does not find in any limb according to any way.
ou en membre principeil cheveit, si com cerveil, cuer, foie, pormon, rains, intestine, vessie, et semblans membres.	or in the principle member, if it is like the brain, liver, spleen, lung, heart, intestine, uterus, and other members.
Quant elle chiet donques en aucun leu de ces membres, et li signe de mort, que je te dirai ci aprés, t’aperent:	When she finds that she does not find in any limb of these members, and the sign of death that I will tell you later appears.
si covient que tu te warses de l’estraction de ceste saiette, car li mors vient aprés en plusors dispositions;	If it comes to your mind that you should remove this arrow, because of the death that follows in many cases.
et quant cist mal signe ne t’aperent mie, et li saiette n’est mie em parfont, si la trai, et cure la plaie.	And when you notice that it is not a lie, and the arrow is not in front, then remove it, and treat the wound.
Et li signe dou cerveil quant li saiette i chiet et perce l’os, et saut li syfac fuer qui est sus le cerveil, est quant scotomie et sode et esvertin et roujor ens eulz, et enflammation et roujor de lengue, et spasme et permixtion d’entendement, et vomissemens de cole;	And the sign of a fracture when the arrow pierces the bone, and the shock that is felt there is when there is scotomy and soreness and shivering and pain in the limbs, and inflammation and pain in the tongue, and spasm and mixture of understanding, and vomiting of cold;
et per aventure ist sans fuer des narines, ou des oreilles;	and by chance it is without eyes or ears.
et par aventure pert la parole et la voix;	And by chance, the word and the voice;
et saut de la plaie moistor blanche semblant a poulz, et en saut ausi com bruee de char;	and a leap of the white, moist wound, resembling a roar of a bull.
et se cist signe t’aperent, si te tien de la cure, et trai la saiette s’elle n’est ens.	and this is the sign you see, if you hold the cure, and draw the arrow if it is not in.
Li signe de la siette quant elle chiet ou cuer, sont qu’elle est pres de la mamele senestre, et sent ausi com s’elle estoit fichie en chose dure, ne mie vuide;	The sign of the arrow when it is drawn or pulled is that it is near the left shoulder, and it feels as if it is stuck in something hard, not empty.
et par aventure li siette se muet ausi com li poulz, et en cort noir sanc, et vient froidor et suor froide, et sincope:	And by chance, the arrow is also silent, and in black blood, and comes with cold and very cold, and sinks.
saiches adonc sens doute ke li mors dessent.	The patient does not doubt that the death has set in.
Et li signe de la saiette que nevre lou pormon est que sans plains d’escume saut de la plaie, et li gorge enfle, et li malaides mue color, et sospire haut et quiert le froit ar.	And the sign of the arrowhead that does not come out is that there are no plains of ecchymosis, a sudden drop in the wound, the throat swells, and the face turns pale, and he sighs high and cries out in pain.
Et se li saiette chiet en la coverture dou pis, si est delez les petites costes;	And if the arrowhead is found in the covering of the chest, it is difficult to find the small ribs.
et giete grant alainne et grant dolor et sospire;	and there is great pain and suffering.
et li muevent tuit li membre des espaules.	and they move all the limbs of the shoulder.
Et se li saiette chiet ou stomac, par aventure si saut de la plaie aucune chose de la viande indigeste.	2. If the arrowhead is found in the stomach by chance, if it jumps from the wound nothing of the undigested meat.
Et se li saiette chiet ou ventre, et en saut point de fien par l’intestine rout, si n’a point d’esperance en la cure, ne en l’estraction de la saiette.	3. If the arrowhead is found in the stomach and in a sudden jump through the intestine, if there is no hope in the cure, nor in the extraction of the arrow.
Et se li saiette chiet en la vessie, et li urine en saut et vient defuer, et li malaides sent fort dolor:	And if the arrowhead is found in the bladder, and the urine comes out suddenly and forcefully, and the patient feels great pain.
saiches que li plaie est mortelz.	The patient suspects that the wound is fatal.
Li autre membre, si com li faice et li colz et li gorge et li espaule et li adjutoire et li espinee dou dos et li forcele et li cuixe et les jambes, et li membre semblant, sont sauf selonc plusors dispositions.	The other member, if the face and chest and shoulder and arm and spine and back and shoulders, and the limbs seeming, are saved according to other dispositions.
Quant li saiette est en lou nerf ou l’artere, et elle n’est venimouse, si com je vos dirai qu’il m’avint, por ceu que vos faciez autretel.	When the artery is in the loins or the limb, and it is not visible, as I will tell you if I remember, because you are doing it.
Il avint a I home c’une saiette li chut ou larmier en la racine dou neis:	It came to my home one day, a arrowhead that was thrown into the root of the neck.
je la tentai, et la traï d’autre part desoz la graisse de l’oreille, et fut sanez sens nusement.	I tried to touch it, and from the other side, I removed the grease from the ear, and it was painful.
Et traï a un jeu une saiette que li chut en la graisse de l’oil desoz la papiere desoz, et li saiette estoit reponue, et n’en poi ataindre que la pointe devers lou fust, et estoit li saiette grans d’un arc turcois, a tout I fer legier sens oreilles;	And I found a bone that was stuck in the grease of the oil of the paper, and it was firmly fixed, and it could not be removed except for the tip towards the other side, and it was as large as a Turkish archer's arrow, making it easy to remove with light blows on the ears.
li jeus fut sanez, et ne li vint nulz mavais accidens.	I managed to remove it, and I never had any accidents.
Et traï une saiette de la gorge a un crestien, et estoit li saiette arabique a oreilles:	And I found a bone from the throat in a cheese, and it was the Arabic bone with ears.
je soiai les barbions, et subtiliai tant que je la traï, et fut sanez li crestiens.	I was aware of the barbs, and they were very subtle as I touched them, and they were healthy crests.
Et traï une saiette a I home, que li estoit cheue ou ventre, et pensai qu’il moroit;	I touched a thorn in my foot, which was long or flat, and I thought it would kill me.
et puis qu’il ot passez XXX jors, si ne mua point sa disposition;	and then if it had not changed its position after XXX days.
je taillai sus la saiette, et l’engignai, et la traï fuer, et n’ot point de mavais accident.	I removed the thorn, I applied pressure, and it stopped bleeding, and there were no other accidents.
Et si vis I home cui une saiette chut ou dos, et fut li plaie soudee sus;	And if your foot or leg has a wound from a thorn, and the wound is deep or large, and it does not heal quickly.
et demora li saiette dedens li, et ne chainja point ses dispositions naturez, ne ne trova nuisement en aucune de ses oevres naturelz.	and the thorn did not leave the wound, and it did not change its natural position, and it was not found in any of its natural works.

et mout d’autres semblans.	and did not have other similarities.
Et traï une saiette a I home des princes le roi, que li estoit cheue enmi lou neiz, et estoit un poc declinans a la destre partie;	And shot an arrow at the king's son, who was swollen in the middle and was slightly bent to the left.
et estoit li saiette toute reponue.	and the arrow was completely embedded.

Si trovai la plaie mult estroite.	If the wound was very tight.

et il sentoit pointure et dolor desoz sa destre oreille.	and he felt a sharp and painful sensation in his left ear.
Je pensai que c’estoit de la pointe de la saiette Je mis sus lou leu emplaustre atratifet digestif, por ceu que li leus n’enflast;	I thought that it was the tip of the arrow I put the sharp, dry, and easily cuttable bone in the wound, because the arrow did not burn.
et m’aparut li leus de la saiette.	and I saw that it was the arrow.
Je i mis l’emplaustre mains jors, et resouda li plaie derechief, et demora ensi li malaides lonc tens, tant qu’il sentit la saiette I jor dedens son neis;	I inserted the sharp bone into the wound, and the right side of the skin was cut, and it took a long time for the pain to subside, until the patient felt the bone leave his body.
et il le me dist.	and he told me.
Je mis sus la plaie medicine ague corrosive par mains jors, tant qu’elle fut overte, et la tentai, et sentis le chief de la saiette qui s’aerdoit au leu;	I applied the medicated plaster to the wound, as thick as possible, and it stuck, and I felt the point of the arrow that was stuck in the skin.
puis ajostai en l’overture de la plaie par celle medicine ague, tant que li chiés de la saiette m’aparut visablement;	Then, in the opening of the wound, by the use of that medicinal herb, until the head of the arrow appeared visible.
et trespassa bien li termines entor IIII mois, et puis eslarja si li plaie que je i boutai les tenailles, et le meus d’une part et d’autre, et ne pot issir;	And it took well over four months to heal, and then the wound was lanced, and I removed all the needles, both sides, and could not stop.
adonques ne cessai de subtiliier et d’engignier de manieres d’estrumens, tant que je la pris I jor as tenailles bien faites, selonc ceu que sa forme venra en la fin de cest chapistre, tant que je la traï, et restourai la plaie. taille donques sus, tant que les tenailles i puissent prendre, et puis l’estrai:	The head is then cut open, as soon as the nails can take hold, and then it is pulled out.
si saut fuer maintenant.	If you jump now.
