Et li maniere de la sainie si est que li malaides boute sa main en aigue chaude, tant que li foscile soit rouges;	And the way to clean it if the patient boils their hand in hot water until the redness subsides.
puis soit liiéz moienement, si que li voinne apere bien, puis le saine maintenant dou travers, ne mie dou large ne dou lonc;	Then it is linked in a proper manner, if the vein appears well, then the proper way now through, no large or long wound.
et soit li pertus larges, et soit sainiez bien pres de la jointe de la main, et se sans n’en puet issir, si remet la main en aigue chaude, et laisse corre lou sanc en l’aigue, tant que tu en aies assez;	And the wound is large, and is healing well near the joint of the hand, and if it cannot be removed, then place the hand in warm water, and let the blood flow through it until you have enough.
et se c’est en esteit, si ne rebouter mie la main en aigue chaude, car on l’i met plus en yver que en esteit;	And if this is not possible, then place the hand in warm water, as it will be more in the pit than here.
et li sainie de ceste voine est plus sauve de toutes autres voinnes, qu’il n’i a ne artere ne nerf.	The healing of this vein is more safe from all other veins, than if it has not been cut or nerved.
Li sainie de la salvatele de la main destre si vaut a toutes les maladies dou foie, et c’est li maniere:	The health of the saved hand is worth all the diseases of the left hand, and this is the way:
estrain la main, et boute en aigue chaude, tant que li voinne soit enflee, si c’on la voie;	Strain the hand, and pour hot water on it until the vein is cold, if you can;
et se la saine de travers, et se tu la copes dou tout en tout, si ne grieve rien;	and if you can pass your hand through it, and if it does not hurt at all, then there is no harm.
et n’aler mie trop em parfont, car li nerf sont desoz toz desnuez de char, et puis remet la main en aigue chaude, se li sans est congelez en la plaie, et n’en puet issir.	and do not force it too far, because the bones are dry and lacking in cartilage, and then put your hand in hot water, if it does not freeze in the wound, and cannot be removed.
Et quant tu avras trait dou sanc tant com mestier t’est, si met sus la voinne oile et seil por souder hastanment, et ensi fai de chescun rain.	And when you have treated as much blood as is customary for your skill, if you put the vein oil and seal it tightly, and then make a thread for each rain.
Li sainie de li en la main senestre si vaut a la maladie de la mice, et fai tout ausi com je t’ai dit devers destre.	The patient with the injury in the left hand if it is of the mouse disease, and I do everything as I have said towards the right.
Li sainie de la sophene si vaut a toutes les maladies que sont desoz le cors, si com maladies de la marris, et retenement de flors, et maladie des rains, et des cuixes et des jambes ancienes, et semblans maladies.	The health of the sore if it is of all diseases that are not good for the heart, like diseases of the lungs, and retention of flowers, and disease of the arms, and legs, and old wounds, and similar diseases.
Et li qualitez de sa sainie si est que li malaides boute som piet en aigue chaude, et frote sus la voinne tant qu’elle pere, et lie desus la jointure dou piet;	And the quality of its healing if it is that the patient can pass his hand in hot water and fry the vein as it bleeds, and then loosen the joint without pain.
et li voinne si est a la cheville, et par desus lou piet en vont mout de rains;	When the vein is at the ankle, and by the doctor's order, it should not be pricked with a needle.
saine la donques ou plus large rain, ou a la cheville, que mues vaut.	If the vein is small or large, or at the ankle, it is worth mentioning.
Et se tu la saines sus lou piet, si te warde des ners qui sont desoz, et la saine de traver ausi com en copant;	And if you follow your doctor's order, if there are nerves that are not in place, and the vein is traversed as it should be.
et soit li flaimes anesil.	And the blood flow is normal.
Et se li sans n’en puet issir, si remet lou piet en l’aigue, et laisse bien vuidier la voine.	And if you cannot cleanse it with soap, then put your hand in the fire and let the vein dry out well.
Et se li sainieres faut la premiere fois, si rencomence la seconde au desus un poc, car li leus est salz;	And if the patient improves the first time, if the second time it does not last more than a short time because the disease is salt.
ne ne douter de nerf, si com nos avons dit, et ensi fai de la sophene de l’autre piet igalment.	Do not doubt the nerves, as we have said, and now I will make a salve of the other doctor in the same way.
Li leus de la voinne sciatique est a la cheville de fuer, et sa sainie vaut a la dolor de la hainche, quant c’est por sanc chaut.	The salve for the sciatica wound is at the ankle of the foot, and its effectiveness is equal to the pain of the thigh, when it is full of pus.
Et li qualitez de sa sainie si est que li malaides entre ou bain, et estraigne desus la cheville IIII dois en tordant, car autrement n’apert li voinne;	And the quality of his health if he has been or bathed, and draws out from his ankle four times in twisting, because otherwise the vein will not open.
et s’elle apert, si le saine en toutes les manieres que tu pues, et en traversant;	And if it opens, then the healthy person in all ways that you can think of, and across.
et vaut mues que tu la copes, car li leus est saus, et elle est mout reponue a mains homes.	And it is worth copying, for the text is read and it is returned to male hands.
Et se tu ne la trueves, si saine aucun rain de li qui apert ou dos dou piet, et vers lou petit doi, et te warde des ners;	And if you do not copy, then no healthy person of the one who opened or at the back of the door, and towards the little door, and it will be granted to you.
et fai tant corre dou sanc que tu vues, et puis deslie lou lien, et met sus coton et l’estraint;	And make so many incisions of blood that you see, and then the link is cut off, and it is tied with thread and it is tightened.
ele est maintenant sanee.	The patient is now healthy.
des sainies de ventouse	Of wounds from ventouse
Ventouses sont fait de cornes, ou d’arain, ou de voirre;	Vacuum pumps are made of horn, or iron, or glass.
et ventosation si est faite selonc II manieres:	and vacuum is created in two ways:
ou par ferir et atraire sanc, ou sens ferir.	either by cutting and drawing blood, or by cutting.
Et ceste ventosation qui est sens ferir si est selonc II manieres:	And this vacuum creation, which is made by cutting, is done in two ways:
ou elle est a tout feu, ou sens feu;	either it is entirely on fire, or on fire.
et ventosation qui est faite par ferir et par estraction de sanc si est faite en XIIII leus dou cors, de coi li uns est tout en som le chief;	and the vacuum creation that is made by cutting and extracting blood is made in twelve hours, with all the wounds being completely closed.
et li autres est emmi le col;	and the other is left open.
et II autres en II costeis dou col;	and two more in the other cheek;
et li ventouse desoz lou menton;	and the suction of the mouth;
et li ventouse des II espaules;	and the suction of the other two shoulder blades;
et li ventouse sus les crupies;	and the suction of the groin;
et les ventouses emmi les II bras;	and the suctions of the inner arms;
et les ventouses des II jambes;	and the suctions of the legs;
et les ventouses des II chevilles;	and the suctions of the ankles;
et li ventosation ne trait point de sanc, fuer que des menues voinnes que sont esparses en la char, et por ceu n’en afoiblist om mie, si com on fait de sainie de voinne;	and the suction does not treat any blood, rather it is for thin veins that are scattered in the body, and therefore it does not cause any harm, as we do with wounds;
et ne covient mie qu’elle soit aministree, ne a tout feu ne sens feu, en aucune maladie qui vient de repletion, tant que toz li cors soit vuidiez.	and it is only necessary that it be moistened, and not with any fire or heat, in no disease that comes from overeating, as long as the chest is dry.
Et se par necessiteit de maladies covient ventoser, ou por acostumances, si l’amenistrons chescune houre en l’encomencement dou mois, ou en la fin, et emmi et en chescun tens;	And if necessity comes from diseases, or for habits, if the midwife comes every hour at the beginning of the month, or at its end, and also in each ten;
car il i a de telz qui, quant il ont mestier de ventoser, si ont pesant chief;	For there are those who, when they have to assist at childbirth, have heavy burdens.
et si a telz qui truevent repletion et roujor en lor faice, et en lor chief, et au col, et tenebrour as eulz;	And if there are those who, when they become swollen and bleeding in their face, in their cheeks, and at the navel, and in the belly, have heavy burdens.
et telz qui truevent une goute de sanc en lor bouche, et ont enflee la lengue, et raichent sanc;	And those who have a thirst for blood in their mouth, and have lost their tongue, and spit out blood.
et si i a de telz qui songent, et voient par nut sanc et navrez et mors et semblans choses.	If they have such things as wounds that prick, and see blood and death and similar things.
Et quant nos voions ces signes, et meismement quant c’est emmi lou mois, nos lou commandons a ventoser aprés III houres dou jor.	When we see these signs, and at the same time when it is three hours after midnight, we command our patient to fast.
Li sainie de la muze si aide a la grieteit dou chief … que vient as eulz, et ne covient mie que ce soit aprés l’evacuation de tout lou cors;	The health of the liver helps in the treatment of long hair… that comes as it is, and it is only necessary after the evacuation of all the blood.
et ceste ventosation si est en leu de la sainie de la cephalique, et ne covient mie que cil qui est de froide complexion en use, ou qui ait chatharre, car ce lor fait mout grant nuisement;	And this ventilation is in the head of the liver health, and it is only necessary for those who have a cold complexion or who have been struck, because this does great harm.
et por ceu ne covient mie que li veillart en usent, ne qui ont ou chief froides maladies.	And that's why it is only necessary for the watchmen to use those who have or not cold diseases.
Et cil qui s’en saine sovent, si devient oblious, et por ce covient mettre la ventouse un poc plus aval par la doutance d’obliance.	And those who often get better soon become obligated, and for this reason, the fasting should be made longer due to the fear of non-compliance.
Li ventosation emmi le col est en leu de la sainie dou chief et de la basilique, et por ceu vaut elle a l’estrecement dou pis, et a fendure de la chenal dou pormon, et a toust, et a repletion;	The patient's neck winding is in the chest of the main and the basilica, and for this it is useful in the emergency of the pinch, and for the cutting of the bone of the ear, and to all, and for filling;
et la covient poc bouter, car s’elle tient trop fermement, si enjanre obliance ou stomac et ou cuer.	and it is meant to be tightened, because it holds too tightly, if it causes indigestion or stomach and or liver;
Li ventosations as II costelz dou col si vaut as dolors dou chief, et obtalmie et emigrainne, et a l’estranglement, et a la dolor as racines des dens, et est en leu de la sainie de la basilique;	The winding of the collar is as the costels of the neck, and it causes pain in the head, and it hurts and pulls, and in the strangulation, and in the pain of the roots of the teeth, and it is in the chest of the main;
et covient que tu comandes au sainor qu’il espresse sa main au mettre, qu’il ne cope l’artere, et ne veigne decorremens de sanc.	And it is necessary that you instruct the patient to express their hand when putting on, so as not to harm the artery and cause further wounds.
Li ventosations desoz lou menton si vaut a maladie de bouche, et a corruption de gencives, et semblans maladies qui sont en la bouche;	The windings of the throat are often due to disease of the mouth, and corruption of the genitals, as well as similar diseases in the mouth.
et est en leu des sainies des II levres.	And it is found in the lips of the cold sweats of the two lips.
Li ventosations des espaules vaut a maladie que vient de chalor et de remplissement.	The second line of the translation is: "Wounds on the shoulders are caused by diseases that come from chill and fullness.
Li ventosations des coutes si vaut autant com des III voinnes dou bras, car elle atrait sanc de ces grosses voinnes;	The windings of the cheeks are as much as three fingers of the arm, because it draws blood from these large veins.
et comande au sainor qu’il ne fiere mie trop em parfont, car li leus est nus de char, et sait desoz ners et arteres.	And instruct the patient not to draw too much blood, because the vein is naked and knows how to avoid nerves and arteries.
Li ventouse qui est sus la croupe si vaut as emoroydes dou fondement, et as maladies desoz, et covient que li ventouse soit grans, et soit d’arain, qu’elle a mestier de bien traire;	The device that is placed on the chest if it is not done with great care can cause injuries and diseases, and it must be large enough to have the ability to well treat.
et par aventure, s’elle estoit subtilz, si briseroit;	and by chance, if it is not done subtly, it may break.
et i fai grans plaies.	and it causes great pain.
Les ventouses des jambes si sainent apertement, car elles atraient sanc de tout le cors, et valent as dolors ancienes des rains, et de la marris, et de la vessie, et ramoinnent les flors;	If the devices on the legs are open, they attract blood from all parts of the body and relieve old pains from the arms, uterus, bladder, and vagina, and draw out the hair.
et sont en leu des II sophenes, et des II chevilles, et toutevoie elles afoiblissent lou cors aprés lonc us, et font venir paumison em plusors dispositions.	and they are on the limbs of the second and third toes, and all of them cause pain in the body after being worn for a long time, and bring about swelling in various positions.
Li maniere de mettre la ventouse si est que tu la mettes premier vuide, et succe tempreement, et la met hastanment, et remue igalment, et ne cesser de ceu faire, tant que tu voies lou leu rouge et enfleit, et apere li roujor dou sanc;	The manner to insert the bougie (cannula) if you put it initially empty, and then subsequently, and move it gently, and do not stop doing this until you see the red and swollen part of the urethra, and the opening of the abscess.
puis fier, et remet les ventouses, et pren warde en la disposition des cors, car il i a telz qui ont tanre char, et clers porez:	Then, close it, and put the bougies back in their original position, as some have such a problem that they cannot manage to hold them.
si covient ferir une fois soulement, et covient faire larges plaies, et un poc parfondes;	If it is necessary to cut once only, and make large incisions, and a smooth surface.
et suce legierement.	and then gently suck.
Et se li sans est gros, si couvient ferir II fois:	And if it is not thin, if it cuts twice:
la premiere fois por subtiliier la voie dou sanc gros.	The first time to subtly open the vein of large blood.
Et se li sans est tres espés, si covient ferir la tierce fois;	And if it is not done quickly, then it can be injured for the third time.
et quant nos volons traire dou sanc poc et poc, si nos soffist soulement une fois.	And when we want to draw out small amounts of blood only once.
Et se nos volons mout de sanc, si rencomensons sovent;	And if we are not afraid to draw blood often.
et se li sans est espés, si fier em parfont, et li termines si est que li keurs soit perciez soudement, et couvient a celui qui a gros cuir et dur, et qui ont estrois porelz, que tu oignes les leus des ventouses d’oile aperitif et dissolutif:	And if it is not done quickly, then it should be stopped if the pain is severe and noticed immediately, and for those who have thick skin and hard hair, and who have long nails, that you oint the ends of the veins with the oily, dissolving ointments of the apothecary:
se c’est en esteit, d’oile violet, ou d’oile d’amandres douces, ou d’oile de semence de cucurbite;	If it is of this nature, from oil of saffron, or sweet almond oil, or oil of the seeds of cucumber.
et se c’est en yveir, d’oile de cresson, ou de lis, ou de camomille, ou autre semblant.	And if it is of this kind, from the oil of lemon, or lavender, or chamomile, or another similar one.
Et se li superfluitez est grosse et froide, si pren oile amaratin, ou de balsamite, ou oile d’anet, et les semblans.	And if the excess is large and cold, then take warm oil, or balsam, or anise oil, and apply them.
Et se cil cui on saine a tendre char et larges porelz, se n’i covient mettre point d’oile, mais le covient laver aprés la ventosation d’aigue rose, ou d’aigue froide, ou d’aigue de morelle, ou d’aigue de cucurbite, ou d’aigue de porcelainne, ou autre semblant.	And if the skin is tender and large pores, it is not recommended to apply oil, but it is recommended to wash after the application of rose water, or cold water, or mushroom water, or onion water, or porcelain water, or any other similar.
Et cil qui a mout de moistor, si se leve d’aisil, ou d’aigue de mirte, et de sumac, et de semblans choses.	And if the one with wet moisture, if it rises from honey, or rose water, and sumac, and similar things.
Et cil qui ont grosses superfluitez se levent de vin viel, ou d’aigue de seuc, ou de decoction d’anet ou de camomile, ou d’autres semblans;	And those who have excessive superfluity rise from wine vinegar, or ague of seuc, or decoction of anet or chamomile, or other similar ones.
et ne se covient mie sainier de ventouse devant le bain ne em bain, mais aprés lou bain une houre ou II;	And it is not necessary to take a cold shower before the bath, but after the bath, an hour or two.
et ne dorme mie aprés la ventosacion, et covient k’il se warse, quant il se doit ventoser et quant il est ventosez.	And do not fall asleep after the ventilation, and it is necessary to wake up when it is time to ventilate and when it is being ventilated.
Et warde se cil qui se saine est coleriques, et se li sans est trop agus et enflamez;	And if the one who is healthy is cold, and the other is too much and inflamed.
si covient qu’il preigne choses froides, si com pomes grenates et endives et laitues a l’aisil, et semblans choses;	If it is necessary to consume cold things, such as lettuce and endive and spinach, and similar things.
et menjuce pucins, et char de chastron, et viandes moistes.	and drink punch, and hot charcoal, and moist meats.
Et cil qui a froide complexion, si preigne syrop de miel, et vin odorant moien, qui est entre viel et noveil, et menjuce poc, et menjuce pucins et petis oiselz et pijons;	And if the one with a cold complexion consumes honey syrup and aromatic wine that is between vinegar and wine, and drinks punch, and drinks punch and small pieces of cheese and pickles.
et lou jor qu’il se ventousera, si doit plus boivre que mengier;	When the joint is dislocated, if it must move more than a little, then it requires more drinking than urine.
et covient doner a aucuns homes aucune fois triaicle ou muscate devant la ventosacion, ou aprés, por conforter les membres principalz;	It is necessary to give some men once a triaicle or muscate before the operation, or afterward, to comfort the main members.
et soit subtiliiez li sans, mais il ne covient mie que cil qui sont chaut le boivent.	And make sure they are quiet without, but only those who are drunk should be made quiet.
Les ventouses que sont mises sens ferir sont celles que sont mises sus lou foie, et sus la mice, et podagre, et sus lou ventre et la boude et les rains et la hainche, car cil membre ne soffrent mie ferir sus oulz, et ne le fait on fuer que por atraire sanc de membre em membre, si com nos mettons sus les mameles quant li neis sainne;	The vents that are made to hurt are those that are made above the liver, and the gallbladder, and rheumatism, and the stomach, and the bowels, and the intestines, because this member does not suffer from external wounds, and only from internal pain when we make it move from one part to another, as we do with the uterus when it is unhealthy.
por oster la viscositeit qui est au membre, si com nos metons ventouses sus le ventre et sus la boude por amenuisier le membre;	For the viscosity that is in the member, if we use suction on the abdomen and the belly to relieve the member.
et oste la dolor, quant il i a opilation ou piere, si oste par sa vertu atractive par aventure l’opilation, ou desaert la piere de son leu;	And ease the pain, when it is inflamed or pierced, if it is attracted by chance to the inflammation, or if it pulls away from its place.
et ensi fait ele quant on le met sus lou foie et sus la mice quant il i a ventositeit retenue, et ces ventouses sont aministrees vuides por sucier tant soulement;	And it is done when it is placed on the liver and the mouse when it has retained inflammation, and these suctions are administered empty by sucking only.
et aucune fois sont aministrees ensamble feu, et aucunes fois plainnes d’aigue tede, si com em maladies dou pleuresin, et en tel maniere c’on emplisse la ventouse d’aigue chaude soule, ou d’aigue ou il ait cuit herbes covenaubles a ceu.	And never have they been administered together with fire, and never have they been thinned with cold tea, as in some diseases that cause sorrow, and in this way one fills the suction with hot water or with water that has been cooked with edible herbs.
Li forme de la ventouse aministré a feu si est ci:	The form of the fire cautery is:
Et ait II dois de large et demi palme de parfont, et ait ou costeit entor lou mileu I petit pertus, ausi com por bouter une aguille, et soit d’arain, souef devant si qu’ele ne blece lou malaide au mettre sus lou membre;	And it has two large and half palm-sized scales on each side, and it either costs a little too much for the little pus, as if to bush a needle, and it is of rainwater, so that it does not rust the surgeon's hand when putting it on the limb.
et ait em mileu une verge de travers d’arain ou de fer, por mettre une chandoile emprise, et en soient et grans et petites selonc les maladies et l’eaige de ces qui les prenent;	and in the environment, it has a tooth of rainwater or iron to wear a tight glove, and it is both large and small according to the diseases and the pain of those who take them.
car les ventouses des enfans sont autres que des vielz, et des maigres que des gras.	For the suction cups of children are not like gills, but thin and lean.
Et doit on ensi mettre ceste ventouse sus lou membre:	And should one put this suction cup on the limb?
empren la chandoile de cire ou I linement, et le met emmi la ventouse au traver de la verge qui est emmi la ventouse, si que li clartez soit au fons de la ventouse qu’elle ne brule le malaide;	The patient should use the wax cauterization or liniment and insert it into the hole through the vein that has been made, so that the wax is at the end of the vein hole to prevent the heater from burning the patient.
et puis la met sus lou membre, et tes dois soit sus lou pertus que nos avons dit, si que quant on vuet, si en va li vapor, et oste on la ventouse;	and then place it on the affected part, and you should be at the vein that we have mentioned, if you see, if there is vapor coming out, and then remove the vein.
et emprent on le linement si com devant, et le rencomence sovent, se tu as mestier.	and use the liniment as before, and repeat it often, if you have skill.
En la ventouse donques qui est aministree em maladie de pleuresin, a tout aigue, n’a point de verge ne de pertus, et n’est amenistree fuer que quant ele est plaine d’aigue, et est mise sus lou membre tant soulement;	In the vein that is in a state of distress due to coughing and cold, there is no hole or windpipe, and it is not in a state of being until it is clear of the cold, and it is placed on the affected part only.
et c’est li forme:	1. "And it is the form: [the following lines are missing]
Sansues ne sont amenistrees fuer que en membres ou on ne puet mettre ventouses por lour petitece, si com levres et gencives, et semblans leus;	Without being harmed, only in parts where there can be ventouses for their small size, like lips and genitals, and similar parts.
et en leus desnuez de char, si com doi ou neis, et autres semblans;	and in them of horsehair, if they are not or not, and other similarities.
et li qualitez de l’user si est que quant tu trueves sansues que sont en aigues douces nettes sens porreture, si les pren;	and the quality of the hair if it is that when you find wet hairs that are not rough, and if they take them.
et les met une nut en aigue douce, tant qu’elles soient famillouses, et n’aient rien en ventres;	and they put a nut in wet hair, as long as they are not pregnant, and have no belly.
et puis soit sainiez de voinne et de ventouse, puis frote le membre tant k’il soit rouges, et met sus les sansues;	and then it is clean of the vein and the wound, then clean the member as much as it is red, and put on the hairs.
et quant elles seront plainnes, et cherront, se c’est leu ou on puisse mettre ventouse, se li met, car ce vaut mout aprés.	When they are flat and smooth, and if it is the shoulder or neck, put a pocket around it, as this is best.

et se li leus saine trop aprés lou cors des sansues, si moille I drapel de lin en aigue froide, et met sus, tant que li sans soit estenchiés;	If it is too tight after the arm is straightened, if the cold wet linen is not stretched enough, then put it on, as long as the arm is not stretched out.
et se li sans est multipliez, si met sus vitriole broié, ou gales, et semblans choses, tant qu’il soit estenchiez;	If the linen is multiplied, then put on vitrol or gas, and similar things, as long as it is stretched.
ou tu met sor le leu moitiez de feves pelees, et les laisse tant qu’elles s’aerdent au leu, si estanchera maintenant;	If you put half of the burned skin on the thigh and leave them as they become dry on the thigh, it will now be firm.
et se tu en as de plus mestier, si pren autres sansues.	And if you use more of it, if you take others without.
Et se les sansues ne se vuellent prendre, si frote le leu de sanc fres, ou tu i fiche une aguille tant que li sans en isse, et puis les met sus, et tantost com elles sentent lou sanc, si s’aerdent;	And if the threads will not take, if you clean the thigh with cold water or use a needle as follows: first insert it, and then place them as they feel the cold, until they dry.
et quant tu vues qu’elles chieent, si poudre sus un poc d’aloen et de seil broiet, ou de cendre, si cherront maintenant.	And when you see that they are cold, if you powder a small piece of aloe and silk or charcoal, it will now be cold.
Ci comence li livre des brisures	Here begins the book of fractures
Cist chapistres est maintes fois necessaires en l’art de medicine, et est restorement de brisure et de desaluement.	Many chapters are necessary in the art of medicine, and it is the restoration of fractures and dislocations.
Saichiez, chier fil, que li fol mire se gietent de cest chapistre, qu’il ne virent onques nul des anciens livres, ne lettre n’en lurent;	1. "Consider the force of the fire cautery, that the patient will not find any ancient books or letters.
et por ceste cause est estraingie li science en nostre terre, car je n’en trovai onques nul boin;	2. "And for this reason, the science is strained in our land, as I have never found any book.
et n’en sai nient, fuer que par la science des anciens livres, ou j’ai tant estudiiet que je en ai traite la science, et par experiment, et par l’acostumance de ma vie;	3. "And I have not found any book, for the science is strained in our land, as I have studied many books and through experience and habit of my life.
et je vos ai jai descrit en cest chapistre ceu qui est contenut, et l’ai abregié en la fin, et ai mostreit clerement les formes des estrumens que sont amenistrez, si com j’ai fait en ces II chapistres ci devant.	4. "And I have described in this chapter what is contained in it, and summarized at the end, and clearly shown the forms of the strangulations that are made, as I have done in these two previous chapters.
Il covient donques que nos disons ou prologue de cest livre les sommes de la parole et les chapistres ou li saiges met son entendement, et demore sus la verteit, si que cil qui sont esproveit saichent et aprenent cest art noble, et l’aprenent a autrui.	It is therefore necessary that we say at the beginning of this book the sum of words and chapters or the surgeon makes his understanding, and more so if those who have practiced it understand and learn this noble art, and learn to teach others.
Je dis que quant brisure ou dislocation ou torsions ou quasseure vient a aucun, si covient que tu te hastes de sainier lou malaide d’une part et d’autre, s’aucune chose ne lou te tot, si com foiblece de cors, ou enfes, ou viellars;	I say that when a fracture, dislocation, twist, or sprain occurs at any joint, if you quickly apply the remedy of both sides of the malady, nothing will fail, as with weakness of the heart, or children, or old age.
ou se li tens n’est tres chaus, ou trop frois;	or if it is not very tense, or too tight.
et menjuce cholz frois, c’est a savoir froides joutes, et char d’oiseil et de chevril, et ne boive point de vin, ne menjuce nules grasses chars, et ne s’emplisse mie trop de viandes qui remplissent les voinnes de sanc, tant que tu n’aies doute d’aposteme chaut, ne d’espandement de matiere au membre;	and if it is too cold, it is known as cold baths, and hot iron and horsehair, and do not drink wine, nor use thin-willed charcoal, and do not fill the veins with blood too much, as long as you have no doubt of apoplexy chaut, or expansion of matter in the member.
si reviegne li malaides a som premerain governement k’il a useit.	If the patient examines the member after his first treatment.
Et quant li os brisiés comence a restourer, si covient que on norrisse le malaide de viandes que font gros norrissement, ou il ait viscositeit, si com froment cuit en aigue, et ris, et testes, et piez, et pance de vaiche, et oefz, et poissons fres, et gros vin, et semblans chose.	And when the bones begin to heal, if it is necessary to remove the patient from the diet of meats that cause large excitements, or if there is viscosity, like bread cooked in hot water, and tests, and pies, and sausages, and lard, and fish, and large wine, and similar things.
Car a teil norrissement se reprent mues et plus tost li brisure.	For the excitement gets worse and the fracture heals faster.
Et saichiez que li os brisiez des vielz et des decrepites ne se pueent mie bien reprendre ne souder selonc lor nature por la sechor des membres, ne cil ausi qui sont trop tendre, si com os de petis enfans;	And you know that bones broken by fractures and decays cannot be well mended or strengthened according to their nature by the care of members, nor also those which are too soft, like small children's bones.
mais n’a cure, ramoinne sus l’os brisiet I gros tenrons qui s’aert et joint le membre ensamble, tant qu’il enforce si com il fut devant;	but there is no cure, first reset the broken bone and large tendons that were split and joined together, as it should have been before.
et ne li tot point de son oevre, et por ceu le covient norrir de grosses viandes, si com nos avons dit.	and do not let it stay in its place, and for this reason it is recommended to avoid large meals, as we have said.
Et saiches que les briseures sont diverses em maintes manieres.	And you know that there are many ways to cut.
Car li brisure dou chief est autre que li brisure dou pis, ou de la jambe, et je vos dirai en cest chapistre toutes manieres de brisure.	For the cut of the head is different from the cut of the leg or foot, and I will tell you all the ways of cutting in this chapter.
Car il i a brisure que vait a arvol, et autre en aguisant, si com li taille d’une penne por escrire.	For there is a cut that goes to the bone, and another that only scratches, like the size of a quill to write.
Et si a brisure avec plaie, et brisure a tout une petite fendure.	And if it is a cut with wound, and a cut is just a small slit.
Et a chescune maniere ait son engien, et son estrument propre en la restauration, selonc ceu que li remembrance vient en son leu;	And to have its engine and proper instrument in the restoration, according to what comes into his mind.
et est conue li brisure de l’os par ceu que li leus est tors, et apert bien par defuer, et sone au presseir de la main;	and it is known that the fracture of the bone by what is in his mind, and is open well by pressure, and some by hand.
et quant il n’i a tortuositeit ne son au tochier, et li malaides ne sent mie grant dolor, se n’i a point de brisure;	And when he has no knots in his way and the patient does not feel much pain, then there is no fracture.
mais il puet bien avoir tortuositeit, ou fendure, ou petite brisure.	However, it may have knots, or twist, or small fracture.
Si ne covient mie que tu lou mueves a la main, mais met sus medicines que vienent ci aprés, et puis l’estraint maintenant subtilment.	If you can only move it with your hand, but use the medicines that will come after, and then gently pull it now.
Et saiches que li brisure que vait en arvol, et sont les II parties desjointes, il les covient maintenant mettre a point igalment, ainsois que apostemes chaus i viegne;	And you should know that the fracture that will be in place is the two parts that are disjointed, and it is now necessary to put them together as evenly as possible, unless they cause pain.
et se apostemes chaulz i vient, si lou laisse aucun jor, tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez;	When the inflammation subsides and the pain comes, if it is not left alone for any length of time, it will increase.
puis le met igal au mues que tu pues legierement et saigement, et saiches que li restauration de li est plus legiere que li restaurations de celi ou il ait pieces;	Then, gently press the affected area with your fingers, and you will notice that the restoration of the joint is lighter than the restorations of other parts or when there are fragments.
puis l’estraint, si com il covient ci aprés.	Then, pull gently, as it should be done after.
Et se en l’os a piéces brisies, si l’estent de II pars, se c’est mains ou piet, ou a ta main se c’est uns petis membres, ou a II cordes, ou a une corde et a ta main;	And if it is in the bone with pieces broken off, if you can remove it by hand, or with your fingers, or with some small limbs, or with a cord and your hand;
et met le membre selonc sa figure natureil, si que quant les parties dou membre brisiet sont desevrees, si ramoinne par toz engiens les additions en lor leus au mues que tu pues, et garde que par ton ovraige ne viegne au malaide lesion ne doulor;	And he puts the limb in its natural position, so that when the parts of the broken member are adjusted, it is held by your hands as you please, and you must ensure that the pain does not return to the injured joint.
et ajoste bien les II chiés des os selonc les millors formes.	And adjust the two heads of the bones according to the best forms.
Et le sent bien a la main s’il te semble k’il ne soit mie bien:	And it feels good in the hand if it seems not well:
si la dresce bellement, et ne l’estraindre mie trop, ne presser si com font cil qui i font venir par lor ovraige aposteme chaut et contraction au membre, si com nos avons veut maintes fois.	If it grows well and is not overstretched, and does not press too much, do not apply pressure like those who make their wounds larger and contract the limb, as we have often wanted.
Et quant li membres est a point, si chastie bien lou malaide qu’il ne lou mueve, ne en veillant ne en dormant, ne en tornant, ne en autre maniere;	And when the limbs are swollen, if the patient is careful not to move them at all, neither during the day nor at night, nor when turning, nor in any other way.
et warde bien que li membres soit si asseurez qu’il ne sente nule dolor.	and make sure that the limbs are not painful.
Car quant il sent nulle dolor, si n’est mie a point, et le covient mettre en teil disposition qu’il ne sent nule dolor;	For when there is no pain, if it is not swollen, and it is necessary to put the limb in a position so that there is no pain.
et te garde k’il soit mis droitement, que tortuositez n’i veigne quant il iert restorez;	and keep it in its place, so that twisting does not occur when you put it back together.
et li qualitez dou membre brisiet est selonc ceu que je te dis.	And the quality of the broken limb is according to what I tell you.
Saiches que li membre brisiet sont divers em petitece et en grandor et en forme.	It is said that the broken limbs are various in size, width, and shape.
Car il i a petis membres, si com brais et dois et semblans:	For if he has eaten members, like bread and such, and similar things:
si covient envoloupeir drapelz de lin molz et subtilz;	If it is necessary to cover the edges of linen and silk with something:
et cil qui sont gros, si com cuixe et jambe:	And those that are large, like a kex and a leg:
si covient envoloupeir d’un liien large et dur, car li larges liiens embraice tout le grant membre, et l’estraint de toutes pars igalment, si qu’il n’i a nule taiche;	If it is necessary to cover the large linen and silk sheets because they wrap around the entire limb and pull at all parts equally, unless there is any flaw:
puis lie entor estoupes legieres, III tours ou IIII selonc lou membre, et estraint ta main un poc a tout le liien, puis vai au desus de la brisure et l’estraint moins, que la brisure puis esloigne un poc la brisure;	Then lightly sew the legs three times or four according to the size of the limb, and then tighten your hand a little on all the linen, then go to the end of the wound and tighten less than the wound, which the wound can enlarge a little;
et mollifie lou liien poc et poc, tant que tu preignes grant partie dou leu sain, puis repren I autre liien, et torne entor derechief sus lou leu brisiet;	And gently bend the limb little by little, as you pull on a large part of the healthy leg, then repeat the other limb, and turn it to the correct side over the broken joint.
puis revai a la partie desoz de la brisure, et l’estraint moienement, ne mie trop fort ne trop molement, si com nos avons dit en la premiere lieure desus;	Then go to the part opposite the break, and extract it gently, not too hard or too forcefully, as we have said in the first chapter;
puis met entre les liiens estoupes de lin ou drapelz, tant qu’il soit toz igalz, puis lie tout par desus I bendeil, et puis met tes esteles bien faites sus, s’il n’i a aposteme ou enfleure.	Then place between the wound edges of linen or cloth, as it is even, then sew it all with threads and then put your stitches well made on, if there is no gangrene or inflammation.
Et s’il i a enfleure ou aposteme, si met sus chose apaisant aposteme chaut, et qui oste l’enfleure, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors;	If it has swollen or become infected, and it is made to rest with things that relieve inflammation, and it is left alone for a while.
puis estrain sus tes esteles, et soient de moitiet d’une large cainne rese saigement, ou de fust dont on fait les clives, ou de rains de palme, et soient selonc ceste figure:	Then strain your belt, and be made of half a wide rope, or of fur from which they make clothes, or of rains from palm trees, and be in this shape:
mais il covient que li estele que om met sus la brisure soit un poc plus grosse et plus large que les autres;	But it is necessary that the belt that is put around the wound be a little larger and wider than the others:
et soit ausi longe com il covient au membre de petitece ou de grandor;	and be as long as it is necessary for the member of small or large size:
puis estraint sus les esteles ausi com tu as fait a la premiere lieure, puis lie desus un fil avenanment, si com en la premiere lieure sus la briseure;	Then tighten the belt as you did in the first place, then tie a string around it, as you did in the first place for the wound:
plus estroit est ensus, adés moins;	As the joint is stretched further, less.
et covient que li fil soient moien, ne trop gros ne trop menus, et soient de lin mol;	It is necessary that the string be thin and not too thick, and be of linen.
car se li fil sont gros, si com j’ai veut des oevres des folz qui font lor lieures des cordes de linement tort, et c’est grant error, car li lieure ne puet estre igal s’il est trop subtilz, et ne covient mie qu’il ait entre chescune estele moins dou doi d’espaice.	For if the string is too thick, as I have seen the works of the weavers who make the hours of the linen ropes, and it is a great error, for the thread cannot be even if it is too fine, and it only requires that there be less space between each thread.
Et se li malaides est navrez par les chiés des esteles aprés l’estrignement en leus sains, si met desoz elles estoupes de lin, ou lainne charpie, si qu’il ne se blece.	When the patient is anesthetized by the heads of the pins after being shaved clean, if they are not soaked with oil, or greased, if it does not cause pain.
Quant li plaie est avec la briseure, et li keurs est rompus, je en dirai la cure ci aprés.	When the wound is treated with a bandage, and the edges are torn, I will explain the treatment for this after.
Et saiches qu’il ne covient mie estraindre d’esteles toz les membres brisiez le premier jor.	And it is difficult to avoid breaking all the limbs when pulling on the pins every time.
Car quant li membres est grans, se n’i covient mie mettre esteles fuer que aprés V jors ou VII, ou plus selonc ta seurteit d’aposteme chaut sorvenant;	For when the limbs are large, it is not necessary to put on these larger sizes if after V years or VII, or according to your size of the aposteme that is causing the problem.

And it comes to pass that you take flour that is fine and well ground, and mix it with a large amount of water, and make this dough, neither too thin nor too thick, and use it, and this is the common way to restore the fracture in other positions, and at the same time for women and young children, because it is neither too hard nor too wet.

Ypocras dist en son livre c’on ne mette sus lou membre brisiet por restorer fuer que cerote fait de cire et d’oile, et nulle autre chose plus, et dist qu’il soit entre dous ne trop molz ne trop durs.	Ypocras states in his book that no matter how broken the bone is, it can be restored by making a mortar of wax and oil, and nothing else is needed, and he says that it should not be too soft or too hard.

It seems that Galen says that when restoring a broken bone, one should put on things that are dry and warm, like mirr and aloe and incense and similar things, as we have said.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre que vaut a lesion et a dolor:	Another way to emphasize that it is a wound and pain:
pren mugath et chevolz d’omes decopez, ou pennes d’oiseil, et vismalve, et seil igalment, et les broie, et en fai emplaustre et lou lie.	Take a piece of cloth and needles of copper, or threads of silk, and thread it, and sew it well, and the wound, and then make an emphasis on it.

si ne lou deslie par mains jors.	unless it is done by hand.

et repose li enflammation dou membre, et soit ostee li dolor, puis rencomence la lieure subtil, et un poc d’emplaustre, et ne l’estraindre mie si fort com devant;	and reduce the inflammation of the limb, and soothe the pain, then resume the application of the linen cloth, a little plaster, and do not strain it too much.

And if you see that gangrene has set in and there is bruising and pain and swelling, and you have the skill to plaster and bind, if it recurs, as you did at first properly.

des diverses manieres de brisure	Of various kinds of wounds
Maintes manieres de brisures sont, et diverses figures, et les causes sont destintees;	This sentence translates to: "There are many types of wounds, and various forms, and the causes are assigned.
car il a brisures que sont faites de percussion d’espee, et li colz oste tout l’os jusc’a syfac qui est desoz l’os, si com fait haiche ou fust;	Car il a brisures que sont faites de percussion d'espee, et le col et les os sont déchiris.
et por ceu est apelee ceste maniere de briseure «haichure».	Et c'est pour cela que cette façon de brisure est appelée "haichure".

et est li plaie de ces II brisures grans ou petite.	Et est la plaie des deux grandes ou petites brisures.
Et s’il i a percussion emboee, ou fendure ou de colz de piere, ou de cheoir sus piere, ou d’autres semblans.	And if it has an impact that is buried, or a cut or from the shattering of the edge, or from the piercing beneath the pierce, or from other such things.
Et s’il a brisure persant, qui aproiche jusc’a la toile qui est desoz l’os, ou elle est sus l’os, et est ceste plaie ou grans ou petite.	If there is a persistent wound, which is close to the skin that is loose from the bone, or it is under the bone, and this is the wound or large or small.
Et si a plaie qui est reponue en l’os ausi subtil com uns chevous, et est li fendure petite, et por ceu est apelee ceste brisure «capillaire»;	Et si une plaie est recouverte dans l'os comme des chaussets, et est une petite fendue, et pour cela est appelée cette façon de brisure "capillaire".
et si la plaie qui est faite ou par ferir de piere, ou par cheoir, ou par semblant chose, et fait entrer la piece de l’os aval, et est li leus chevez si com font li chaudelier quant il fierent sus les chaudieres;	If the wound is caused by injury from piercing, or choking, or something similar, and it allows the piece of bone to enter, and it is the same as when they make the hot iron enter the heating;
si entre li piere dedens.	If it enters the wound.
Et ceu avient plus a sous qui ont ou chief moistes os, si com chief d’enfant;	And there are more who have been hurt by moist bones, like children's joints.
et avient a toutes ces manieres de brisure que pieces menues en sont desevrees si com esteles;	and come in all these ways of fracture that light pieces are broken if they are like these.
et je em parlerai en son leu.	and I will speak about it in his ear.
Et conoissons toutes manieres de briseures par la detraction sus elles, et l’inquisition a tentes, et par la char corrumpue qui est sus.	2. And let us know all ways of fractures by the dislocation they cause, and through inquiries made, and by the crooked one that is caused.
Li semblance capillaire est conue par ceu que quant on a descovert l’os, et on frote enche sus, si apert li brisure noire.	3. The apparent appearance is known by the fact that when one discovers the bone, and one rubs it with fire, if the dark fracture is not open, it is not true.
En la cure de la brisure, pren garde as accidens dou malaide, et se tu vois nul malvais accident, si com vomissement de cole, et amission d’entendement, et estension, et paumeson, et fievre ague, et les eulz issir fuer et rougir, et autres semblans em plusors dispositions, si ne puet saner sens doute.	4. In the treatment of the fracture, keep a close watch on the patient, and if you see no such accident, then it is like vomiting of cole, and admission of understanding, and extension, and pulsatility, and fever ague, and the wounds issue and redden, and other signs appear in various dispositions, unless it can be cured with doubt.
Et se tu ne vois accident espoantauble, et tu esperes salut, si comence la cure.	If you do not see an unexpected accident, and you expect a cure to begin.
Et quant li navrez vient premier a toi, et c’est en yver, si covient oster l’os devant lou quatorzime jor au mues que tu pues.	And when the first pain comes to you, and it is in the rib, if it comes before the fourteenth day, then you should see a bone surgeon.
Et se c’est en esteit, si te haste d’oster l’os devant lou septime jor, ainsois que li toile desoz l’os soit corrumpue, et vienent li accident que nos avons dit.	And if it is in this way, if you haste to see the bone before the ninth day, then the cloth that covers the bone is corrupting, and the accident we have mentioned comes.
Et se li brisure de l’os vient jusc’a la toile que cuevre lou cerveil, si covient que tu fendes la partie fendue ensi:	And if the bone fracture comes near the skin that covers the earlobe, then you must cut off the damaged part.
et est que tu preignes lou chief dou malaide navreit, et descuevre sus l’os en toutes les manieres que tu pues, et sus la figure de la plaie plus souef que tu pues, et se decorrement de sanc vient au descovrir l’os, ou aposteme chaus, se li aide de ceu qu’il covient, et est que tu emplisses lou leu de drapelz moilliez en oile roset;	and it comes that you ignite the head of the patient's shoulder, and cut through the bone in all ways that you can, and through the figure of the wound more so than you can, and it dislocates from the sinus coming to reveal the bone, or abscess, if it helps with what comes, and it comes that you fill the shoulder with softened oils in rose oil.
et fai reposer la plaie tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et soies asseurez de decorrement de sanc;	and make the wound rest until the abscess is healed and is assured of dislocation of the sinus.
puis comence entor l’os a oster, et c’est fait selonc II manieres d’ovraige:	Then the bone begins to osteotomy, and it is done according to two ways of opening:
l’une manieres si est que tu copes au taillement estroit devant, et c’est li forme:	The first line of the translation is: "If one manner is such that you cut at the narrowed end, and it is shaped like this:".
Et puis i boute I autre taillement plus grant que lou premier.	Then there is another cut of a larger size than the first.
Et li seconde maniere si est que tu aies nombre de taillemens divers, les uns estrois et les autres larges, et soient a pointe, et soient de fer inde;	And the second line of the translation is: "And if you have many different-sized blades, some narrow and others wide, and they are sharp and made of iron;
et en oevre legierement, que tu ne bleces le chief.	And in light work, if you do not wound the head.
Et se li os est fors et durs, si covient que tu lou perces entor, ainsois que tu i aministres taillemens avec tareres, ne mie parfont qu’il ne percent outre l’os dou test, et doit avoir desus la pointe une marge ou I cercle, que ne laisse passer la pointe outre l’os;	And if the bone is hard and dense, then you must perforate it with great care, otherwise you will injure the bone with sharp tools. It should have a margin or a circle around it that does not allow the tip to pass over the bone.
et t’en covient avoir plusors, si que chescuns viegne en son leu de l’espés de l’os, si que tu aies tareres por toz test;	and you will have more, if every bone in your shoulder fits perfectly, if you have paid attention to this test.
et c’est li forme des III manieres de tareres:	And it is the form of the three ways of testing:
Li qualitez por percier entor l’os brisiet est que tu mettes I tarere sus l’os, et torne a tes dois tant que tu saiches que li os est perciez;	The quality of feeling through the broken bone is that you place one test on the bone, and turn it around as much as you can until you feel that the bone is perceived.
puis remet lou tarere autre part un poc aprés, et ensi fai tout entor, puis cope as incisoires l’espaice de l’os qui est entre les pertu, et fai ceu plus subtilment que tu pues, et legierement, si com nos avons dit, tant que tu en traies l’os a ta main, ou a aucun des estrumens que tu as si com tenailles, pinceures;	Then place the other test a little further on, and then feel all around, then cut into the edges of the bone that are between the holes, and do it as subtly as you can, and gently, as we have said, as you draw the bone with your hand, or with any of the nails, tenailles, pinceures.
et garde que tu ne touchier au cerveil ne au syfac.	And keep your hands away from the skull and the face.
Et quant tu avras l’os perciet, et trait, si couvient que tu reses l’apreteit qui est demoree de l’os a tout I autre estrument semblant a un incisoire, mais il covient qu’il soit plus tenves et plus subtilz que li autre incisoire;	When you have the bone perceived, and treated, if it comes that you reset the cut made in the bone with another instrument seeming like a cautery, but it should be more gentle and subtle than the other cautery;
et s’il demore rien des petis os, ne nulles escailles, si les oste legierement a I des estrumens;	and if it does not cut any of the small bones, nor the lighter ones of the bones, if they are slightly torn by the strips;
puis cure la plaie de tentes et d’oignemens que nos avons dit.	then treat the wound with tent and bandages that we have mentioned.
Et li autre maniere d’ovraige si est cil que Galiiens dist, qui est plus saus;	And the other way of opening is when it is said by the Galenic method, which is more correct;
et le loa molt fort, et c’est sa parole.	And the loud one very much, and that is his word.
Il covient premier que tu descuevres une partie de l’os, lai ou li brisure apert mues, si que quant tu avras descovert celle partie, si metras desoz lou chief de cest incisoire lenticulaire, de coi ci est li forme:	It is necessary first to remove a part of the bone, where the open fracture is located, so that when you have removed this part, if you measure from the root of this incision, the form is:
Et ne trenche mie d’une part, et est li partie ague en II costez, si que li trenchans est devers l’os;	And do not cut from one side, and the other part is turned in two pieces, if the cutting is towards the bone.
puis fier d’un petit maillet sus, si que tu copes legierement l’os tout entor, et te done bien en garde de la toile que est desoz;	Then firmly with a small nail, if you lightly touch the bone all around, and then well be careful of the cloth that is soaked.
s’elle est aerse a l’os, si l’oste legierement, car on l’oste bien sens nuisement, et sens paor.	If it is near the bone, if it touches the bone lightly, because it feels badly, and causes pain.
Et se li brisure de l’os ne perce jusc’a la toile, et li os est copez tant soulement par desus, et il i a petites pieces, si couvient rere celle asperiteit, et oster les escailles au raseur subtil dont tu dois avoir diverses quantitez, por amenistrer en chescun leu le plus covenauble, selonc l’ovraige et la figure de la brisure.	When the fracture of the bone does not pierce through the skin, and the bone is only covered by soft tissue, and it has small pieces, if they are covered by that roughness, and file down the scales with a subtle raser, you must have several quantities of it to meet each need according to the degree and appearance of the fracture.
Si reis devant de grant raseurs, et aprés de plus subtilz, et ne cesser de ceu faire tant k’il soit bien.	If you use a coarse raser first, and then a softer one afterward, and continue to do this as much as it is well.
En chescune des autres tailleures capillaires et brisure subtil, covient que tu amenistres cause selonc son adrecement;	In each of the other haircuts and subtle wounds, it is necessary to follow according to his command.
et c’est chose que n’est mie reponue a celui qui a mis son estude en cest art.	And this is something that cannot be answered by the one who placed their study in this art.
Et se li syfac est descovers, si covient que tu preignes I drapeil de lin, selonc la quantiteit de la plaie, et le moille en oile roset, et le mete sus la plaie;	And if the suture is discovered, then it is necessary that you apply a piece of linen to the wound according to its size, and grease it with rose oil, and place it on the wound.
puis pren I autre drapeil doublé en II ou en III, et le moille en vin et en oile roset, et le met sus le premier drapeil;	Then take another piece of suture doubled in II or III, and grease it with wine and rose oil, and place it over the first suture.
et fai ceu plus legierement que tu pues, que tu ne grever lou syfac, puis aministre par desus I autre liien, et ne l’estraindre mie fuer que tant k’il teigne la plaie soulement;	And do this more gently than you please, as you do not grease the suture, and maintain it with another piece of linen, and do not strain it too much, only as it touches the wound.
et le laisse ensi I jor ou II, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, puis le deslie, et i aministre medicines si com racines de lis, et farine de veces, et poudre d’encens, et aristologe, et semblans choses;	And let it lie for one or two days, until the wound is calmed, then remove it, and administer medicines as follows: roots of various kinds, flour, powdered frankincense, aristolochic acid, and similar things.
et de ces choses fai poudre, et met sus la plaie, et i aministre adés medicines mondefians sens mordication;	And make a powder of these things, and place it on the wound, and administer further medicine without bittering.
et warde que li plaie soit adés nette, que tu n’i laissier mie l’oignement, ne n’i laissier mie assembler bowe, car quant bowe s’asemble sus la toile dou cerveil, si la corront et porrist, et avient au malaide grans malice;	And make sure the wound is clean, and do not apply ointment, nor stitch it up, because when bowstrings are assembled on the skin, they can cause great pain to the patient.
car quant on met sus lou syfac chose mordant, si nercist par desus.	When one puts on a piece of clothing that bites, it can cause discomfort.
Pren warde donques, se nulz mavais accidens vient au malaide, si com nos avons dit, si est doutable sens doute.	When a sudden accident comes to the patient, if no one is present, it is uncertain what to do, as we have said, if there is any doubt in the matter.
Et se noiror n’i vient fuers que por la medicine c’on a mise sus, que teil vertu ait, si covient que tu preignes une partie de miel, et III parties d’oile roset et en glue I drapel, et lou met sus lou syfac;	And if the blacking does not come off except with medicine, which we have applied, then it is recommended that you put a part of honey and three parts of olive oil and one part of glue in a pot, and then apply it to the clothing.
puis lou cure de manieres de cures qu’il couvient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then the treatment is carried out in various ways, as necessary, to make it healthy.
Saiches que aucune fois sont brisies les II parties dou neis desus, ou li une par li soulement, car ce sont II os;	Scars that are never broken are the two parts of the skin that are not cut, or only one, because they are bones.
et cil desoz est cartillaginous, et ne brise mie, si ne fait fuer k’enbower ou tordre, et puis saine.	And this is cartilage, and does not break, unless it is bent or twisted, and then it heals.
Et se l’une des II parties est brisie, si covient que tu boutes ton petit doi ou pertus dou neis, et met igal cele brisure dedens a ton doi indice, et au pouchet par defuer, tant que li neis reveigne selonc sa figure natureil;	If one of the two parts is broken, then you should cut off your small toe or nail and make the break as equal as possible on your thumb index, and in the pouch according to its natural form.
et fai ce legierement, et warde que li malaides ne sente dolor par ton ovraige.	And do this lightly, and make sure that the patient does not feel pain from your action.
Et se li brisure est en la partie desus lou neis, et ne puet venir li dois au leu, si couvient que tu lou mettes igal au chief d’un rait un poc gros.	If the break is in the part of the toe that does not touch the ground, and cannot be reached by the big toe, then you should place it equally at the base of a large finger.
Et se li brisure est de II pars, si refai autretel, et te haste de restorer lou premier jor, se tu pues;	If the break is in the second part, then you should repeat the action, and if you are able to restore the first joint, then do so.
se ce non, aprés lou septime ou le disime, quant li apostemes chaus est apaisiez, puis bouthe au chief dou neis tentes de drapelz de lin, se li brisure est en une partie.	If this is not possible, then after the ninth or tenth day, when the wound has healed and the patient is calm, cut off the toe or nail that is causing the pain, and if the break is in one part.
Ou tu boutes I autre d’autre part, se li brisure i est;	If you cut one part, the other will also break.
et soient les tentes si grosses qu’eles emplissent les pertus dou neis.	and if they are large, they fill the cavities with pus.
Et dirent aucun restorour c’on doit moillier les tentes em burre, et muer chescun jor.	And no restorer says we must smooth the edges in burr, and each one dies every day.
Il ne me semble mie que ce soit bien, mais covient qu’elles soient moillies en confection d’aubun d’uef, et de poudre de molin;	It seems only then, but they must be made in the form of uff's flour and powdered milled;
puis laisse la tente, tant que li os soit fers, et li cartilaiges endurcis.	then leave the dressing, as long as the bone is firm, and the cartilage is hardened.
Et aucune fois boute on ou neis pennes d’oie en leu de tentes, et si a I souef drapeil entor, et se tient la briseure, et soffle li malaides parmi;	And no time should you cut or pull out the wings of the goose from the wounds, and if the skin is hanging loosely, and holds tightly, and blows the salves among;
or fai lou kel ke tu vues.	For the fire cautery, instruct the patient to let the hairs grow long and even; and if they prick at their base, hold the eyes steady so they do not move until they grow.
Et se apostemes chaus vient au neis tandis com tu i oevres, si i met cerote ou coton moilliet en oile roset, ou en I poc de dyaquilon.	When the hot iron comes to the skin while you are working, if it touches a piece of wool or silk that is slightly oily or in a pouch of alcohol.
Et se apostemes chaus n’i vient, si met emplastre par defuer, de farine de sisament, et de poudre d’encens, confites avec aubun d’uef, puis met sus estoupes legieres, et ne liier mie lou neis;	And if the abscess does not come out, apply plaster made of flour and incense powder, mixed with egg yolk, then put on light sponges, and do not tie it too tightly.
et se li brisure dou neis est petite, et il est brisiés em menues pieces, si l’estrai as estrumens covenables a ceu, puis cout la fendure, et la cure de choses enjanrans char, et soudant, si com emplastres et oignemens covenables a ceu;	And if the wound is small and it is torn into fine pieces, if the extraction is done with suitable tools, then cut the skin, and the cure of things enchanting charms, and soothing, if like plasters and ointments are suitable for this;
et s’il n’a dedens lou neis nule plaie, si lou cure de tentes, et i met cainnes de plonc, tant qu’il soit sanez.	If there is no wound and the patient is healthy, if the cure of tentacles occurs and he puts in pins, as long as it is healthy.
de la routure de la mandibule	Of the dislocation of the lower jaw
Quant li mandibule est route desoz, et il n’i a point de plaie defuer, et li brisure est defuer tant soulement, et n’est mie brisiez en dous, fuer que corbelz dedens, si le conoist on legierement.	When the lower jaw is dislocated, there is no wound, and the fracture is not deep, but only slightly so, and it is not broken into pieces, but rather bent slightly, like a bow. If it is noticed, it can be gently treated.
Il covient, se li brisure est en la destre partie, que tu boutes ton doi indice en la bouche dou malaide;	It is necessary to note that if the fracture is on the left side, you should cut your finger in the mouth of the helper.
et se li brisure est en la mandibule senestre, si boute ton doi indice de la main destre, et boute la brisure dedens legierement, et l’afaite a l’autre main par defuer, et met igal.	And if the fracture is on the left side of the mandible, cut your finger on the right hand, and lightly cut the fracture, and do it with the other hand in reverse, and hold steady.
Et se li brisure de la mandibule est desevree en II, si covient que tu aministres extension de II pars, tant qu’il soit igalz.	And if the fracture of the lower jaw is described in two parts, then it comes that you administer extension of two parts, as long as it is equal.
Et se commovemens des dens avient, ou routure, si les estrain d’un fil d’or ou d’argent ou de soie, puis met sus la mandibule brisie cerote, et met sus I drapel double;	And if the teeth move or fracture, if they are pulled from a gold, silver, or silk thread, then put it on the broken mandible, and put on two folds.
et met sus lou drapel une grant estele bien faite, ou une piece de cuir igal, longe et large selonc la mandibule, et la lie sus au mues que tu pues, et comande a malaide qu’il se repose, et menjuce viandes legieres.	And place under the louse a well-made iron nail, or a piece of leather similar, long and wide according to the mandible, and tie it to the mouth you choose, and instruct the patient to lie down, and give him light food.
Et se tu vois que li figure se chainge, si le deslie au tier jor, et puis remet a point ceu que c’est chaingiet;	If you see that the figure changes, if it moves too much, and then return to the point where it was originally;
et met emplaustre sus, de la poudre dou moulin avec abun d’uef ou farine de sisament, aprés ceu que tu as osteit lou cerote;	and apply plaster with flour from the grinding mill, or sisal thread, after you have set the lice;
et met sus l’emplaustre lainne legiere, et se li emplaustres s’aert, et li disposition dou malaide ne se chainge, laisse le tant k’il soit sanez;	and apply the plaster on the inside of the lice, and when it is dry, press it onto the skin, and the position of the patient does not change, leave it as long as it remains healthy;
maintes fois est sanez en III semainnes.	The patient's condition improves after three weeks.
Et se apostemes chaus vient, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit maintes fois.	And if the abscess bursts, if we have not said this many times before.
Et s’il i a brisure et plaie ensamble, rewarde se nule piece de l’os en est ostee;	And if there is a fracture and wound in the same bone, it is repaired with a small piece of bone.
si subtilie de l’oster as estrumens covenaubles a ceu.	If the bone has thin and flexible parts in this area.
Et se li plaie est estroite, si l’eslarge a flaime selonc ta necessiteit.	If the wound is large, then enlarge it according to your need.
Et quant tu avras ostees toutes ces pieces, et il n’i demore nule, si cout la plaie, s’ele est large, et met sus I des emplaustres covenaubles a ceu, por enjanrer char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	When you have all these pieces, and there is no lack of pain, if the wound is wide, and it is large, and put on flexible dressings at this point, to ensure health until it is cured.
de la forcele	of its strength.
Li forcele brise plusors fois devant, devers l’espaule, et li brisure si est selonc III manieres:	The break occurs more often in front of the shoulder, and the fracture is repaired in three ways.
ou elle est brisie et desevree en II, et i a pieces, et est li plus legiere a restorer;	Or, it is broken and dislocated in two places, and there are pieces, and it is the lightest to restore.
ou il i a brisure avec plaie.	Or, there is a fracture with a wound.
Et li ovraiges si est quant li brisure est sens plaie, que tu aies II ministres, si que li uns teigne l’ajutoire que sent la forcele brisie;	And the dressing should be changed as soon as the wound is sore, if you have two assistants, so that one can hold the injured part while the other changes the dressing.
et li autres estende lou col vers la partie;	and he extends the other arm towards the part.
puis met igal la brisure a tes dois, si que li forme soit si com il covient, et n’i ait ne apparance ne chevement.	then place the incision at your two fingers, if it forms as it should, and there should be no appearance or movement.
Et se tu a mestier de plus estendre, si met desoz l’espaule au malaide une spere reonde de drap, ou de lainne, et soit grosse selonc ta necessiteit;	And if you have to extend further, if you place the elbow of the patient against a round object such as a spoon or a ring, and it is large according to your need.
et estent et lieve la forcele, et estraint le spere a ta main, si que tu mettes igal la brisure, si com il covient.	and stretch and lighten the force, and hold the sphere at your hand, if you place the incision exactly as it should be.
Et se tu ne pues traire le chief de la forcele au defuer, por ceu qu’elle vient em parfont, si covient que li malaides gise sovin sus son hatereil, et met desoz l’espaule I oreillier moien, et boute li ministres l’espaule aval, tant que li os de la forcele soit levez.	1. If you do not treat the head of the strong force, because it comes in front, then the patient's strength will increase, and they should take care of their shoulder or ear, and hold the muscles of the shoulder, until the bone of the strong force is raised.
Et puis adrece la brisure a tes dois, et se tu lou trueves debrisiet, si covient que tu fendes sus;	Then direct the incision to your two fingers, and if you break the bone, it should be cut off. If you manage to do this, you will succeed.
et trai fuer les pieces legierement, et se li os ne puet joindre por aucun sormontement, si le cope a l’un des incisoires que tu as;	And then cut through the lighter pieces, and if the bone cannot be joined by any means, if it is one of the incisions you have.
mais que tu mettes desoz la forcele cest estrument, por warder lou syfac:	But make sure to use enough force with this instrument to ensure its effectiveness.
et semble une cuiller, et n’est mie chevez, et soit ausi large com il lou covient, selonc la grandor de l’os et la possance de l’uevre;	And it seems like a spoon, and is not too sharp, and should be as wide as the bone requires, according to the size of the bone and the strength of the hand.
et ait II chiés, si com tu vois, et soit li uns larges, et li autres estrois, si com est li routure de la plaie que tu as fait quant tu as trait les os;	And it has two ends, as you see, and the larger ones should be wider than the others, as the fracture of the wound you made when you treated the bone.
et quant tu es asseurez d’aposteme chaut, si cout la plaie, et se li routure est petite, ou tu doutes aposteme chaut, si emple la plaie de drapelz et de tentes, selonc sa quantiteit.	When you are sure of the incision point, if the wound is small, and if you doubt the incision point, if you use the wound of linen and tapestry, according to its quantity.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si moille I drapel en oile roset et en aisil et en vin, et met sus.	2. And if apostemy is large, it comes, if you have a lot of cloth in oil and wool and wine, and put it on.
Li estrignement de l’os, quant il est sens plaies et sens tailleure, est que tu mettes sus l’os l’enplaustre de la poudre dou molin et d’aubun d’uef, et met estoupes legieres sus, et met une spere desoz l’assele, se tu en as mestier;	The stripping of the bone, when it is sensitive to pain and to the tailor's cut, is that you place on the bone the pulverized powder of millstone and oakum of mackerel, and light sponges on top, and a small dot of glue at the seam, if you can;
puis pren une tres grant bende d’une palme de large, puis met I drapeil double sus estoupes, et l’emplaustre;	Then take a very thick band of a palm leaf, then put on a double fold of cloth, and apply it;
puis pren une estele subtil de III dois de large et de lonc, et l’envoloupe entor celui bendeil, si que li chief dou bendeil soient pendant;	Then take a small needle of III degrees wide and long, and wrap it around the bend, so that the head of the bend remains stable.
et met l’estele sus la briseure, et torne le bendeil sus lou col, et desoz l’asselle sainne, et desoz l’asselle malaide;	And put the needle on the bracelet, turn the bend over the shoulder, and unloose the healthy arm, and unloose the injured arm.
et la ramoinne de chescune partie, et quant tu vois ke li lieure tient la briseure avenanment, et tu vois clerement que li estele ne se muet desus l’os brisiet, si le rewarde chescun jor, et quant li liiens eslaiche, si lou restraint;	And tighten each part, and when you see that the ligature holds the bracelet firmly, and you see clearly that the needle does not move on the broken bone, then reward each one, and when you untie it, if the restraint is loose.

Poc avient que li espaule brise ou large leu ne em mileu, et ne lou seit on fuers que par lou touchement;	A sudden injury occurs when the shoulder breaks or becomes too wide due to the bone not being in its proper position, and it does not heal on its own, only through touching.

de la brisure de l’ajutoire	The first sentence to translate is "de la brisure de l’ajutoire". The translation of this phrase
Li adjutoires est ceu qui est entre lou coute et lou chief de l’espaule, et s’il est brisiez, si le doit on restorer selonc l’une des II manieres:	The assistant is that which is between the shoulder bone and the shoulder blade of the arm, and if it is broken, then it should be repaired according to one of the following two methods:
dont l’une est que tu pren I fust plain de moiene groissor, selonc ceste forme:	The other method is to use a piece of clean cloth, according to this form:
Et lie as II chiés II liens, et les pent en haut, et siece li malaide sus I siege;	And tie the two ends together, and pull them up, and place the blade under the stitch.
puis li giete som bras brisiet sus le fust, tant qu’il viegne a l’aissele, et ait em mi une corbeure de fust, puis pent sus aucune pesant chose ou li ministres l’estende aval;	Then place the sleeve over the broken arm, until it reaches the wrist, and make a loop with the sleeve, then it can hold any heavy thing or extend the sleeve around it.
puis mette li mires la briseure igal a ses mains ensamble, tant que li briseure retorne si com il covient.	Then put the forceps evenly in your hands, as long as the forceps return to its place as intended.
Et li autre maniere si est que on sovine le malaide sus son hatereil, et li lie la main a son col, puis comande a II ministres que li uns teigne ceu qui est sus la briseure a ses mains, et li autres teigne desoz a tout I liien, et estende chescuns a sa partie.	If the patient is unable to hold the dislocated head in place, the surgeon should lift the patient's arm and place their hand on the patient's collarbone. The surgeon should then instruct the patient to touch the mark made by the surgeon's hand at their own fingers, and also touch other marks on different parts of the body. The patient should extend each limb to its full length.
Et se tu vues que li estraction soit plus fors, si estraint I liien desoz la briseure, et sus la briseure, et estende chescuns des ministres a sa part.	And if you see that the extraction is more difficult, then break the lock and extend each of the parts.
Et se li briseure est prochiene au chief de l’espaule, si covient que tu mettes I liien moien desoz l’assele, et I autre vers lou coute, desoz la briseure;	And if the forceps are tilted towards the shoulder blade, then you should tie one end of the string to the shoulder blade and the other end to the opposite side, so that the forceps do not slip.
et ausi se li briseure est devers lou coute, si i covient mettre I liien legierement, sens labor, tant que li briseure soit igalz sus lou leu, et sus lou coute;	And if the forceps are tilted towards the elbow, then you should lightly tie one end of the string to the elbow and the other end to the opposite side, so that the forceps do not slip, while ensuring that the forceps are even with the shoulder blade and the elbow.
puis met igal la brisure, si com il covient, et l’estraint, se apostemes chaus n’i vient.	Then place the forceps evenly as intended, and tighten it, hold your breath so that nothing happens.

And tie the bandage, and extract it with the aid, and from the arm, if the arm is in the elbow, nothing will stop you, or if the shoulder is not moved.

de la brisure du bras	of the fracture of the arm.
Li bras est compos de II os, qui sont apelez li dui «foscile», de coi li uns est petis, et est cil qui enseut le pouchet;	The arm is composed of two bones, which are called the "funicle," and some are smaller, and it is these that form the pouch.
et li autres est grans, et est cil qui est desoz, devers lou petit doi;	and the other is large, and it is the one that is dislocated, towards the small joint.
par aventure brise li grans foscile soulement, ou li petis, et par aventure andui ensamble.	by chance only the large bone is broken, or the small one, and by chance they are assembled together.

et quant li grans est brisiez, si est li sanation male, et plus griés que quant il sont brisiez andui ensamble.	and when the large bones are broken, it is a poor cure, and more painful than when they are broken together.

Et se c’est li grans foscile, si le covient estraindre plus fort;	And if it is the large bone, then the treatment must be strained more forcefully.

puis estende li ministres som bras a la partie desoz a sa main, ou a I liien, et uns autres ministres a I autre au desus.	Then extend the shoulder muscles of the arm to the opposite side, either towards the thumb or towards the elbow, and some other muscles in the opposite direction.
Et puis le mette li mires igal, selonc sa millor forme.	And then he puts the head in place, according to his best form.
Et se en la brisure a pieces, si met chescune en son leu, et s’il en i a nule desevree ke poigne lou keur, et tu ne la pues restorer en son leu, si fent sus et l’oste, si com nos avons dit devant.	And if it is in pieces, then he puts each piece in its place, and if there are no deviations that point to the cause, and you cannot restore it in its place, then follow our advice and the bone, as we have said before.
