si pren la cure.	if they take care.
Et se en l’encomencement dou restorement sorvient apostemes chaus, si glue I drapeil de cerote fait d’oile roset et de cire blainche, que ne soit mie ne trop durs ne trop molz;	And if in the beginning of restoration, abscesses appear, and they are treated with ointments made of rose oil and wax, which are neither too hard nor too soft, nor too greasy;
et lie I drapeil par sus subtilment, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez.	and they are applied gently, until the abscesses are relieved.
Et puis oste lou cerote, et i met l’emplaustre de la poudre dou molin avec abun d’uef, pues met les esteles, et soit li estele de la briseure adés plus fors, et un poc plus large que les autres;	And then the bone, and he puts the powder of the fine mill with a lot of urine, then the seeds, and it is the seed of the brisket that is more forward, and a little wider than the others.
et saiches que il doit avoir VI esteles ou bras em plusors dispositions:	and he says that it must have VI branches or arms in different positions:
soit que li briseure soit en l’un des os, soit en II;	whether it is in one of the bones, or in II:
et estraint plus sus la briseure que autre part, et toz jors moins en aloignant, si com j’ai dit au comencement dou chapistre;	and it is drawn up more above the brisket than other parts, and less by moving away, as I said at the beginning of this chapter:
et soient li drapelz que sont sus la briseure molz et moistes, et ne soient mie dur ne aspres;	and be the belts that are above the wet and moist brisket, and not be too hard or rough:
et soit li filz, dont il est estrains, de lin, ne trop gros ne trop menus, si com nos avons dit.	And let the child, whose parents are absent, of the lineage, not too large nor too small, as we have said.
Et rewarde lou membre et lou liien aprés aucuns jors.	And reward the member and the limb after some years.
Et se aucuns mavais accidens vient au membre, si com prurite ki vient au membre, si covient que tu aroses lou membre d’aigue chaude, tant que cil prurites soit apaisiez;	And if any one happens to have an accident come to the member, if prickling comes to the member, if you should cool the member with warm water as much as possible, until the prickling is calmed.
et laisse le membre ne mie estroit reposer.	and let the member rest without moving.
Et puis rencomence l’estrignement, et se li liiens est amolis et li os desevrez, et semblant chose, si l’adresce.	And then the stripping resumes, and if the limb is softened and the bones are loosened, and it seems like something, then it will be loosened.
Et se pren warde se li norrissemens ne puet venir au membre, por ceu qu’il est trop estrois, si covient que tu l’amollisses I poc, et laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant que li norrissemens i corre, et puis l’estraint.	And if the nails come to the member, because it is too tight, then you must soften it in a short time, and let some years pass, until the nails grow, and then strip it.
Et se nules de ces choses que nos avons dit ne vient au malaide, si ne lou desliier jusc’a XX jors.	And if these things do not come to the patient when we have said them, within twenty years.
ou enqui entor, puis li pent les mains a son col, et soit ses cols igalz, et se warde de movement et de degitement, et dorme sus son dos;	Or if the patient is in pain, then he can put his hands on his chest, and his chest should be even, and with little movement and relaxation, he falls asleep on his back.
et saiches que ceste briseure est restoree en XXX jors ou en XXXV, et par aventure en XX jors, selonc les compositions et les complexions des vertus.	And it is restored in XXX years or XXXV, and by chance in XX years, according to the compositions and complexions of the virtues.
de la brisure de la main	of the hand fracture
Saiches que au dos de la main et as nous des dois avient poc de briseures, et n’i vient mais que ploieure maintes fois.	It is hoped that on the back of the hand and at both wrists there are few fractures, and only sprains many times.
Et quant li plante de la main est brisie ou ploie, si covient que li malaides siece croisiet, et siet droitement devant lui igalement;	When the bone of the hand is broken or crushed, if the patient manages to hold it steady, and holds it firmly in front of them,
puis met sa main sus la toie estendue, et estende li ministres les os brisiez, et les mete igalz li mires, tant qu’il soient bien joint;	then they extend their hand over the extended toe, and extend the broken bones, and place them evenly in the joints, as long as they are well connected.
et met l’emplastre et les estoupes, se apostemes n’i vient, puis i met une estele selonc la quantiteit dou leu;	and apply the plaster and bandages, if necessary, then put on a splint according to the size of the limb.
et soit envoloupee en I drapeil de lin.	and is wrapped in one fold of linen.
Et se li briseure est au pardedens entor lou ventre de la plante, si fai une spere de drapelz, et comande au malaide qu’il l’estrigne a sa plante brisie;	And if the fracture is at the heel of the foot, then make a ball of bandages, and instruct the patient to pull the bandage over the broken heel.
et puis l’estrain d’un lonc drapeil, et soit li estele de keur souef ausi grans com li plante de la main, et l’estraint, si com il covient.	And then the strain of a long, flaccid member, and it is the size of the hand, and it is strained, as it should be.
Et se li brisure est au defuer, si covient que tu mettes une estele sus, et une autre desoz en la plante, si que li mains soit overte et droite, puis le lie tot entor la main, et estanche lou liien entre les dois.	If the fracture is at the bone, then it comes that you place a splint on it, and another one on the foot, if the hand is over and right, then the line goes through the hand, and it is tightened between the two.
Et se li briseure vient a aucun des nous des dois, se c’est li pouchés, si le met igal, si com il covient;	And if the fracture comes to none of us on both sides, and they are locked, then it should be placed evenly, as it should be.
et l’estraint avec la plante, et se tu vues si met une estele droite petite por lever la briseure, et ne se mueve;	And it is strained with the palm, and if you see that a straight small nail is placed to lift the fracture, and does not move.
et se li brisure est as autres dois, si com en l’indice ou l’un des autres, si le met igal, et lou lie avec lou doi sain qui est aprés;	And if the fracture is in others, and as in the index or one of the others, if it is placed evenly, and it is held with the healthy finger that follows.
ou tu les lie toz en I tenant, que mues vaut, ou tu met sus une estele, si com ou pouchet;	If you tie them all together with what you have, or if you put them on a sling, as much as you can.
et pren warde en la restauration et en la disposition d’aposteme chaut, et secor ceu qui i vient, si com j’ai dit.	And take care in the restoration and positioning of the dislocation, and cut what comes, as I have said.
de la cuixe brisie	Of the broken joint
Li os de la cuixe est maintes fois brisiez, et bien le voit on quant elle torne devant et derrier;	The bones of the elbow are often broken many times, and it is clear when it turns in front and behind.
et li restauration si est c’on lie I liien desus la briseure, et I autre desoz.	And the restoration if it is tied with the lines of the fracture, and the other is not.
Et li malaides gise sus sa faice, puis estende chescuns ministres son lien a sa part igalment;	And the patient lies on their face, then extend each member of its ligament to its equal part.
et c’est quant li brisure est emmi l’os.	And it happens when the fracture is set in the bone.
Et se li brisure est prochiene a la racine de la cuixe, si soit li uns des liiens devers lou poignil, et li autres liiens desoz la briseure.	And if the fracture is near the root of the joint, then some of the bones are pulled in one direction and the others in another, causing the break to be uneven.
Et ausi s’elle est prochiene au genoil, et adonques soit li liens delez lou genoil, et soit li extension aval;	And if it comes to the joint of the knee, then loosen the ligaments of the knee and extend the leg.
puis mette li mires l’os igal a ses II mains, tant qu’il soit selonc sa figure natureil, et puis met l’emplaustre, et lou lie, se apostemes chaz n’i vient.	Then place the bone even with your two hands, according to its natural shape, and then place the splint, and the bandage, and if it does not move, it is correct.
Et s’il i a aposteme chaut, si le laisse apaisier puis revien a ton ovraige et a ta cure;	And if it moves slightly, then let it rest and return to your work and your care.
li lieure est faite en teil maniere.	The bandage is made in parts.
Il covient que tu envoloupes sus la briseure I bendeil dur doublé en II ou III, et en demoure li superfluitez, puis torne la jambe tant que li talons veigne a la racine de la naige, et boute I fil lonc entre la cuixe et la jambe, delez lou genoil desoz, et veignent li chief dou fil au desus;	It is necessary that you wrap it around the fracture, doubling it in two or three layers, and removing the excess, then bend the leg until the heel comes to the root of the nail, and put one long thread between the kneecap and the leg, loosening the knee joint, and the end of the thread goes to the ankle;
puis torne sus la jambe et sus la cuixe le bendeil, puis met sus la briseure esteles, et met une estele sus l’os de la jambe;	Then turn the leg and the knee of the bend, then put the splint on, and put a splint on the bone of the leg.
puis emple le leu vuit entre la jambe et la cuixe de drapelz souef por mettre igal l’estrignement, puis comence a liier forment III tors ou IIII sus la briseure;	Then use the fifth finger between the leg and the knee of the cloth to evenly stretch the strap, then start to tie the form III or IV on the splint.
et quant plus vas en sus de la briseure, et moins l’estraint;	And as you go further on the splint, less is tied.
puis enten as II chiés dou fil que tu as bouteit entre la jambe et la cuixe, et en lie III esteles que sont desus, puis revai au desoz au chief dou fil, tant que tu veignes delez le piet;	Then take the two strings that you have tied between the leg and the knee, and the third splint that is attached, then go back to the other end of the file at the head of the string, as long as you can see the piebald.
et l’estraint, si qu’il ne se mueve de son leu, puis le laisse ensi, puis k’il n’i vient ne aposteme ne enfleure n’autre semblant.	When the limb is strained, if it does not move from its joint, then it is left alone, and there is no signs of inflammation or swelling.
Et s’il i avient, si le deslie, et adresce ceu que i vient, si com nos avons dit maintes fois;	And if it comes, if it does not return, and addresses what comes, as we have said many times.
et se il i a pieces de l’os que poigne, si le covient ewer, s’om puet;	And if it has pieces of the bone that pricks, then it can be treated; and it can be.
et s’on ne puet, si covient fendre le leu, et traire fuer;	And if it cannot be treated, then it is necessary to cut the limb, and drain it.
et le cure si com nos avons dit, tant k’il soit sanez.	And the treatment is as we have said, whether it is healthy or not.
Et aucune fois est brisie li cuixe ensi c’on i met esteles, si com en l’ajutoire et ou bras;	And never has the joint been broken in, if it is not put in its place, as we have said in the shoulder and arm.
toutevoie, en la restauration ensi faite ne cloche mie li malaides.	The first sentence to translate is: "Ou cautere de feu comande au malaide qu’il laisse les poilz tant qu’ils soient lons et igals; et s’il le poignent a lor nassance, se li estraint les eulz qu’il ne se muevent tant qu’il naissent.
Et saiches que li cuixe est restoree en L jors, ou poc moins ou poc plus, selonc les diversitez des complexions.	He advises that the elbow is restored in L years, or less than less, according to the differences of complexions.
de la ruelle dou genoil	Of the right knee joint
Saiches que en la ruelle dou genoil avient poc brisure, mais elle ploie maintes fois.	It is said that in the right knee joint there is little fracture, but it wheezes many times.
Et s’elle brise, si n’est mais c’une fendure, ou I pertus, et avient a tout plaie, et sens plaie, et ce sent om bien.	And if it breaks, if not but a bruise, or a puncture, and comes to all wounds, and feels pain, and that is well.
Et li restauration si est c’on mette igal ceu qui est rons a ses dois, tant qu’il soit assemblez mues c’on puet;	And the restoration is placed if one makes equal those that are lost to their other side, as long as they are assembled in their place.
puis met l’emplaustre, et i met une estele reonde, se tu en as mestier, et l’estraint si com il covient, puis rewarde toutes les dispositions que nos avons dit ens autres briseures, si com aposteme chaut et autre semblant;	Then place the template, and insert a rounded staple, if you are skilled at it, and tighten it as it should be, then reward all the adjustments we have mentioned in other fractures, such as dislocation and other similar cases.
si met a chescun accident ceu k’il li covient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	If you place at each accident what it should be, as long as it is safe.
de la brisure de la jambe	Of the break of the leg
Saiches que en la jambe ait II os, de coi li uns est apelez par droit non «mustelz», et li autres est apelez «foscile»;	That in the leg there are two bones, because some are called by right not "mustelz", and the others are called "foscile".
et avient tout auteil briseure com il vient au bras, et por ceu est li restauracion si com celle dou bras igalment, et li ovraiges est tout i. Et se li dui os sont brisiet ensamble, si torne li jambe de toutes pars.	When a fracture occurs at the elbow, and it is treated in the same way as a properly set arm, and all the parts are restored. And if both bones are broken together, then turn the leg of all parts.
Et se li os subtilz est brisiez, si torne devant.	And if the fine bones are broken, then turn forward.
Et se li gros os est brisiez, si sent on grant dolor, et le voit on bien;	And if the large bones are broken, and it feels great pain, and one can see well.
et torne desoz.	then turn around.
Adonques amenistre extension, et le met igal, et lie les esteles igalement;	After the extension, put it in place, and hold it evenly.
mais toutevoie, il covient se li brisure est laide, et il i a plusors pieces, que li extension soit menor et plus legiere;	But if it is not, it is necessary that the fracture be straight, and if there are more pieces, then the extension should be smaller and lighter.
et l’alige selonc ta vertu.	and the other according to your virtue.
Et quant tu as tout acomplit ton ovraige, si pren II faixes de fust chevees que porpreignent la jambe d’une part et d’autre, et soient dou lonc de la jambe des le genoil jusque desoz;	When you have completed your work, if you take two pieces of braided hair that point in opposite directions and are long enough to reach from the thigh to the knee, then...
puis envoloupe en II leus I bendeil desus et desoz, et le lie em mileu ausi, et a ceste lieure ne pora li jambe decliner a destre ne a senestre, et ensi est bien;	then wrap them around the leg from the thigh to the knee, and tie it off there, and at this point do not allow the leg to lean to the right or left, and it will be well.
et aucun i aministrent I bers dou lonc de la jambe, et s’est de fust, et i met on la jambe por warder de movement, et proprement fait on ceu en la brisure ou il a plaie;	and no one maintains the length of the hair on the leg, and it is made of wool, and it is placed on the leg to prevent movement, and this is done properly in the break or wound.
et remue chescun jor la jambe, por veoir s’il i a aposteme chaut n’autre accident;	and move each leg to see if it has an abscess or any other accident.
si le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	if the cure is done when it is healthy.
de la brisure des os dou piet	Of the fracture of the bones of the hand
A la cheville ne vient point de brisure, mais as os dou piet vient aucune fois brisure et as dois poc, et n’i avient fuer que quassure em plusor dispositions.	At the ankle, there is never a fracture, but the bones of the hand come to no fracture and must be careful, and only twisted in more positions.
Et s’il avient as os dou piet brisure, et tu vois ces os sormonter l’un l’autre, si mette si malaides som piet sus la terre, ausi com s’il voloit aler, et puis met maintenant ton piet sus lou sien, lai ou li os sont levez, puis le presse tant k’il reveignent en lor leus;	And if there are many bones broken, and you see them breaking over each other, then set them as straight as possible, as if they were on the ground, just like when they were flying, and then place your foot on the leg, and lift the bones as much as they can stand in their places;
puis met l’emplaustre et estoupes sus, et met desoz lou ventre dou piet une petite tauble a II chiés plains, puis l’estraint au piet avenanment, puis que tu as envoloupez drapelz entor, et autres choses dont tu as mestier.	then apply the bandage and stitch, and then make a small tableau at the bottom of the limb, then draw it up to the knee, then when you have wrapped it around, then wrap drapes around the rest of the body, and other things that you know how to do;
Et quant III jors ou IIII seront passez, si deslie lou liien, car tu troveras les os igalz, soient brisiez, soient desaluez.	And when three or four days have passed, if the bone is not straightened, you will find the bones uneven, broken, dislocated.
Et s’il i a aucuns des dois brisiez, si les restoure, si com nos avons dit as dois de la main;	If there are no broken bones, if they are repaired, then as we have said, it should be done with the hand.
puis met au doi brisiet une estele selonc la longesce dou doi, et soit un poc plus large, puis met desoz le piet celle tauble que j’ai dit, et l’estrain avenanment;	Then, place the other bone in the stele according to the length of the other, and make a larger pocket, then put the point that I mentioned in, and stretch it accordingly.
et s’il en i a II ou III, ou plus, brisiez, si met sus chescun doi une estele selonc sa quantiteit, envoloupee en I drapeil de lin, et estraint la tauble desoz lou piet;	And if there are two or more broken bones, if you place one on each with a stele according to its quantity, wrapped in a single layer of linen, and stretch the point, it will be fine.
et soit estans sus lou chief de la tauble defuer lou ventre dou piet, si qu’il le teigne bien.	And if it is placed on the top of the point with the stomach of the point, then it will be well etched.
Et covient que tu n’oblier mie les autres choses que j’ai dit as autres briseures, des que nos avons dit;	It is necessary that you do not neglect the other things I have said for other breaks, as we have said.
et secor chescun accident si com il covient.	And cut out every accident as it comes.
de la brisure de l’os dou poignil	The following sentence should be translated into English: "of the fracture of the bone
Quant li os de la nature la femme est brisiez, si la fai seoir enlargie, puis l’encline a la partie dou dos, et soit tenue par derrier;	When the woman's nature is broken, if it is made larger, then it leans towards the painful side, and should be held by the side.
puis emplisse li baile la nature de la malaide de couton, et en i mette ausi gros com I sto;	Then fill the knee of the patient's nature with wool, and put as much as I have.
puis deboute la femme, et lieve lou dos poc et poc, et adonques saut li coton, tant qu’il vient a l’entree de la nature, et revient li os avec lou sto;	Then lay the woman down, and gently raise her shoulders, and then jump the wool, as it comes to the entrance of the nature, and return the knee with the cloth.
et quant elle vuet pissier, si oste lou coton, et quant elle a pissiet, se li remette, et ensi faice VII jors ou entor:	When she sees the wound, if it is bone, and when she has cleaned it, she puts on the dressing, and in seven days or more, it will heal.
si sera restoree li brisure, et se tu vues, pren une vessie de berbis, et lie au pertus une cainne, et boute toute la vessie en la nature;	If the fracture is healed, and if you see it, take a bowl of bloodroot, and attach a cord to the wound, and pour all the blood into the bowl in nature.
puis soffle en la cainne forment, tant que li vessie soit enflee dedens:	Then blow into the cord until the bowl is full of blood.
la nature si revenra li brisure;	Nature will heal the fracture.
puis soit emplie de coton, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then it will be filled with cotton, and left alone for no more than seven days, until it is healthy.
Et quant li os dou poignil de l’ome est brisiez, ou de la femme, si le restoure ensi com nos avons dit en l’os de la hainche;	And when the bone of the arm is broken, or of the woman, if it is restored as we have said in the bone of the elbow.
et ne sont mie occultees ces briseures prochienes a celui qui i met son estude et son us, et entent mon livre.	And these breaks are not well known to those who study and use it, and they do not read my book.
Car li brisure li signifie em plusors dispositions la droite voie de la restauration:	For the break means in more ways the right way of restoration:
enten le donques.	understand the doubts.
En la verge, quant elle est brisie, pren une gorge d’oie et i boute la verge;	In the jaw, when it is broken, take an owl's gape and bite the jaw;
puis envoloupe drapelz entor, et le laisse III jors ou enqui entor, et il sera sanez hastanment.	Then wrap it with cloth, and leave it for three days or until it is healthy again.
de brisure avec plaie	Of fracture with wound
Il covient a celui qui a brisure avec plaie, meismement s’elle est grans, si com li os de la cuixe ou de l’ajutoire ou semblant, qu’il soit sainiez maintenant, si que les sainies que nos avons dit le tesmoignent.	It is necessary for the one who has a fracture with wound, even if it is large, such as the bone of the arm or shoulder, or seeming, that he be healthy now, if that the wounds we have said testify.
Et se li plaie saine, si la restainche de vitriole, se tu n’as autre chose, puis rencomence a restorer la briseure en cele meisme houre, ou celui jor, se apostemes chaus n’i vient.	And if the wound is healthy, if the vitrolle burns, if you have nothing else, then resume restoring the fracture at the same hour, or the next day, if the patient does not come.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si laisse la restauration jusc’a nuevime jor, tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez, et n’i touchier ne au tier jor ne au quart, car tu i feroies venir malvais accident.	And if the patient does not come the next day, leave the restoration until the following day, as long as the patient is calmed, and do not touch him again on the third or fourth day, because you will cause the patient to come with evil accident.
Et se li os brisiez est aparans sus lou keur descovert, si covient que tu lou mettes a point legierement a tes mains, a extension petite.	If the bone is broken, it should be set in place as soon as possible, if you can manage to do so gently with your hands, at a slight extension.
Et se li extensions ne t’est apareillie por mettre igal a tes mains, si le ramoine a cest estrument qui est de fer, qui a VII dois ou VIII de lonc, et li largesce est selonc la quantiteit de la plaie;	And if the extensions are not apparent to put them evenly on your hands, if the rammer has this instrument made of iron, which is seven or eight inches long, and the width is according to the size of the wound.
et por ceu est mestier au mire qu’il empreigne III ou IIII, selonc ceu qu’il en ait mestier en chescune cure de briseure;	and because it is necessary to press three or four times, according to how many there are in each treatment of the splint.
et soit rons et un poc gros, k’il ne ploie mie a la compression sus lou membre a ton ovraige, et soit agus devant, et gros des le mileu en avant, ensi:	and it should be sharp and of medium size, so that it does not tear at the compression on your limb, and it should also be ahead, and large in front, like this:
Et est apelez «palainche», por coi il covient que li chiés corbes soit mis sus lou chief de l’os apparent;	And is called the "palisade", because it should have the heads of the screws placed on the end of the bone.
et le boute a une fois, tant k’il reviegne, et soit igalz l’un encontre l’autre.	And the bone once again, as much as it rises, and make them equal on both sides.
Et se li brisure est subtilz, et li estrumens ne puet bien prendre l’os, si covient que tu copes lou chief de l’os, tant que li estrumens en ait possance.	And if the fracture is slight, and the fragments cannot well grasp the bone, then it comes that you cover the head of the bone with the bandage, as much as the fragments have power.
Et se tu ne pues ramener l’os, si com nos avons dit, si lou cope d’un estrument covenable a ceu, ou incisoire ou soieure, a ton pooir;	And if you cannot return the bone, as we have said, if it manages to pass through an appropriate instrument, either a cautery or an incision or a more suitable one, for your own good.
puis reis ceu qui est demorez en l’os d’aspreteit et de menues escorces.	Then use this which is made of sharpness and small scratches.
Et quant li os est ramenez, et li malaides sent grant dolor aprés, saiches qu’il n’est mie en son leu natureil.	When the bone is reset, and the patient feels great pain afterwards, seek help immediately, as it may not be in its natural state.
Si fai tant qu’il soit en son leu, puis moille I drapeil en vin stiptique noir, et proprement se c’est en esteit;	If you make it so that it is in its place, then wrap it with a strip of black, warm ointment, and properly so.
et ne mettre mie sus la plaie cerote ne autre chose ou il ait oile, qu’il n’i faice venir porriture et corruption;	and do not put anything else on the wound, such as oil, so that it does not come to be sore and corrupt.
puis aministre esteles quant tu as restoreit l’os, et laisse la plaie descoverte, et cope la coverture tout entor, selonc la quantiteit de la plaie, et te done bien en garde que li plaie ne soit estrainte avec la brisure;	Then administer the ointments when you have restored the bone, and leave the wound exposed, and cover it with a cloth entirely, according to the size of the wound, and make sure the wound is not tightened with the fracture.
et maintes fois ont ce fait li fol mire, et ont fait venir sus le malaide ou mort ou corrodent aucune fois;	And many times it has caused the patient's leg to be paralyzed, and they have brought in the physician or died or were corroded never.
et soit li estrignemens plus molz et plus souef des autres brisures.	And the scars are softer and more supple than the others.
Et se li plaie est male ou grans, et tu doutes que mavais accidens n’i veigne, si com nos avons dit, et tu trueves dolor au leu, si n’i covient mie mettre sus esteles;	And if the wound is large or great, and you doubt that you have had accidents but did not come, as we have said, and you feel pain in the leg, if it does not happen that you put ointments on it.
mais envoloupe entor, en leu d’esteles, drapelz durs, et les lie.	But envelops around, on the side of the elbow, hard wrappings, and they tie.
Et quant tu vois aprés I jor ou II enjanrer bowe a la plaie, si oste ceu que tu as mis sus a tout vin, et i met oignement sanant plaies, si com oignement tetrafarmaçon et semblans.	When you see after the first or second day that the wound is healing, and if all that you have placed on it has come out, and you put on a salve to heal wounds, which is a common and similar ointment.
Et covient que tu deslies lou membre II fois le jor, lou matin et au vespre, tant qu’il soit soudez et sanez.	It is necessary that you unbandage the limb twice a day, in the morning and evening, as long as it is not swollen and healthy.
Et covient que li membres soit aparilliez en teil maniere que li bowe corre aval legierement.	It is necessary that the member be straightened in a partly manner that the belly can be moved lightly.
Et se maint jor trespassent, et il ne puet souder mais rent adés bowe, saiches k’il i a petites pieces d’os, por coi il covient que tu quieres la plaie avec tente, et oste toutes ces pieces desevrees que font venir celle dolor.	If they continue to twist, and it cannot be held together but moves away from the belly, with small pieces of bones, because it is necessary that you close the wound with a tent, and all these broken parts cause that this pain comes.
Et se fistule vient au leu, ou autre maniere de corruption, si covient que tu le cures, selonc ceu qu’il dist en son chapistre ci devant.	And if a fistula comes to the shoulder, or any other form of corruption, it is necessary that you treat it according to what is written in this chapter before.
Et quant li os est brisiez, et apert sus lou membre, si com li os de la cuixe ou de l’ajutoire, et autres semblans des grans membres, si ne le traire mie, car maintes fois en vient li mors, mais le laisse tant qu’il porrisse;	And when the bone is broken, and it is opened at the joint, as with the bone of the elbow or the shoulder, and other similar bones of the large limbs, if it is not treated, because many times death comes, but it is left open until it bleeds;
par aventure cherra par lui aprés XX jors ou XXX, puis cure la plaie, se tu pues;	by chance a wound may be found on it after 20 or 30 days, then treat the wound, if you can;
et se tu ne pues, si la laisse.	and if you cannot, then leave it;
des brus qui vienent sor la sodure	of thorns that come out during the heat
Nous vienent maintes fois aprés la santeit de la briseure, meismement quant c’est pres de la jointure, et laide chose est a veoir li figure dou membre;	Many times after the healing of the fracture, we come when it is near to the joint, and it is a matter to see the appearance of the limb;
et par aventure ne puet faire li membres ses ovraiges naturelz.	And by chance, it cannot make the limbs its natural position.
Pren warde donques se li nous est fres:	If we find that it is fresh:
si li aministre medicines stiptiques, si com aloes, encens, et mirre, et sarcocolle, acaice, et semblans autres, ensi que tu preignes aucune de ces choses, ou toutes ensamble, et les confit avec vin stiptique ou avec abun d’uef ou avec aisil;	If it is treated with styptic medicines such as aloes, incense, and myrrh, and sarcolla, acacia, and similar ones, if you do not use any of these, or all together, and mix them with spikenard or with a large amount of beer or with asafetida;
et les met sus le nout en estoupes, et l’estraint bien, et ne la desliier en mains jors;	and apply them to the wound, and extract it well, and do not let it drip in your hands;
et puis la desloie, et rencomence une autre, tant que li nodations soit ostee;	and then let it drip, and continue with another one until the swelling is reduced;
ou tu estrain sus une piece de plonc bien faite;	If you strain too hard on a well-made piece of cloth.
car li proprietez dou plonc si est qu’il oste toutes les enfleures desus les membres;	For if the fabric does not hold up, it will tear all the threads from the limbs.
et se li nodation est ja convertie en durteit ausi com piere, et il est besoing de l’oster, si la cope desus, et fent la superfluiteit apparent;	And if the blister is converted into hardness as a piercing, and it becomes sore to the touch, if the covering is removed, and the excess is revealed;
ou tu la reis a aucun raseur, tant qu’ele soit ostee, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee.	Or you do not shave it as soon as it is healed, until it is healthy, and the care as soon as it is healthy.
dou membre qui est foibles aprés la garison	A weak limb that is weak after a cast
Quant li brisure de l’os est restoree, et demoure aprés li membres foibles et subtilz, si avient por mout de causes:	When the bone fracture is restored, and the swelling disappears after weak and subtle limbs, if it comes from various causes.
de coi l’une est por ceu qu’il fut liiez trop estroit, et ne fut mie liiez si com il covenoit;	If one of the bones is because it was cut too tightly, and it did not fit as expected.
ou por ceu qu’il i ot trop de liiens, et ne pooit venir li norrissemens au membre;	Or because there were too many stitches, and the nerves could not come to the member.
ou por multitude d’arosement;	Or due to the multitude of stitching.
ou por trop grans movements, ne mie en son houre;	Or because there were too many large movements, and it did not fit at its time.
ou por ceu qu’il a poc de sanc en son cors, si est foibles.	Or because there is little blood in the body, which makes them weak.
Et li cure si est que tu faices mengier le malaide, et faire le cors tendre, tant que li sans soit multipliiez en lui;	And if the treatment is that you make the patient lie down, and make the chest tense as much as possible without multiplying in it.
et li aministre bain, et li done joie et liesce;	and administer baths, and then he becomes joyful and calm.
puis met poix sus le membre, si que li poix atraie a li grant norrissement, et l’arose sovent d’aigue tede, tant que li norrissement corre au membre;	Then apply poultice to the member, if it attracts the great swelling, and the redness often comes from the red tede, until the swelling reaches the member.
et reviegne a sa figure natureil.	and returns to its natural shape.
dou membre tort aprés la santeit	A dislocated limb after injury
Quant li membres est tors aprés la restauration, et li os brisiez apert, et li forme dou membre est laide, toutevoie ne pert mie son ovraige natureil:	When the limbs are twisted after resetting, and the bone is broken open, and the form of the affected member is deformed, it does not fit its natural shape.
si ne croire mie les folz qui dient c’on doit brisier lou membre tout de noveil, et maint fol mire ont ce fait en nostre terre;	if one does not believe the folk who say that one must break the member completely at once, and most have done this in our land.
et cist ovraiges est blamez, et en vient grans malz, et par aventure li mors;	and these operations are blamed, and great harm comes of it, and often death occurs.
toutevoie, se li nodations et li torture sont fres, si covient k’il soient arosez d’aigue chaude, ou herbes mollifians soient cuites, si com foilles de vismalve, et racines, et mellilote, et semblans choses;	The first line of the text translates to: "All wounds, if they are nodulations and tortures, are fresh, if they are raised with hot water, or herbs that soften, if like soles of feet, and roots, and honey-locust trees, and similar things.
et li fai I emplaustre mollificatif, si com dyaquilon bien fait, et tu pren le muscillaige de vismalve, et la confit avec graisse de geline ou oile de sisament, et fai emplaustre sus;	The second line of the text translates to: "And I apply a mollifying substance if it is well made, as dysentery is, and take the sole of the foot, and cook with fat or linseed oil, and apply on top.
ou tu pren figues graisses, et les broie avec fien de colon, et semblans medicines que amenuisent le soudement.	The third line of the text translates to: "Or you take fat figs, and crush them with colon fat, and similar medicines that moisten the dysentery.
Et aucune fois est ostee li nodacion por froter continuelment et longement a mains moistes.	And no time is there where the noose is tightened continuously and for a long time with wet hands.
Et soit amenistrez movement au membre chescune houre.	And allow movement to the limb at each hour.
Et se li tortuositez est enveillie et endurcie, ausi com piere, et besoins est de l’oster au fer, si la covient coper jusc’a l’os, a l’incisoire subtil legierement;	When the tortuosity is aroused and becomes painful, like a piercing, and there is a need for the ointment at the forge, if it comes to touch the bone, under the subtle incision lightly.
et mettre cusenson et estude en la cure.	and put on linen and study in the treatment.
Ci encomence li livres des dislocations	Here begins the book of dislocations.
Dislocations est issue d’aucune jointe de son leu, por coi il ne se puet muevre, et est li membres mal figurez, et sent li malaides grant dolor et grant lesion.	Dislocation occurs when a joint moves out of its place, which prevents it from moving, and the limb is misaligned, causing the patient great pain and injury.
Quant dislocation vient a aucun, si le covient maintenant ramener sens targier.	When dislocation occurs at no joint, if it comes now to return sensation to the limb.
Car s’on tarde, si enfle li leus, et par aventure si le remet on a poines au leu;	For if we are delayed, if it becomes swollen, and by chance if it is reset at the shoulder.
por ceu ne covient mie c’on le mueve a l’oure k’il est enflez:	because it does not matter how we move it at the ear when it is swollen.
maintes fois fait venir spame et autres dolors;	Many times brought to vomit and other pains.
toutevoie, quant ce avenra, si fai sainier lou malaide, puis le laisse, tant que li apostemes chas soit apaisiez;	Indeed, when this happens, if I make the patient well, then let it go, as long as the abscess is not healed.
puis arose le membre d’aigue chaude et d’oile, puis le ramoinne legierement, et cure chescun membre si com li cure venra en son leu.	Then, the patient's inflamed and oily limb was raised, then gently reset, and each member was treated as if the treatment came from their own legs.
Et j’ai ordenez les chapistres des dislocations des lou chief jusc’a piez.	I have ordered the cauteries for the dislocations of the shoulder bones.
des mandibules	for the dislocations of the mandibles.
Poc avient que les mandibules soient desaluees andous, et li dislocations d’ambedous est selonc II manieres:	Recently, it has been found that the mandibles are often dislocated, and there are two ways to reset them:
ou elles sont un poc ostees de lor leus, et mollifies un poc;	either they are a small piece of their bones, and are softened slightly;
ou elles sont desaluees entierement, et pendent vers lou pis, et cort li salive de la bouche qu’il ne la puet tenir, ne ne puet clore sa bouche, et envoloupe sa langue avec la parole.	or they are completely dislocated and hang downwards, and cut the saliva from the mouth that cannot be held, and cannot close the mouth, and wrap the tongue with speech;
Quant li dislocations est petite, si revient par li em plusors disposicions.	If the dislocation is small, it returns through the more common positions.
Et s’elle est entiere et acomplie, si covient que tu la ramoinne hastanment, et ne targier mie;	And if it is completely achieved and accomplished, then you must gently reset it, and do not touch it.
et en tel maniere que li ministres teigne le chief dou malaide, et boute li mires som pochet de l’une de ses mains en la racine de la dislocation de la mandibule dedens la bouche, se li dislocations est de II pars;	And in such a way that the minister burns the child's head of the patient, and pierces the tip of one of his hands at the root of the dislocation of the mandible, which causes the mouth to close, if it is dislocated by II parts.
et li autre doi des mains soient defuer, por mettre igal;	And the other two hands are deformed to make them equal.
et comande au malaide qu’il les amollisse, ses mandibules, et les mueve de toutes pars.	And instruct the patient to smooth out his mandibles and move them all parts.
Et li mires la mete igal, tant qu’elle reveigne en son leu.	And the patient should be held steady until it is in its proper place.
Et se li ramener est griés, meismement se ce sont les II mandibules ensamble, si les arose d’aigue chaude et d’oile, tant que les ramoinnes legierement;	And if it is reset, it should be greased, just like the two mandibles together, with hot oil and ointment, until it is reset lightly.
ne ne targier mie dou ramener, si com nos avons dit.	There is no need to translate this line as it seems to be a command or instruction rather than a medical term. It could be translated as "Do not try to bring it back, as we have said." However, without more context, it's difficult to provide an accurate translation.
Et quant elles sont ramenees igalment, et li bouche dou malaide clot bien sens mollifiier, si met sus drapelz moilliez en cerote fait d’oile roset et de cire, puis le lie legierement de molz liiens;	When the hairs are returned evenly, and the patient's mouth feels relaxed, if you put soft flannels moistened with oil of roses and wax on it, then gently bind the hair with threads or strings.
et dorme li malaides sus son dos, et ses chiés soit estans entre II cussins, si qu’il ne lou mueve ne a destre ne a senestre, ne ne s’efforce mie de maixier, mais preigne legiere viande, tant que les dolors soient ostees, et soient noees les mandibules;	When the patient falls asleep on his back, and his head is between two pillows, if he does not move to the right or left, and does not strain himself, but prays with light food, as long as the pain is steady and does not affect the jaws.
et puis menjuce ce qu’il vuet legierement, et ne se travaille mie d’ovrir la bouche au mengier et au boivre, tant que li mandibule soit bien noee et sanee.	Then he swallows what he sees lightly, and does not strain himself to open his mouth for eating and drinking, as long as the jaw is well steadied and healthy.
Et se les II mandibules ne pueent estre remises a point a une houre, et ne sont mie converties a lor leus, si en vient fievres et sode acostumees, et par aventure solution de ventre, et par aventure vomist cole pure.	And if the two jaws cannot be set at once in an hour and are not converted to their proper positions, then if fevers and customary coldness come on, and by chance stomach pain and vomiting of clear bile arrive.
Et quant tu verras ceu, adonc saiches que c’est perdicions;	And when you see this, you will know that it is a disaster.
et maintes fois muert cil cui il avient, en VIIII jors.	And many times he died, in nine years.
de la forcelle	from the force.
Li forcele ne puet desaluer dou costeit dedens la continuation de li et dou pis, et est desaluee aucune fois au defuer, et bien le sent on.	The force cannot be removed from the cost of continuing the arm and the hip, and it is never fixed at the deflation, and it is felt as such.
Et li restauration si est que li malaides gise sovin sor son dos, et estende ses bras;	And if the patient has a dislocation, it is when the shoulder pains on its side, and extends its arms.
et puis presse le leu forment a ta palme, et elle revenra;	Then press the shoulder with your hand, and it will return.
puis met sus l’emplaustre et lou bendeil, et l’estraint;	Then place the cautery and the burn on the skin, and pull it off.
et li chiez qui est devers lou coute ne puet desaluer;	And the head that is towards the chest cannot be dislocated.
se poc non, et se il desalue aucune fois, si le ramoinne a son leu, si com nos avons dit;	If it does not happen, and if it does not dislocate ever, then reset the shoulder at its place, as we have said.
puis met sus l’emplaustre et le bendeil, et l’estraint, et coumande au malaide qu’il se repose tant qu’il soit sanez;	Then place the cautery and the burn on the skin, and pull it off, and instruct the patient to rest as long as they are healthy.
et ensi meisme est ramenez li chiés de l’espale, quant il est desevrez de son leu.	And then, bring the shoulder head back to its place when it is out of its socket.
de la dislocation de l’espaule	Of the shoulder dislocation
Saiches que li espaule n’est desaluee fuer que selonc III manieres:	There are three ways in which the shoulder is dislocated:
de coi l’une est qu’ele desalue a la partie de l’assele au desoz;	If one part of the shoulder is dislocated, it is due to the muscle being pulled away from the bone.
et li seconde est a la partie dou pis;	And the second way is in the muscle area that is closest to the bone.
et par aventure desalue a la partie desus, et ceu avient poc;	And by chance, it can also be dislocated at the other end, but this happens rarely.
et ne desalue mie derrier por l’espaule, et ne desalue mie dedens por les ners;	And it does not get dislocated from the shoulder muscle or nerve.
et plusors fois desalue desoz vers l’assele, meismement a ces qui ont poc de char, car a ces saut ele fuer hastanment;	And more often than not, it gets dislocated towards the shoulder blade, especially for those who have poor posture, because they jump higher.
a ces qui ont assez char, saut ele a poines, et rentre a poines.	For those who have enough fat, they jump and prick themselves with points, and then return to their points.
Et par aventure avient a aucuns homes percussion ou casseure, et enfle li espaule d’un aposteme chaut, et cuide qu’elle est desaluee par ceu.	And by chance, it happens to some men that they are struck or crushed, and the muscle of their spine is torn out by an abscess, and ensure that it is not dislocated by this.
Il covient donques que tu l’esprueves, tant que tu en soies certains;	It is therefore necessary that you stretch it, as long as you are sure of it.
et adonques encomence la cure.	and then begin the treatment.
Et est conue li dislocations quant il est aval vers l’assele, et met difference entre l’espaule malade et la saine, et tu troveras entre lor diversiteit manifeste;	And it is known that dislocations occur when they are pulled towards the shoulder, and there is a difference between the sick shoulder and the healthy one, and you will find a clear difference between them.
et troveras au chief de l’espaule une fosse, et desoz l’assele au tochier le chief de l’espaule, ausi com se ce soit uns oes;	and you will find at the top of the shoulder a hollow, and from there to the shoulder, as it is in some cases, and so it is with others.
et ne puet li malaides ramener sa main a son neis, ne movoir de nulz movemens;	and cannot bring his hand to his face, and does not move at all.
et ausi, s’elle est desaluee en haut, si n’est mie occultee, car tu le trueves manifestement au tochier;	and also, if it is dislocated above, then it is not hidden because you can see the scar.
et ceste maniere de dislocation n’est mie fors a ramener, quant elle est novele, ou se li enfes est malaides.	and this manner of dislocation is not easy to reset when it is new, or if the child is young.
Et li maniere est que li ministres lieve la main dou malaide en haut, puis met tes peuchas desoz l’assele, et lieve la jointure a force en haut au leu;	And the method is to gently hold the hand of the young patient high, then place your fingers on the knee, and gently pull up on the joint.
et li ministres lieve la main, et l’estende en haut, pues le mette desoz;	And he gently holds the hand, extends it upwards, and places it aside.
si venra hastanment.	If a sudden cold comes.
Et s’elle ne vient si com nos avons dit em mains jors aprés, si covient ke li malaides soit baigniez en aigue chaude;	And if it does not come as we have said in our hands just afterward, then the patient should be bathed in hot water.
et li amenistre arosement mollifiant et assouajant, si com decoction de altee et de fenugrec et de mellilote en aigue, et soit amenistree;	and the patient should be given a warm, soothing and softening remedy, such as a decoction of aloe and fenugreek and honey in hot water, and it should be given.
puis soit sovinez li malaides sus son dos, et mette on desoz l’assele un sto de lainne igal, ne trop mol ne trop dur, puis mette li mires son talon sus le sto, et lieve le chief de l’espaule vertuousement, et traie la main dou malaide;	Then the patient should be relieved of the pain on his back, and put a wet bandage on the ankle, not too soft or too hard, then put the heel of the foot on the bandage, and gently lift the shoulder of the upper arm, and move the hand of the patient.
et uns autres ministres teigne lou chief dou malaide, si qu’il ne se mueve aval;	and some other signs indicate that the patient's shoulder is dislocating, if it does not move freely.
celle espaule revient tout maintenant, et se tu vues si le ramoinne selonc ceste maniere:	That shoulder is back now, and if you see that the dislocation is reset in this way:
et est que tu faices estre present I home qui soit plus grans que li malaides;	and it is that you make sure to present the home that is greater than the shoulder;
et soit drois devers lou costeit, et boute s’espaule desoz l’assele dou malaide, et lieve l’assele en haut, si que li malaides pende en l’ar;	and it is that the breast is turned towards the chest, and the shoulder is pulled away from the body of the patient, and the body is lifted up, so that the shoulder hangs freely;
et uns autres ministres traie la main dou malaide aval devers lou ventre.	and some other signs indicate that the patient's hand is being turned towards the abdomen.
Et se li malaides est trop legiers, si pent avec lui aucune chose pesant, et li dislocation revient maintenant.	And if the patient is too heavy, then with them there is nothing heavy that can be done, and the dislocation returns now.
Et le ramoinne on ausi en autre maniere:	And the resetting is done in another way as well:
et est c’on fiche I lonc tison en terre, dont li chiés soit ausi reons com I pistal, et ne soit ne trop gros ne trop graile;	and it is made by measuring a long thread on the ground, and the head of the shoulder is also reset as if it were a pin, and it should not be too thick or too rough.
puis soit mis desoz lou malaide, mais k’il ait drapelz souef sus, et li malaides soit estans dou lonc dou fust;	Then it is placed on the patient's shoulder, but if it has been twisted too much, and the shoulder is too long or too thick, it should be adjusted accordingly.
puis soit estendue sa main aval d’autre part forment, et li jointure revenra en son leu hastanment;	Then it is extended on the other hand, and the joint returns to its proper place.
et s’elle ne vuet revenir por toutes ces choses que nos avons dit, si fai ceste cure:	If it does not return to its proper place after these things we have said, then this treatment is not effective.
pren I tison de II bras de grant et IIII dois de large, qui ait le chief reont por mues entrer em parfont desoz l’assele, selonc ceste forme:	1. Take a strip of two arms of great and four of wide size, which can enter the joint through the front of the bone, according to this form:
puis lie sus le chief dou fust drapelz souez, que li fust ne blece lou malaide, puis le met desoz l’assele dou malaide;	2. Then wrap the strip around the head of the bone, making sure it is not too tight, so as not to harm the patient, and then place it on the affected joint;
et estende som bras sus le fust dou lonc, et lie l’ajutoire sus le fust, et lou bras au chief de la main, puis met le bras sus I eschillon d’une eschiele dou large, et soit estendue li mains aval, et soit laissiez li cors pendans d’autre part:	3. Extend the arm on the long side of the bone, and place the assistant on the head of the arm, and the other arm at the wrist, then extend the hands and leave the chest hanging from the other side:
li jointure reva ens maintenant.	The joint now reveals itself.
Et quant elle est ens, en quel maniere que ce soit, si covient que tu mettes desoz l’assele une spere de laine igal, puis met l’emplaustre aparilliet de poudre dou molin, avec encens et aubun d’uef, sus toute l’espaule et entor, puis l’estrain desoz l’assele avenanment, et torne le liien sus l’emplaustre, et embraice la main a son col, et soit li mains demorans ensi.	If the joint is realigned in this manner, if it comes to pass that you place a ball of thread equal to the size of the arm on one side, then place a powdered spice spray on the other side, with incense and vinegar, all along the shoulder blade and down the back, then tighten the thread on one side, turn the limb over the spray, and wrap the hand around the arm, and let the hand remain in this position.
Et covient qu’il menjuce poc, tant que li membres soit confortez, car il sanera plus tost;	And it is necessary that he be treated quickly, as the member will recover faster if it is comfortable.
et puis menjuce plus aprés V jors ou VII, et le mueve;	and then treat again after 4 or 7 days, and move it.
et s’il est fermeis et il n’est mollifiez, si est sanez.	And if it is tight and not softened, it will be cured.
Et se li jointure est fuer de leu por moistor que i est venue, ou por autre cause, si covient que tu i aministres cauteres a III pertus, si com il est mis devant ou chapistre des cauteres.	And if the joint is stiff due to moisture that came, or for another reason, it comes that you apply cauterizations at III incisions, as it is placed before or in the chapter of cauterizations.
Et se tu fais tout ceu, et il deslie aprés VII jors, et li jointure ne se tient, et ne puet lever som bras amont, adonc saiches que li nerf au chief de l’espaule sont copeit ou estendut ou amollis;	And if you do everything correctly, and after 7 days it does not hold, and the joint does not rise with the arm raised forward, then you should suspect that the nerve at the top of the shoulder is compressed or extended or softened.
et saiches que li jointure n’iert jamais fichie en son leu.	And suspects that the joint will never return to its place in its socket.
Li dislocation qui est devers lou pis, et les mameles, ou derrier, si est faite par impulsion, et estendement de mains, et i aministre on autre lieure;	The dislocation that is towards the foot, and the ankles, or knees, if it is made by force, and extension of hands, and it is treated at another time.
et cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	and treat until it is healthy.
Et se aprés la sanation vient grietez au membre, et tardemens em movement, si use li malaides bain maintes fois, tant que celle grietez soit alegie, et reviegne a sa premiere nature.	And after the cure comes pain in the member, and then with movement, if it is used with hot water many times, until that pain is alleviated, and return to its original state.
de la dislocation dou coute	of the dear dislocation
Saiches que li jointure dou coute est desaluee a poinnes, et a poinnes revient;	Shoulder joints that are stiff and dislocate again and again.
et s’est desaluee de toutes pars, et meismement devant et derrier, et li dislocations n’est mie reponue, car on la voit bien et sent bien;	And it has become loose in all directions, and even forward and backward, and the dislocation is not well repaired because it can be seen and felt well.
et desalue selonc chescune figure.	And it becomes loose according to each figure.
Et quant tu joins le coute malaide avec lou sain, si le pues veoir apertement.	And when you join the sharp edge with the clean part, if you see it open widely.

de la dislocation dou genoil	Of the shoulder's dislocation

c’est a savoir, dedens et defuer, et derrier;	It is known as trenching and deferring, and delaying.

et uns autres ministres estende son piet, tant que li genous reviegne a son leu, et li signes est qu’il aert bien sa jambe a sa cuixe legierement;	And other assistants extend the foot, as long as the knee returns to its place, and the sign is that it is well dislocated lightly.
et met l’emplastre sus, et fai aerdre la jambe a la cuixe, et les loie ensamble fort III jors ou IIII, puis le deslie;	and apply the plaster above, and make the leg straight at the knee, and assemble the toes as much as three or four times, then cut it off.
et ne se travaille mie li malaides d’aler, tant que li membres soit confortez.	and do not work on the joint of the elbow, until the limb is comfortable.
Et se li membres n’est a point, si aministre estendement fort, si com nos avons dit en la cure de la hainche, tant qu’il soit sanez	And if the limb is not present, then extend the treatment firmly, as we have said in the treatment of the wound, as long as it is healthy.
de la dislocation dou talon	of the dislocation of the heel
Li talons est aucune fois esmeus, et aucune fois desaluez plenement, et dedens et defuer.	The heel is never twisted, and never completely dislocated, and it is difficult to mend.
Et li signes si est que li cheville est enflee, et tent avant a la partie ou elle est desaluee:	And if the knee is swollen, and try before the part where it is dislocated.
li ramenemens si est legier, et le doit on estendre legierement a ses mains quant il est esmeus soulement.	If the limb is light, and it should be stretched gently with your hands only when it is weak.
Et quant il est desaluez dou tot, si covient que tu faices seoir le malaide droit, et le tigne I ministres fors par la jambe, desus la cheville;	And if it is completely dislocated, then you must make the patient sit straight, and hold the limb with one hand, and tighten the knee with the other.
puis trai le piet a toi a ta main destre, et puis a la senestre II fois, puis l’estent en haut, et boute bellement lou piet en haut;	Then draw the point on your right hand, and then on your left, twice, then pull it up, and hold it well at the top.
et fai ce II fois, si com nos avons dit, em boutant et en traiant lou piet;	And do this twice, as we have said, by bending and drawing the point.
s’elle revient, c’est bien;	If it returns, that's good.
se ce non, si rencomence l’ovraige, car il revient;	If not, then the work is repeated because it returns.
et s’il ne puet revenir ensi, si fai gesir lou malaide sor son dos sus terre, et fiche I passeil fermement en terre entre ses cuixes, et lie drapelz entor, qu’il ne blece lou malaide;	And if it cannot return, then I will make the patient lie on his back on the ground, and firmly press his heels against the ground between his toes, and spread his legs wide so that the point does not pierce the skin.
puis teigne li ministres la cuixe, et uns autres ministres estende lou piet a ses mains ou a I liien, k’il lie sus le col dou piet;	Then, the minister traces the cup with their hand, and some other ministers extend their hands or arms to the collar of the shoulder.
puis estende chescuns ministres igalment, et li passelz soit adés entre les cuixes dou malaide por retenir le malaide quant on l’estent;	Then, all ministers extend their hands equally, and the pins are placed either inside or outside the joint of the patient to hold the patient in place while they are extended.
puis mette li mires igal la dislocation a ses mains, et uns autres ministres teigne la jambe sainne au desoz, et li dislocation revenra hastanment.	Then, the minister places the dislocation in their hands, and some other ministers trace the healthy leg at the ankle, and the dislocation returns to its original position.
Et quant elle iert a point, si met l’emplastre et estoupes sus, et l’estrain forment, et lie lou piet a la jambe, et warde les ners qui sont sus la cheville derrier, que li liiens ne soit trop estrois;	And when it is firm, if the plaster is applied and the stitches are removed, and the joint is formed, and the tendons that were under the ankle are tightened, so that the ligaments are not too tight.
puis le laisse II jors ou III, et se li liiens amolist, si l’estrain;	Then it is left alone for 2 or 3 days, and if it becomes loose, it should be tightened.
puis le deslie au tier jor ou au quart, et deffent a aler lou malaide par IIII jors;	Then it is tightened after the third or fourth day, and the patient should use the aid for 4 days.
et s’il va devant cel termine, ce n’est mie seurtez qu’il ne desalue encor.	And if the patient advances as far as the end, it is only a matter of time before it dislocates again.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si covient que tu l’apaises, si com nos avons dit autre part, tant qu’il soit sanez.	2. And if an abscess forms, it comes, and if you can calm it down, as we have said elsewhere, as soon as it is healthy.
des dois	The first line of the text is
Quant li doi sont desaluez, si les covient bellement estendre sens travail, et c’est legiere chose.	When the shoulders are dislocated, if they can be extended well with effort, and it is a light thing.
Et se li dislocations est en aucun nout dou dos dou piet, si covient que tu faices seoir le malaide sus I leu plain ou sus .ie. table tot droit, et met ton piet sus ce qui apert de ces jointures, puis presse a ton piet forment, tant qu’il reviegne;	And if the dislocation occurs in no part of the shoulder, it is only a matter of time before it dislocates again. Then, place the aid on the shoulder at the same level as the joint or above it, and press on the parts that open these joints, until it realigns.
et quant il est igalz, et il n’i apert nient, si met desoz la plante dou piet une table a II chiés, puis l’estrain forment, et le laisse III jors, puis le deslie;	When the hair is long and even, and it does not prick, if one makes a cut in the flesh at the base of the hair, then the wound forms and is left for three days, then it heals.
et le fai reposer, tant qu’il soit sanez.	and it rests, as long as it is healthy.
de plaie et de dislocation ensamble	Of wounds and dislocation together
Quant plaie vient avec la dislocation, et on la vuet restorer, maintes fois avient que li malaides muert:	When a wound comes with the dislocation, and it is seen to be restored, many times the patient dies.
si ne soies mie presumptuous en la cure, se tu n’es saiges en l’art et tu ne l’as useit longement, et se tu n’es pitous et misericors et tardis, ne mie hardis;	If you are not presumptuous in the cure, if you are not skilled in the art and have not used it for a long time, and if you are merciful and slow, do not be hardhearted.
et use au comencement de choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et laisse le malaide en la main Deu, se tu n’i vois esperance de santeit;	And begin with calming remedies for abscesses, and leave the patient in God's hand, if you see no hope of health.
et quant tu i vois esperance, si ramoinne maintenant le membre au leu, ainsois que li apostemes chaus i viegne;	And when you see hope, then immediately reset the limb at the joint, even if the abscess is still present.
et quant li membres est a leu, si aministre choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et cure la plaie, si com il covient, d’oignemens desiccatis;	And when the limb is at the joint, if you can calm the abscess and treat the wound, according to what is necessary, use drying herbs.
et se avec la dislocation a brisure, et os menus desevrez, si les oste, et fai ce que nos avons dit en maladies simples;	And if the dislocation is accompanied by fracture, and the bones are broken, then the bones, and do what we have said in simple diseases.
et te garde d’entrer en voie de paour, selonc ce que j’ai dit, car ce te vaut mues selonc ton Creator, et por la saveteit de t’arme et de ton cors.	And keep away from the path of despair, according to what I have said, for it is good for you according to your creator, and by the wisdom of your arm and your heart.
